Section 1:
As Amended by House Committee
Session of 2025
By Committee on Judiciary
Requested by Nancy Strouse on behalf of the Kansas Judicial Council.
2-7

2 adult guardianship and protective proceedings jurisdiction act and the
3 uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other protective
4 arrangements act; amending K.S.A. 9-1215, 17-2263, 17-2264, 21-

19
20 Be it enacted by the Legislature of the State of Kansas:
21 New Section 1. Sections 1 through 23, and amendments thereto, may
22 be cited as the uniform adult guardianship and protective proceedings
23 jurisdiction act (2007).
24 New Sec. 2. As used in this act:
25 (a) "Adult" means an individual who has attained 18 years of age or
26 an emancipated individual under 18 years of age.
27 (b) "Conservator" means a person appointed by the court to
28 administer the property of an adult, including a person appointed under
29 section 93, and amendments thereto.
30 (c) "Guardian" means a person appointed by the court to make
31 decisions regarding the person of an adult, including a person appointed
32 under section 72, and amendments thereto.
33 (d) "Guardianship order" means an order appointing a guardian.
34 (e) "Guardianship proceeding" means a judicial proceeding in which
35 an order for the appointment of a guardian is sought or has been issued.
HB 2359—Am. by HC 2
1 (f) "Incapacitated person" means an adult for whom a guardian has
2 been appointed.
3 (g) "Party" means the respondent, petitioner, guardian, conservator or
4 any other person allowed by the court to participate in a guardianship or
5 protective proceeding.
6 (h) "Person," except in the term "incapacitated person" or "protected
7 person," means an individual, corporation, business trust, estate, trust,
8 partnership, limited liability company, association, joint venture, public
9 corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency or
10 instrumentality, or any other legal or commercial entity.
11 (i) "Protected person" means an adult for whom a protective order has
12 been issued.
13 (j) "Protective order" means an order appointing a conservator or
14 other order related to management of an adult's property.
15 (k) "Protective proceeding" means a judicial proceeding in which a
16 protective order is sought or has been issued.
17 (l) "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible
18 medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is
19 retrievable in perceivable form.
20 (m) "Respondent" means an adult for whom a protective order or the
21 appointment of a guardian is sought.
22 (n) "State" means a state of the United States, the District of
23 Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, a federally
24 recognized Indian tribe or any territory or insular possession subject to the
25 jurisdiction of the United States.
26 New Sec. 3. A court of this state may treat a foreign country as if it
27 were a state for the purpose of applying sections 1 through 17 and sections
28 21 through 23, and amendments thereto.
29 New Sec. 4. (a) A court of this state may communicate with a court in
30 another state concerning a proceeding arising under this act. The court may
31 allow the parties to participate in the communication. Except as otherwise
32 provided in subsection (b), the court shall make a record of the
33 communication. The record may be limited to the fact that the
34 communication occurred.
35 (b) Courts may communicate concerning schedules, calendars, court
36 records and other administrative matters without making a record.
37 New Sec. 5. (a) In a guardianship or protective proceeding in this
38 state, a court of this state may request the appropriate court of another state
39 to do any of the following:
40 (1) Hold an evidentiary hearing;
41 (2) order a person in that state to produce evidence or give testimony
42 pursuant to procedures of that state;
43 (3) order that an evaluation or assessment be made of the respondent;
HB 2359—Am. by HC 3
1 (4) order any appropriate investigation of a person involved in a
2 proceeding;
3 (5) forward to the court of this state a certified copy of the transcript
4 or other record of a hearing under paragraph (1) or any other proceeding,
5 any evidence otherwise produced under paragraph (2) and any evaluation
6 or assessment prepared in compliance with an order under paragraph (3) or
7 (4);
8 (6) issue any order necessary to assure the appearance in the
9 proceeding of a person whose presence is necessary for the court to make a
10 determination, including the respondent or the incapacitated or protected
11 person; and
12 (7) issue an order authorizing the release of medical, financial,
13 criminal or other relevant information in that state, including protected
14 health information as defined in 45 C.F.R 160.103.
15 (b) If a court of another state in which a guardianship or protective
16 proceeding is pending requests assistance of the kind provided in
17 subsection (a), a court of this state has jurisdiction for the limited purpose
18 of granting the request or making reasonable efforts to comply with the
19 request.
20 New Sec. 6. (a) In a guardianship or protective proceeding, in
21 addition to other procedures that may be available, testimony of a witness
22 who is located in another state may be offered by deposition or other
23 means allowable in this state for testimony taken in another state. The
24 court on its own motion may order that the testimony of a witness be taken
25 in another state and may prescribe the manner in which and the terms upon
26 which the testimony is to be taken.
27 (b) In a guardianship or protective proceeding, a court in this state
28 may permit a witness located in another state to be deposed or to testify by
29 telephone or audiovisual or other electronic means. A court of this state
30 shall cooperate with the court of the other state in designating an
31 appropriate location for the deposition or testimony.
32 New Sec. 7. (a) As used in sections 7 through 15, and amendments
33 thereto:
34 (1) "Emergency" means a circumstance that likely will result in
35 substantial harm to a respondent's health, safety or welfare, and for which
36 the appointment of a guardian is necessary because no other person has
37 authority and is willing to act on the respondent's behalf;
38 (2) "home state" means the state in which the respondent was
39 physically present, including any period of temporary absence, for at least
40 six consecutive months immediately before the filing of a petition for a
41 protective order or the appointment of a guardian, or if none, the state in
42 which the respondent was physically present, including any period of
43 temporary absence, for at least six consecutive months ending within the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 4
1 six months prior to the filing of the petition; and
2 (3) "significant-connection state" means a state, other than the home
3 state, with which a respondent has a significant connection other than mere
4 physical presence and in which substantial evidence concerning the
5 respondent is available.
6 (b) In determining under sections 9 and 16(e), and amendments
7 thereto, whether a respondent has a significant connection with a particular
8 state, the court shall consider:
9 (1) The location of the respondent's family and other persons required
10 to be notified of the guardianship or protective proceeding;
11 (2) the length of time the respondent at any time was physically
12 present in the state and the duration of any absence;
13 (3) the location of the respondent's property; and
14 (4) the extent to which the respondent has ties to the state such as
15 voting registration, state or local tax return filing, vehicle registration,
16 driver's license, social relationship and receipt of services.
17 New Sec. 8. Sections 7 through 15, and amendments thereto,
18 provides the exclusive jurisdictional basis for a court of this state to
19 appoint a guardian or issue a protective order for an adult.
20 New Sec. 9. A court of this state has jurisdiction to appoint a guardian
21 or issue a protective order for a respondent if:
22 (a) This state is the respondent's home state;
23 (b) on the date the petition is filed, this state is a significant-
24 connection state and:
25 (1) The respondent does not have a home state or a court of the
26 respondent's home state has declined to exercise jurisdiction because this
27 state is a more appropriate forum; or
28 (2) the respondent has a home state, a petition for an appointment or
29 order is not pending in a court of that state or another significant-
30 connection state, and, before the court makes the appointment or issues the
31 order:
32 (A) A petition for an appointment or order is not filed in the
33 respondent's home state;
34 (B) an objection to the court's jurisdiction is not filed by a person
35 required to be notified of the proceeding; and
36 (C) the court in this state concludes that it is an appropriate forum
37 under the factors set forth in section 12, and amendments thereto;
38 (c) this state does not have jurisdiction under either subsection (a) or
39 (b), the respondent's home state and all significant-connection states have
40 declined to exercise jurisdiction because this state is the more appropriate
41 forum and jurisdiction in this state is consistent with the constitutions of
42 this state and the United States; or
43 (d) the requirements for special jurisdiction under section 10, and
HB 2359—Am. by HC 5
1 amendments thereto, are met.
2 New Sec. 10. (a) A court of this state lacking jurisdiction under
3 section 9(a), (b) or (c), and amendments thereto, has special jurisdiction to
4 do any of the following:
5 (1) Appoint a guardian in an emergency for a term not exceeding 90
6 days for a respondent who is physically present in this state;
7 (2) issue a protective order with respect to real or tangible personal
8 property located in this state;
9 (3) appoint a guardian or conservator for an incapacitated or protected
10 person for whom a provisional order to transfer the proceeding from
11 another state has been issued under procedures similar to section 16, and
12 amendments thereto.
13 (b) If a petition for the appointment of a guardian in an emergency is
14 brought in this state and this state was not the respondent's home state on
15 the date the petition was filed, the court shall dismiss the proceeding at the
16 request of the court of the home state, if any, whether dismissal is
17 requested before or after the emergency appointment.
18 New Sec. 11. Except as otherwise provided in section 10, and
19 amendments thereto, a court that has appointed a guardian or issued a
20 protective order consistent with this act has exclusive and continuing
21 jurisdiction over the proceeding until it is terminated by the court or the
22 appointment or order expires by its own terms.
23 New Sec. 12. (a) A court of this state having jurisdiction under
24 section 9, and amendments thereto, to appoint a guardian or issue a
25 protective order may decline to exercise its jurisdiction if it determines at
26 any time that a court of another state is a more appropriate forum.
27 (b) If a court of this state declines to exercise its jurisdiction under
28 subsection (a), it shall either dismiss or stay the proceeding. The court may
29 impose any condition the court considers just and proper, including the
30 condition that a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a
31 protective order be filed promptly in another state.
32 (c) In determining whether it is an appropriate forum, the court shall
33 consider all relevant factors, including:
34 (1) Any expressed preference of the respondent;
35 (2) whether abuse, neglect or exploitation of the respondent has
36 occurred or is likely to occur and which state could best protect the
37 respondent from the abuse, neglect or exploitation;
38 (3) the length of time the respondent was physically present in or was
39 a legal resident of this or another state;
40 (4) the distance of the respondent from the court in each state;
41 (5) the financial circumstances of the respondent's estate;
42 (6) the nature and location of the evidence;
43 (7) the ability of the court in each state to decide the issue
HB 2359—Am. by HC 6
1 expeditiously and the procedures necessary to present evidence;
2 (8) the familiarity of the court of each state with the facts and issues
3 in the proceeding; and
4 (9) if an appointment were made, the court's ability to monitor the
5 conduct of the guardian or conservator.
6 New Sec. 13. (a) If at any time a court of this state determines that it
7 acquired jurisdiction to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order
8 because of unjustifiable conduct, the court may:
9 (1) Decline to exercise jurisdiction;
10 (2) exercise jurisdiction for the limited purpose of fashioning an
11 appropriate remedy to ensure the health, safety and welfare of the
12 respondent or the protection of the respondent's property or prevent a
13 repetition of the unjustifiable conduct, including staying the proceeding
14 until a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a
15 protective order is filed in a court of another state having jurisdiction; or
16 (3) continue to exercise jurisdiction after considering:
17 (A) The extent to which the respondent and all persons required to be
18 notified of the proceedings have acquiesced in the exercise of the court's
19 jurisdiction;
20 (B) whether it is a more appropriate forum than the court of any other
21 state under the factors set forth in section 12(c), and amendments thereto;
22 and
23 (C) whether the court of any other state would have jurisdiction under
24 factual circumstances in substantial conformity with the jurisdictional
25 standards of section 9, and amendments thereto.
26 (b) If a court of this state determines that it acquired jurisdiction to
27 appoint a guardian or issue a protective order because a party seeking to
28 invoke its jurisdiction engaged in unjustifiable conduct, it may assess
29 against that party necessary and reasonable expenses, including attorney
30 fees, investigative fees, court costs, communication expenses, witness fees
31 and expenses and travel expenses. The court may not assess fees, costs or
32 expenses of any kind against this state or a governmental subdivision,
33 agency or instrumentality of this state unless authorized by law other than
34 this act.
35 New Sec. 14. If a petition for the appointment of a guardian or
36 issuance of a protective order is brought in this state and this state was not
37 the respondent's home state on the date the petition was filed, in addition
38 to complying with the notice requirements of this state, notice of the
39 petition must be given to those persons who would be entitled to notice of
40 the petition if a proceeding were brought in the respondent's home state.
41 The notice must be given in the same manner as notice is required to be
42 given in this state.
43 New Sec. 15. Except for a petition for the appointment of a guardian
HB 2359—Am. by HC 7
1 in an emergency or issuance of a protective order limited to property
2 located in this state under section 10(a)(1) or (2), and amendments thereto,
3 if a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a protective
4 order is filed in this state and in another state and neither petition has been
5 dismissed or withdrawn, the following rules apply:
6 (a) If the court in this state has jurisdiction under section 9, and
7 amendments thereto, it may proceed with the case unless a court in another
8 state acquires jurisdiction under provisions similar to section 9, and
9 amendments thereto, before the appointment or issuance of the order.
10 (b) If the court in this state does not have jurisdiction under section 9,
11 and amendments thereto, whether at the time the petition is filed or at any
12 time before the appointment or issuance of the order, the court shall stay
13 the proceeding and communicate with the court in the other state. If the
14 court in the other state has jurisdiction, the court in this state shall dismiss
15 the petition unless the court in the other state determines that the court in
16 this state is a more appropriate forum.
17 New Sec. 16. (a) A guardian or conservator appointed in this state
18 may petition the court to transfer the guardianship or conservatorship to
19 another state.
20 (b) Notice of a petition under subsection (a) must be given to the
21 persons that would be entitled to notice of a petition in this state for the
22 appointment of a guardian or conservator.
23 (c) On the court's own motion or on request of the guardian or
24 conservator, the incapacitated or protected person, or other person required
25 to be notified of the petition, the court shall hold a hearing on a petition
26 filed pursuant to subsection (a).
27 (d) The court shall issue an order provisionally granting a petition to
28 transfer a guardianship and shall direct the guardian to petition for
29 guardianship in the other state if the court is satisfied that the guardianship
30 will be accepted by the court in the other state and the court finds that:
31 (1) The incapacitated person is physically present in or is reasonably
32 expected to move permanently to the other state;
33 (2) an objection to the transfer has not been made or, if an objection
34 has been made, the objector has not established that the transfer would be
35 contrary to the interests of the incapacitated person; and
36 (3) plans for care and services for the incapacitated person in the
37 other state are reasonable and sufficient.
38 (e) The court shall issue a provisional order granting a petition to
39 transfer a conservatorship and shall direct the conservator to petition for
40 conservatorship in the other state if the court is satisfied that the
41 conservatorship will be accepted by the court of the other state and the
42 court finds that:
43 (1) The protected person is physically present in or is reasonably
HB 2359—Am. by HC 8
1 expected to move permanently to the other state, or the protected person
2 has a significant connection to the other state considering the factors in
3 section 7(b), and amendments thereto;
4 (2) an objection to the transfer has not been made or, if an objection
5 has been made, the objector has not established that the transfer would be
6 contrary to the interests of the protected person; and
7 (3) adequate arrangements will be made for management of the
8 protected person's property.
9 (f) The court shall issue a final order confirming the transfer and
10 terminating the guardianship or conservatorship upon its receipt of:
11 (1) A provisional order accepting the proceeding from the court to
12 which the proceeding is to be transferred which is issued under provisions
13 similar to section 17, and amendments thereto; and
14 (2) the documents required to terminate a guardianship or
15 conservatorship in this state.
16 New Sec. 17. (a) To confirm transfer of a guardianship or
17 conservatorship transferred to this state under provisions similar to section
18 16, and amendments thereto, the guardian or conservator must petition the
19 court in this state to accept the guardianship or conservatorship. The
20 petition must include a certified copy of the other state's provisional order
21 of transfer.
22 (b) Notice of a petition under subsection (a) must be given to those
23 persons that would be entitled to notice if the petition were a petition for
24 the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a protective order in both the
25 transferring state and this state. The notice must be given in the same
26 manner as notice is required to be given in this state.
27 (c) On the court's own motion or on request of the guardian or
28 conservator, the incapacitated or protected person, or other person required
29 to be notified of the proceeding, the court shall hold a hearing on a petition
30 filed pursuant to subsection (a).
31 (d) The court shall issue an order provisionally granting a petition
32 filed under subsection (a) unless:
33 (1) An objection is made and the objector establishes that transfer of
34 the proceeding would be contrary to the interests of the incapacitated or
35 protected person; or
36 (2) the guardian or conservator is ineligible for appointment in this
37 state.
38 (e) The court shall issue a final order accepting the proceeding and
39 appointing the guardian or conservator as guardian or conservator in this
40 state upon its receipt from the court from which the proceeding is being
41 transferred of a final order issued under provisions similar to section 16,
42 and amendments thereto, transferring the proceeding to this state.
43 (f) Not later than 90 days after issuance of a final order accepting
HB 2359—Am. by HC 9
1 transfer of a guardianship or conservatorship, the court shall determine
2 whether the guardianship or conservatorship needs to be modified to
3 conform to the law of this state.
4 (g) In granting a petition under this section, the court shall recognize
5 a guardianship or conservatorship order from the other state, including the
6 determination of the incapacitated or protected person's incapacity and the
7 appointment of the guardian or conservator.
8 (h) The denial by a court of this state of a petition to accept a
9 guardianship or conservatorship transferred from another state does not
10 affect the ability of the guardian or conservator to seek appointment as
11 guardian or conservator in this state under sections 24 through 135, and
12 amendments thereto, if the court has jurisdiction to make an appointment
13 other than by reason of the provisional order of transfer.
14 New Sec. 18. If a guardian has been appointed in another state and a
15 petition for the appointment of a guardian is not pending in this state, the
16 guardian appointed in the other state, after giving notice to the appointing
17 court of an intent to register, may register the guardianship order in this
18 state by filing as a foreign judgment in a court, in any appropriate county
19 of this state, certified copies of the order and letters of office.
20 New Sec. 19. If a conservator has been appointed in another state and
21 a petition for a protective order is not pending in this state, the conservator
22 appointed in the other state, after giving notice to the appointing court of
23 an intent to register, may register the protective order in this state by filing
24 as a foreign judgment in a court of this state, in any county in which
25 property belonging to the protected person is located, certified copies of
26 the order and letters of office and of any bond.
27 New Sec. 20. (a) Upon registration of a guardianship or protective
28 order from another state, the guardian or conservator may exercise in this
29 state all powers authorized in the order of appointment except as
30 prohibited under the laws of this state, including maintaining actions and
31 proceedings in this state and, if the guardian or conservator is not a
32 resident of this state, subject to any conditions imposed upon nonresident
33 parties.
34 (b) A court of this state may grant any relief available under this act
35 and other law of this state to enforce a registered order.
36 New Sec. 21. In applying and construing this uniform act,
37 consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law
38 with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it.
39 New Sec. 22. This act modifies, limits or supersedes the electronic
40 signatures in global and national commerce act, 15 U.S.C. § 7001 et seq.,
41 but does not modify, limit or supersede section 101(c) of that act, 15
42 U.S.C. § 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices
43 described in section 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. § 7003(b).
HB 2359—Am. by HC 10
1 New Sec. 23. (a) This act applies to guardianship and protective
2 proceedings begun on or after January 1, 2026.
3 (b) Sections 1 through 6 and 16 through 22, and amendments thereto,
4 apply to proceedings begun before January 1, 2026, regardless of whether
5 a guardianship or protective order has been issued.
6 New Sec. 24. Sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto, may
7 be cited as the Kansas uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other
8 protective arrangements act.
9 New Sec. 25. As used in this act:
10 (a) "Adult" means an individual at least 18 years of age or an
11 emancipated individual under 18 years of age.
12 (b) "Adult subject to conservatorship" means an adult for whom a
13 conservator has been appointed under this act.
14 (c) "Adult subject to guardianship" means an adult for whom a
15 guardian has been appointed under this act.
16 (d) "Claim" includes a claim against an individual or conservatorship
17 estate, whether arising in contract, tort or otherwise.
18 (e) "Conservator" means a person appointed by a court to make
19 decisions with respect to the property or financial affairs of an individual
20 subject to conservatorship. "Conservator" includes a co-conservator.
21 (f) "Conservatorship estate" means the property subject to
22 conservatorship under this act.
23 (g) "Expressly and with informed consent" means consent
24 voluntarily given with sufficient knowledge of the subject matter
25 involved, including a general understanding of the procedure,
26 medically acceptable alternative procedures or treatments and
27 substantial risks and hazards inherent in the proposed treatment or
28 procedures, to enable the person giving consent to make an
29 understanding and enlightened decision without any element of force,
30 fraud, deceit, duress or other form of constraint or coercion.
31 (h) "Full conservatorship" means a conservatorship that grants the
32 conservator all powers available under this act.
33 (h)(i) "Full guardianship" means a guardianship that grants the
34 guardian all powers available under this act.
35 (i)(j) "Guardian" means a person appointed by the court to make
36 decisions with respect to the personal affairs of an individual. "Guardian"
37 includes a co-guardian but does not include a guardian ad litem.
38 (j)(k) "Guardian ad litem" means a person appointed to inform the
39 court about, and to represent, the needs and best interest of an individual.
40 (l) "Hydration" means water or fluid administered in any
41 manner.
42 (k)(m) "Individual subject to conservatorship" means an adult or
43 minor for whom a conservator has been appointed under this act.
HB 2359—Am. by HC 11
1 (l)(n) "Individual subject to guardianship" means an adult or minor
2 for whom a guardian has been appointed under this act.
3 (m)(o) "Less restrictive alternative" means an approach to meeting an
4 individual's needs which restricts fewer rights of the individual than would
5 the appointment of a guardian or conservator. "Less restrictive alternative"
6 includes supported decision making, appropriate technological assistance,
7 appointment of a representative payee and appointment of an agent by the
8 individual, including appointment under a power of attorney for healthcare
9 or power of attorney for finances.
10 (n)(p) "Letters of office" means a record issued by a court certifying a
11 guardian's or conservator's authority to act.
12 (o)(q) "Limited conservatorship" means a conservatorship that grants
13 the conservator less than all powers available under this act, grants powers
14 over only certain property or otherwise restricts the powers of the
15 conservator.
16 (p)(r) "Limited guardianship" means a guardianship that grants the
17 guardian less than all powers available under this act or otherwise restricts
18 the powers of the guardian.
19 (q)(s) "Minor" means an unemancipated individual under 18 years of
20 age.
21 (r)(t) "Minor subject to conservatorship" means a minor for whom a
22 conservator has been appointed under this act.
23 (s)(u) "Minor subject to guardianship" means a minor for whom a
24 guardian has been appointed under this act.
25 (v) "Nutrition" means sustenance administered in any manner.
26 (t)(w) "Parent" does not include an individual whose parental rights
27 have been terminated.
28 (u)(x) "Person" means an individual, estate, business or nonprofit
29 entity, public corporation, government or governmental subdivision,
30 agency or instrumentality or other legal entity.
31 (y) "Person legally incapable of making health care decisions"
32 means any person who:
33 (1) (A) Has been declared legally unable to make decisions
34 affecting medical treatment or care; and
35 (B) in the reasonable medical judgment of the attending
36 physician, is unable to make decisions affecting medical treatment or
37 other health care services; or
38 (2) is a minor.
39 (v)(z) "Property" includes tangible and intangible property.
40 (w)(aa) "Protective arrangement instead of conservatorship" means a
41 court order entered under section 121, and amendments thereto.
42 (x)(bb) "Protective arrangement instead of guardianship" means a
43 court order entered under section 120, and amendments thereto.
HB 2359—Am. by HC 12
1 (cc) "Reasonable medical judgment" means a medical judgment
2 that would be made by a reasonably prudent physician,
3 knowledgeable about the case and the treatment possibilities with
4 respect to the medical conditions involved.
5 (y)(dd) "Record," used as a noun, means information that is inscribed
6 on a tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium
7 and is retrievable in perceivable form.
8 (z)(ee) "Respondent" means an individual for whom appointment of a
9 guardian or conservator or a protective arrangement instead of
10 guardianship or conservatorship is sought.
11 (aa)(ff) "Sign" means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a
12 record:
13 (1) To execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or
14 (2) to attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic
15 symbol, sound or process.
16 (bb)(gg) "Standby guardian" means a person appointed by the court
17 under section 57, and amendments thereto.
18 (cc)(hh) "State" means a state of the United States, the District of
19 Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands or any territory or
20 insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States. "State"
21 includes a federally recognized Indian tribe.
22 (dd)(ii) "Supported decision making" means assistance from one or
23 more persons of an individual's choosing in understanding the nature and
24 consequences of potential personal and financial decisions, which enables
25 the individual to make the decisions, and in communicating a decision
26 once made if consistent with the individual's wishes.
27 New Sec. 26. Unless displaced by a particular provision of this act,
28 the principles of law and equity supplement its provisions.
29 New Sec. 27. (a) Except to the extent jurisdiction is precluded by the

1 which the petition is filed has:
2 (1) Exclusive jurisdiction to determine the need for the guardianship,

8 New Sec. 29. (a) Except as provided in subsection (e), venue for a
9 guardianship proceeding for a minor is in:
10 (1) The county in which the minor resides or is present at the time the
11 proceeding commences; or
12 (2) the county in which another proceeding concerning the custody or
13 parental rights of the minor is pending.
14 (b) Except as provided in subsection (e), venue for a guardianship
15 proceeding or protective arrangement instead of guardianship for an adult
16 is in:
17 (1) The county in which the respondent resides;
18 (2) if the respondent has been admitted to an institution by court
19 order, the county in which the court is located; or
20 (3) if the proceeding is for appointment of an emergency guardian for
21 an adult, the county in which the respondent is present.
22 (c) Except as provided in subsection (e), venue for a conservatorship
23 proceeding or protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is in:
24 (1) The county in which the respondent resides, whether or not a
25 guardian has been appointed in another county or other jurisdiction; or
26 (2) if the respondent does not reside in this state, in any county in
27 which property of the respondent is located.
28 (d) If proceedings under this act are brought in more than one county,
29 the court of the county in which the first proceeding is brought has the
30 exclusive right to proceed unless the court determines that venue is
31 properly in another court or the interest of justice otherwise requires
32 transfer of the proceeding.
33 (e) If proceedings under this act are brought in a county other than as
34 provided in subsections (a), (b) or (c), the court may determine that venue
35 is proper if it is in the best interest of the respondent and in the interest of
36 justice for the proceedings to take place in that county.

42 other state, after giving notice to the appointing court, may register the
43 conservatorship in this state by filing as a foreign judgment, in a court of a

1 county in which property belonging to the individual subject to
2 conservatorship is located, certified copies of the order of conservatorship,
3 letters of office and any bond or other asset-protection arrangement

5 (c) On registration under this section of a guardianship or
6 conservatorship order from another state, the guardian or conservator may
7 exercise in this state all powers authorized in the order except as
8 prohibited by this act and law of this state other than this act. If the
9 guardian or conservator is not a resident of this state, the guardian or
10 conservator may maintain an action or proceeding in this state subject to

16 amendments thereto, jurisdiction remains with the court that established
17 the guardianship or conservatorship.
18 New Sec. 50. (a) An individual who is subject to guardianship or
19 conservatorship, or person interested in the welfare of an individual
20 subject to guardianship or conservatorship, who reasonably believes the
21 guardian or conservator is breaching the guardian's or conservator's
22 fiduciary duty or otherwise acting in a manner inconsistent with this act
23 may file a grievance in a record with the court. The clerk of the district
24 court shall forward the grievance to the presiding judge.
25 (b) Subject to subsection (c), after receiving a grievance under
26 subsection (a), the court:
27 (1) Shall review the grievance and, if necessary to determine the
28 appropriate response, court records related to the guardianship or
29 conservatorship;
30 (2) shall schedule a hearing if the individual subject to guardianship
31 or conservatorship is an adult and the grievance supports a reasonable
32 belief that:
33 (A) Removal of the guardian and appointment of a successor may be
34 appropriate under section 81, and amendments thereto;
35 (B) termination or modification of the guardianship may be
36 appropriate under section 82, and amendments thereto;
37 (C) removal of the conservator and appointment of a successor may
38 be appropriate under section 112, and amendments thereto; or
39 (D) termination or modification of the conservatorship may be
40 appropriate under section 113, and amendments thereto; and
41 (3) may take any action supported by the evidence, including:
42 (A) Ordering the guardian or conservator to provide the court a
43 report, accounting, inventory, updated plan or other information;
HB 2359—Am. by HC 26
1 (B) appointing a guardian ad litem;
2 (C) appointing an attorney for the individual subject to guardianship
3 or conservatorship; or
4 (D) holding a hearing.
5 (c) The court may decline to act under subsection (b) if a similar
6 grievance was filed within the six months preceding the filing of the
7 current grievance and the court followed the procedures of subsection (b)
8 in considering the earlier grievance.
9 New Sec. 51. (a) A person becomes a guardian for a minor only on
10 appointment by the court.
11 (b) After a hearing under section 53, and amendments thereto, the
12 court may appoint a guardian for a minor who does not have a guardian if
13 the court finds the appointment is in the minor's best interest and:
14 (1) Each parent of the minor, after being fully informed of the nature
15 and consequences of guardianship, consents;
16 (2) all parental rights have been terminated;
17 (3) there is clear and convincing evidence that the parents of the
18 minor are unwilling, unable or unfit to exercise the powers the court is
19 granting the guardian; or
20 (4) there is clear and convincing evidence that highly unusual or
21 extraordinary circumstances exist that cause the court to appoint the
22 guardian over the objection of a parent of the minor.
23 New Sec. 52. (a) A person interested in the welfare of a minor,
24 including the minor, may file a verified petition for appointment of a
25 guardian for the minor.
26 (b) A petition under subsection (a) must state the petitioner's name,
27 principal residence, current street address if different, relationship to the

39 attorney for each parent of the minor;

1 (b) Unless excused by the court for good cause, the person proposed

13 New Sec. 56. (a) After a hearing under section 53, and amendments
14 thereto, the court may appoint a guardian for a minor, if appointment is
15 proper under section 51, and amendments thereto, dismiss the proceeding
16 or take other appropriate action.
17 (b) In appointing a guardian under subsection (a), the following rules
18 apply:
19 (1) The court shall appoint a person nominated as guardian by a
20 parent of the minor in a will or other record unless the court finds the
21 appointment is contrary to the best interest of the minor.
22 (2) If multiple parents have nominated different persons to serve as
23 guardian, the court shall appoint the nominee whose appointment is in the
24 best interest of the minor, unless the court finds that appointment of none
25 of the nominees is in the best interest of the minor.
26 (3) If a guardian is not appointed under paragraph (1) or (2), the court
27 shall appoint the person nominated by the minor if the minor is 12 years of
28 age or older unless the court finds that appointment is contrary to the best
29 interest of the minor, in which case, the court shall appoint as guardian a
30 person whose appointment is in the best interest of the minor.
31 (c) An order granting a guardianship for a minor must state that each
32 parent of the minor is entitled to notice that:
33 (1) The guardian has changed the residence or school of the minor
34 subject to guardianship;
35 (2) the court has modified or limited the powers of the guardian; or
36 (3) the court has removed the guardian.
37 (d) An order granting a guardianship for a minor must identify any
38 person, in addition to a parent of the minor, who is entitled to notice of the
39 events listed in subsection (c).
40 (e) The appointment of a guardian under this section shall not be
41 construed to relieve a parent of any obligation imposed by law for the
42 support, maintenance, care, treatment, habilitation or education of that
43 parent's minor child.

1 New Sec. 57. (a) A standby guardian appointed under this section
2 may act as guardian, with all duties and powers of a guardian under
3 sections 59 and 60, and amendments thereto, when no parent of the minor
4 is willing or able to exercise the duties and powers granted to the guardian.
5 (b) A parent of a minor, in a signed record, may nominate a person to

7 a signed record, may revoke or amend the nomination at any time before
8 the court appoints a standby guardian.
9 (c) The court may appoint a standby guardian for a minor on:
10 (1) Petition by a parent of the minor or a person nominated under
11 subsection (b); and
12 (2) finding that no parent of the minor likely will be able or willing to
13 care for or make decisions with respect to the minor not later than two
14 years after the appointment.

43 New Sec. 58. (a) On its own, or on verified petition by a person
HB 2359—Am. by HC 32
1 interested in a minor's welfare, the court may appoint an emergency
2 guardian for the minor if the court finds a sufficient factual basis to
3 establish probable cause that:
4 (1) Appointment of an emergency guardian is necessary to prevent
5 imminent and substantial harm to the minor's health, safety or welfare; and
6 (2) no other person has authority and willingness to act in the
7 circumstances.
8 (b) The duration of authority of an emergency guardian for a minor
9 may not exceed 30 days, and the emergency guardian may exercise only
10 the powers specified in the order of appointment. The emergency
11 guardian's authority may be extended up to three times for not more than
12 30 days per extension if the court finds good cause and that the conditions
13 for appointment of an emergency guardian in subsection (a) continue.
14 (c) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (d), reasonable notice
15 of the date, time and place of a hearing on a petition for appointment of an
16 emergency guardian for a minor must be given to:
17 (1) The minor, if the minor is 12 years of age or older;
18 (2) any attorney appointed under section 54, and amendments thereto;
19 (3) each parent of the minor;
20 (4) any person, other than a parent, having care or custody of the
21 minor; and
22 (5) any other person the court determines.
23 (d) The court may appoint an emergency guardian for a minor
24 without notice under subsection (c) and without a hearing only if the court
25 finds from an affidavit or testimony that the minor's health, safety or
26 welfare will be substantially harmed before a hearing with notice on the
27 appointment can be held. If the court appoints an emergency guardian
28 without notice to an unrepresented minor or the attorney for a represented
29 minor, notice of the appointment must be given not later than 48 hours
30 after the appointment to the individuals listed in subsection (c). Not later
31 than seven days after the appointment, the court shall hold a hearing on the
32 appropriateness of the appointment.
33 (e) Appointment of an emergency guardian under this section, with or
34 without notice, is not a determination that a basis exists for appointment of
35 a guardian under section 51, and amendments thereto.
36 (f) The emergency guardian shall make any report the court requires.
37 (g) The court may remove an emergency guardian appointed under
38 this section at any time.
39 New Sec. 59. (a) A guardian for a minor is a fiduciary. Except as
40 otherwise limited by the court, a guardian for a minor has the duties and
41 responsibilities of a parent regarding the minor's support, care, education,
42 health, safety and welfare. A guardian shall act in the minor's best interest
43 and exercise reasonable care, diligence and prudence.
HB 2359—Am. by HC 33
1 (b) A guardian for a minor shall:
2 (1) Be personally acquainted with the minor and maintain sufficient
3 contact with the minor to know the minor's abilities, limitations, needs,
4 opportunities and physical and mental health;
5 (2) take reasonable care of the minor's personal effects and bring a
6 proceeding for a conservatorship, or protective arrangement instead of
7 conservatorship, if necessary to protect other property of the minor;
8 (3) if authorized by the court under section 61, and amendments
9 thereto, expend funds of the minor which have been received by the
10 guardian for the minor's current needs for support, care, education, health,
11 safety and welfare;
12 (4) conserve any funds of the minor not expended under paragraph
13 (3) for the minor's future needs, but if a conservator is appointed for the
14 minor, pay the funds at least quarterly to the conservator to be conserved
15 for the minor's future needs;
16 (5) report the condition of the minor and account for funds and other
17 property of the minor in the guardian's possession or subject to the
18 guardian's control, as required by court rule or ordered by the court on
19 application of a person interested in the minor's welfare;
20 (6) inform the court of any change in the minor's dwelling or address;
21 and
22 (7) in determining what is in the minor's best interest, take into
23 account the minor's preferences to the extent actually known or reasonably
24 ascertainable by the guardian.
25 New Sec. 60. (a) Except as otherwise limited by court order, a
26 guardian of a minor has the powers a parent otherwise would have
27 regarding the minor's support, care, education, health, safety and welfare.
28 (b) Except as otherwise limited by court order, a guardian for a minor
29 may:
30 (1) If authorized by the court under section 61, and amendments
31 thereto, apply for and receive funds and benefits otherwise payable for the
32 support of the minor to the minor's parent, guardian or custodian under a
33 statutory system of benefits or insurance or any private contract, devise,
34 trust, conservatorship or custodianship;
35 (2) unless inconsistent with a court order entitled to recognition in
36 this state, take custody of the minor and establish the minor's place of
37 dwelling and, on authorization of the court, establish or move the minor's
38 dwelling outside this state;
39 (3) if the minor is not subject to conservatorship, commence a

1 (c) The court may authorize a guardian for a minor to consent to the

6 New Sec. 61. A guardian for a minor may not exercise any control or
7 authority over the minor's estate, unless specifically authorized by the
8 court. Any guardian who is granted such authority must prepare an
9 inventory and provide notice of the inventory as provided in section 104,
10 and amendments thereto. The court may assign such authority to the
11 guardian and may waive the requirement of the posting of a bond, only if:
12 (a) Initially, the combined value of any funds and assets owned by the
13 minor equals $25,000 or less;
14 (b) either the court requires the guardian to report to the court the
15 commencement of the exercising of such authority, or requires the
16 guardian to obtain court authorization to commence the exercise of such
17 authority, as the court shall specify; and
18 (c) the court also requires the guardian, whenever the combined value
19 of such funds and property exceeds $25,000, to:
20 (1) File a guardian's plan as provided for in section 63, and
21 amendments thereto, that contains elements similar to those that would be
22 contained in a conservator's plan as provided for in section 103, and
23 amendments thereto;
24 (2) petition the court for appointment of a conservator; or
25 (3) notify the court as the court shall specify that the value of the
26 minor's estate has equaled or exceeded $25,000, if the court has earlier
27 appointed a conservator but did not issue letters of conservatorship
28 pending such notification.
29 New Sec. 62. (a) Guardianship under this act for a minor terminates:
30 (1) On the minor's death, adoption, emancipation or attainment of
31 majority; or
32 (2) when the court finds that the standard in section 51, and
33 amendments thereto, for appointment of a guardian is not satisfied, unless
34 the court finds that:
35 (A) Termination of the guardianship would be harmful to the minor;
36 and
37 (B) the minor's interest in the continuation of the guardianship
38 outweighs the interest of any parent of the minor in restoration of the
39 parent's right to make decisions for the minor.
40 (b) A minor subject to guardianship or a person interested in the
41 welfare of the minor may petition the court to terminate the guardianship,
42 modify the guardianship, remove the guardian and appoint a successor
43 guardian or remove a standby guardian and appoint a different standby

1 guardian.

23 New Sec. 63. (a) At any time, the court may require the guardian of a
24 minor, or the guardian of a minor may choose, to develop and file with the
25 court a plan of care for the minor. Any such plan must be based on the
26 needs of the minor and take into account the best interest of the minor as
27 well as the minor's preferences, to the extent known to or reasonably
28 ascertainable by the guardian. The guardian may include in the plan:
29 (1) Where the minor will reside and attend school;
30 (2) whether the parents of the minor will have contact or visitation
31 with the minor;
32 (3) whether the parents of the minor will have access to medical,
33 educational or other records of the minor;
34 (4) whether the parents of the minor will retain any rights to decision
35 making regarding the minor's healthcare, education or other matters;
36 (5) any other provisions the guardian deems appropriate; and
37 (6) any other provisions the court requires.
38 (b) The guardian for a minor shall give notice of the filing of the
39 guardian's plan under subsection (a), together with a copy of the plan, to
40 the minor if the minor is 12 years of age or older, any attorney representing
41 the minor in the guardianship proceeding or any other proceeding
42 concerning the care or custody of the minor identified in the petition, each
43 parent of the minor, a person entitled to notice under section 56(d), and
HB 2359—Am. by HC 36
1 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
2 determines. The notice shall include a statement of the right to object to
3 the plan and shall be given at the time of the filing.
4 (c) The minor, a parent of the minor and any person entitled under
5 subsection (b) to receive notice and a copy of the guardian's plan may
6 object to the plan in writing not later than 21 days after the filing.
7 (d) The court shall review the guardian's plan filed under subsection
8 (a) and determine whether to approve the plan, modify the plan or require
9 a new plan. In deciding whether to approve the plan, the court shall
10 consider an objection under subsection (c) and whether the plan is
11 consistent with the guardian's duties and powers under sections 59 and 60,
12 and amendments thereto. The court may not approve the plan until 30 days
13 after the filing.
14 (e) After the guardian's plan filed under this section is approved by

16 minor is 12 years of age or older, to any attorney representing the minor in

19 minor, to any person entitled to notice under section 56(d), and

22 New Sec. 64. (a) On petition and after notice and hearing, the court
23 may:
24 (1) Appoint a guardian for an adult if the court finds by clear and
25 convincing evidence that:
26 (A) The respondent lacks the ability to meet essential requirements
27 for physical health, safety or self-care because the respondent is unable to
28 receive and evaluate information or make or communicate decisions, even
29 with appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported
30 decision making; and
31 (B) the respondent's identified needs cannot be met by a protective
32 arrangement instead of guardianship or other less restrictive alternative; or
33 (2) with appropriate findings, treat the petition as one for a
34 conservatorship under sections 83 through 118, and amendments thereto,
35 or a protective arrangement under sections 119 through 130, and
36 amendments thereto, issue any appropriate order or dismiss the
37 proceeding.
38 (b) The court shall grant a guardian appointed under subsection (a)
39 only those powers necessitated by the demonstrated needs and limitations
40 of the respondent and issue orders that will encourage development of the
41 respondent's maximum self-determination and independence. The court
42 may not establish a full guardianship if a limited guardianship, protective
43 arrangement instead of guardianship or other less restrictive alternatives

2 New Sec. 65. (a) A person interested in an adult's welfare, including
3 the adult for whom the order is sought, may file a verified petition for
4 appointment of a guardian for the adult.
5 (b) A petition under subsection (a) must state the petitioner's name,
6 principal residence, current street address if different, relationship to the

9 following:
10 (1) The respondent's name, age, principal residence, current street
11 address if different and address of the dwelling in which it is proposed the
12 respondent will reside if the petition is granted;
13 (2) the name and address of the respondent's:
14 (A) Spouse or, if the respondent has none, an adult with whom the
15 respondent has shared household responsibilities for more than six months
16 in the 12-month period immediately before the filing of the petition;
17 (B) adult children, adult stepchildren, adult grandchildren and each
18 parent and adult sibling of the respondent, or, if none, at least one adult
19 nearest in kinship to the respondent who can be found with reasonable
20 diligence; and
21 (C) adult former stepchildren with whom the respondent had an
22 ongoing relationship in the two-year period immediately before the filing
23 of the petition;
24 (3) the name and current address of each of the following, if
25 applicable:
26 (A) A person primarily responsible for care of the respondent;
27 (B) any attorney currently representing the respondent;
28 (C) any representative payee appointed by the social security
29 administration for the respondent;
30 (D) a guardian or conservator acting for the respondent in this state or
31 in another jurisdiction;

39 New Sec. 66. (a) On filing of a petition under section 65, and
40 amendments thereto, for appointment of a guardian for an adult, the court
41 shall set a date, time and place for hearing the petition.
42 (b) A copy of a petition under section 65, and amendments thereto,
43 and notice of a hearing on the petition must be served personally on the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 39
1 respondent. The notice must inform the respondent of the respondent's
2 rights at the hearing, including the right to an attorney and to attend the
3 hearing. The notice must include a description of the nature, purpose and
4 consequences of granting the petition. The court may not grant the petition
5 if notice substantially complying with this subsection is not served on the
6 respondent. The court may order any of the following persons to serve the
7 notice upon the respondent:
8 (1) The petitioner or the attorney for the petitioner;
9 (2) the attorney appointed by the court to represent the respondent;
10 (3) any law enforcement officer; or
11 (4) any other person whom the court finds to be a proper person to
12 serve this notice.
13 (c) In a proceeding on a petition under section 65, and amendments
14 thereto, the notice required under subsection (b) must be given to the
15 persons required to be listed in the petition under section 65(b)(1) through
16 (3), and amendments thereto, and any other person interested in the
17 respondent's welfare the court determines. Failure to give notice under this
18 subsection does not preclude the court from appointing a guardian.
19 (d) After the appointment of a guardian, notice of a hearing on a
20 petition for any other order under sections 64 through 82, and amendments
21 thereto, together with a copy of the petition, must be given to:
22 (1) The adult subject to guardianship;
23 (2) the guardian; and
24 (3) any other person the court determines.
25 New Sec. 67. (a) On receipt of a petition under section 65, and
26 amendments thereto, for appointment of a guardian for an adult, the court
27 may appoint a court liaison. The court liaison must be an individual with
28 training or experience in the type of abilities, limitations and needs alleged
29 in the petition.
30 (b) (1) A court liaison appointed under subsection (a) shall interview
31 the respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is best able to
32 understand:
33 (A) Explain, in general, the petition and the nature and purpose of the
34 proceeding, including the potential loss of rights as a result of the
35 proceeding; and
36 (B) obtain the respondent's views about the appointment sought by
37 the petitioner, including views about a proposed guardian, the guardian's
38 proposed powers and duties and the scope and duration of the proposed
39 guardianship.
40 (2) These explanations and discussions are not intended to be a
41 substitute for the attorney appointed to represent the respondent to inform
42 the respondent of the respondent's rights and the nature and purpose of the
43 proceeding.

4 New Sec. 68. (a) The court shall appoint an attorney to represent the
5 respondent, regardless of the respondent's ability to pay. The court shall
6 give preference in the appointment of an attorney to any attorney who has
7 represented the respondent in other matters if the court has knowledge of
8 that prior representation or to an attorney whom the respondent has
9 requested. Any appointment made by the court shall terminate after the
10 guardian's plan has been approved and after any appeal from the
11 appointment of a guardian, unless the court continues the appointment by
12 further order. Thereafter, an attorney may be appointed by the court if
13 requested, in writing, by the adult subject to guardianship, the guardian, or
14 upon the court's own motion.
15 (b) An attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding for
16 appointment of a guardian for an adult shall:
17 (1) Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes;
18 (2) advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably
19 ascertainable; and
20 (3) if the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable,
21 advocate for the result that is the least restrictive in type, duration and
22 scope, consistent with the respondent's interests.
23 (c) An attorney representing the respondent shall interview the
24 respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is best able to
25 understand:
26 (1) Explain to the respondent the substance of the petition, the nature,
27 purpose and effect of the proceeding, the respondent's rights at the hearing
28 on the petition and the general powers and duties of a guardian;
29 (2) determine the respondent's views about the appointment sought by
30 the petitioner, including views about a proposed guardian, the guardian's
31 proposed powers and duties and the scope and duration of the proposed
32 guardianship; and
33 (3) inform the respondent that all costs and expenses of the
34 proceeding, including respondent's attorney fees, may be paid from the
35 respondent's assets.
36 New Sec. 69. (a) Upon the filing of the petition or any other time at
37 or before the hearing, if the contents of the petition or evidence at the
38 hearing support a prima facie case of the need for a guardian, the court
39 shall order an examination and evaluation of the respondent to be
40 conducted through a general hospital, psychiatric hospital, community
41 mental health center, community developmental disability organization or
42 by a licensed physician, psychiatrist, psychologist, physician assistant,
43 nurse practitioner, social worker or other professional appointed by the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 42
1 court who is qualified to evaluate the respondent's alleged cognitive and
2 functional abilities and limitations and will not be advantaged or
3 disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition or otherwise have a
4 conflict of interest.
5 (b) Unless otherwise specified by the court, the report of the
6 examination and evaluation submitted to the court shall contain:
7 (1) The respondent's name, age and date of birth;
8 (2) a description of the respondent's physical and mental condition;
9 (3) a description of the nature and extent of the respondent's cognitive
10 and functional abilities and limitations, including adaptive behaviors and
11 social skills, and, as appropriate, educational and developmental potential;
12 (4) a summary of self-care and independent-living tasks the
13 respondent can manage without assistance or with existing supports, could
14 manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive services,
15 technological assistance or supported decision making, and cannot
16 manage;
17 (5) a prognosis for any improvement and, as appropriate, any
18 recommendation for treatment or rehabilitation;
19 (6) a list and description of any prior assessments, evaluations or
20 examinations of the respondent, including the dates thereof, which were
21 relied upon in the preparation of this evaluation;
22 (7) the date and location where this examination and evaluation
23 occurred, and the name or names of the professional or professionals
24 performing the examination and evaluation and such professional's
25 qualifications;
26 (8) a statement by the professional that the professional has
27 personally completed an independent examination and evaluation of the
28 respondent, and that the report submitted to the court contains the results
29 of that examination and evaluation, and the professional's opinion with
30 regard to the issues of whether or not the respondent is in need of a
31 guardian and whether there are barriers to the respondent's attendance and
32 participation at the hearing on the petition; and
33 (9) the signature of the professional who prepared the report.
34 (c) The professional shall file with the court, at least five days prior to
35 the date of the trial, such professional's written report concerning the
36 examination and evaluation ordered by the court. The report shall be made
37 available by the court to counsel for all parties.
38 (d) In lieu of entering an order for an examination and evaluation as
39 provided for in this section, the court may determine that the report
40 accompanying the petition is in compliance with the requirements of this
41 section and that no further examination or evaluation should be required,
42 unless the respondent, or such person's attorney, requests such an
43 examination and evaluation in writing. Any such request shall be filed with
HB 2359—Am. by HC 43
1 the court, and a copy thereof delivered to the petitioner, at least four days
2 prior to the date of the trial. Accompanying the request shall be a statement
3 of the reasons why an examination and evaluation is requested and the
4 name and address of a qualified professional or facility willing and able to
5 conduct this examination and evaluation. If the court orders a further
6 examination and evaluation, the court may continue the trial and fix a new
7 date, time and place of the trial at a time not to exceed 30 days from the
8 date of the filing of the request.
9 New Sec. 70. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (b), a
10 hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto, may not proceed unless
11 the respondent attends the hearing. If it is not reasonably feasible for the
12 respondent to attend a hearing at the location court proceedings typically
13 are held, the court shall make reasonable efforts to hold the hearing at an
14 alternative location convenient to the respondent or allow the respondent
15 to attend the hearing using real-time audio-visual technology.
16 (b) A hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto, may
17 proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court finds by clear
18 and convincing evidence that:
19 (1) The respondent is choosing not to attend the hearing after having
20 been fully informed of the right to attend and the potential consequences
21 of failing to do so; or
22 (2) there is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and
23 participate in the hearing even with appropriate supportive services and
24 technological assistance.
25 (c) The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under section 66, and
26 amendments thereto, by a person or persons of the respondent's choosing,
27 assistive technology or an interpreter or translator, or a combination of
28 these supports. If assistance would facilitate the respondent's participation
29 in the hearing, but is not otherwise available to the respondent, the court
30 shall make reasonable efforts to provide it.
31 (d) The respondent has a right to retain an attorney to represent the
32 respondent at a hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto.
33 (e) At a hearing held under section 66, and amendments thereto, the
34 respondent may:
35 (1) Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents;
36 (2) examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator and
37 the court liaison; and
38 (3) otherwise participate in the hearing.
39 (f) Unless excused by the court for good cause, a proposed guardian
40 shall attend a hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto.
41 (g) A hearing under section 66, and amendments thereto, must be
42 closed on request of the respondent and a showing of good cause.
43 (h) Any person may request to participate in a hearing under section

1 66, and amendments thereto. The court may grant the request, with or
2 without a hearing, on determining that the best interest of the respondent
3 will be served. The court may impose appropriate conditions on the
