5 New Sec. 71. (a) The existence of a proceeding for or the existence of
6 a guardianship for an adult is a matter of public record unless the court
7 seals the record after:
8 (1) The respondent or individual subject to guardianship requests the
9 record be sealed; and
10 (2) either:
11 (A) The petition for guardianship is dismissed; or
12 (B) the guardianship is terminated.
13 (b) (1) The following court records are a matter of public record
14 unless sealed by the court:
15 (A) Letters of guardianship;
16 (B) orders suspending or removing a guardian; and
17 (C) orders terminating a guardianship.
18 (2) All other court records of a guardianship proceeding are not a
19 matter of public record except as further provided.
20 (3) The following persons are entitled to access court records of the
21 proceeding and resulting guardianship, including the guardian's plan under
22 section 79, and amendments thereto, and report under section 80, and
23 amendments thereto:
24 (A) An adult subject to a proceeding for a guardianship, whether or
25 not a guardian is appointed;
26 (B) an attorney designated by the adult;
27 (C) a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and amendments
28 thereto, or a subsequent order; and
29 (D) a licensed attorney, abstractor or title insurance agent.
30 (4) A person not otherwise entitled to access court records under this
31 subsection for good cause may request permission from the court for
32 access to court records of the guardianship, including the guardian's report
33 and plan. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest of the
34 respondent or adult subject to guardianship or furthers the public interest
35 and does not endanger the welfare or financial interests of the adult.
36 (c) A report under section 67, and amendments thereto, of a court
37 liaison or a professional evaluation under section 69, and amendments
38 thereto, is confidential and must be sealed on filing, but is available to:
39 (1) The court;
40 (2) the individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation,
41 without limitation as to use;
42 (3) the petitioner, court liaison and petitioner's and respondent's
43 attorneys, for purposes of the proceeding;
HB 2359—Am. by HC 45
1 (4) unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a
2 power of attorney for healthcare or power of attorney for finances in which
3 the respondent is the principal; and
4 (5) any other person if it is in the public interest or for a purpose the
5 court orders for good cause.
6 New Sec. 72. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c), the
7 court in appointing a guardian for an adult shall consider persons qualified
8 to be guardian in the following order of priority:
9 (1) A guardian, other than a temporary or emergency guardian,
10 currently acting for the respondent in another jurisdiction;
11 (2) a person nominated as guardian by the respondent, including the
12 respondent's most recent nomination made in a power of attorney;
13 (3) an agent appointed by the respondent under a power of attorney
14 for healthcare;
15 (4) a spouse of the respondent;
16 (5) a family member or other individual who has shown special care
17 and concern for the respondent; and
18 (6) a person nominated as guardian by the spouse, adult child or other
19 close family member of the respondent.
20 (b) If two or more persons have equal priority under subsection (a),
21 the court shall select as guardian the person the court considers best
22 qualified. In determining the best qualified person, the court shall consider
23 the person's relationship with the respondent, the person's skills, the
24 expressed wishes of the respondent, the extent to which the person and the
25 respondent have similar values and preferences and the likelihood the
26 person will be able to perform the duties of a guardian successfully.
27 (c) The court, acting in the best interest of the respondent, may
28 decline to appoint as guardian a person having priority under subsection
29 (a) and appoint a person having a lower priority or no priority.
30 (d) In determining whether the appointment of a proposed guardian is
31 in the best interest of the respondent, the court shall consider the number
32 of other cases in which the proposed guardian, other than a corporation, is
33 currently serving as guardian, particularly if that number is more than 15.
34 (e) The following persons shall not be appointed as guardian unless
35 the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that the person is the best
36 qualified person available for appointment and the appointment is in the
37 best interest of the respondent:
38 (1) A person that provides paid services to the respondent, or an
39 individual who is employed by a person that provides paid services to the
40 respondent, or is the spouse, parent or child of an individual who provides
41 or is employed to provide paid services to the respondent;
42 (2) an owner, operator or employee of any entity at which the
43 respondent is receiving care; and
HB 2359—Am. by HC 46
1 (3) a person who provides care or other services, or is an employee of
2 an agency, partnership or corporation that provides care or other services
3 to persons with needs similar to those of the respondent.
4 New Sec. 73. (a) A court order appointing a guardian for an adult
5 must:
6 (1) Include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence
7 established that the identified needs of the respondent cannot be met by a
8 protective arrangement instead of guardianship or other less restrictive
9 alternative, including use of appropriate supportive services, technological
10 assistance or supported decision making; and
11 (2) include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence
12 established the respondent was given proper notice of the hearing on the
13 petition.
14 (b) A court order establishing a full guardianship for an adult must
15 state the basis for granting a full guardianship and include specific findings
16 that support the conclusion that a limited guardianship would not meet the
17 functional needs of the adult subject to guardianship.
18 (c) A court order establishing a limited guardianship for an adult must
19 state the specific powers granted to the guardian.
20 (d) A court order appointing a guardian for an adult must include the
21 date of a review hearing to be set 90 days after the order of appointment is
22 entered. At that hearing, the court shall review the guardian's plan filed
23 pursuant to section 79, and amendments thereto.
24 (e) The court, as part of an order establishing a guardianship for an
25 adult, shall identify any person that subsequently is entitled to:
26 (1) Notice of the rights of the adult under section 74(b), and
27 amendments thereto;
28 (2) notice of a change in the primary dwelling of the adult;
29 (3) notice that the guardian will be unavailable to visit the adult for
30 more than two months or unavailable to perform the guardian's duties for
31 more than one month;
32 (4) a copy of the guardian's plan under section 79, and amendments
33 thereto, and the guardian's report under section 80, and amendments
34 thereto;
35 (5) access to court records relating to the guardianship;
36 (6) notice of the death or significant change in the condition of the
37 adult;
38 (7) notice of a petition or hearing to limit or modify the powers of the
39 guardian or that the court has limited or modified the powers of the
40 guardian; and
41 (8) notice of a petition or hearing to remove the guardian or that the
42 court has removed the guardian.
43 (f) A spouse and adult children of an adult subject to guardianship are
HB 2359—Am. by HC 47
1 entitled to notice under subsection (e) unless the court determines notice
2 would be contrary to the preferences or prior directions of the adult subject
3 to guardianship or not in the best interest of the adult.
4 New Sec. 74. (a) Not later than 14 days after the appointment, a
5 guardian appointed under section 72, and amendments thereto, shall give
6 the adult subject to guardianship and all other persons given notice under
7 section 66, and amendments thereto, a copy of the order of appointment.
8 (b) Not later than 30 days after appointment of a guardian under
9 section 72, and amendments thereto, the court or the court's designee shall
10 give to the adult subject to guardianship, the guardian and any other person
11 entitled to notice under section 72(e), and amendments thereto, or a
12 subsequent order a statement of the rights of the adult subject to
13 guardianship and procedures to seek relief if the adult is denied those
14 rights. The statement must be in at least 16-point font, in plain language
15 and, to the extent feasible, in a language in which the adult subject to
16 guardianship is proficient. The statement must notify the adult subject to
17 guardianship of the right to:
18 (1) Seek termination or modification of the guardianship, or removal
19 of the guardian, and choose an attorney to represent the adult in these
20 matters;
21 (2) file a grievance against the guardian under section 50, and
22 amendments thereto;
23 (3) be involved in decisions affecting the adult, including decisions
24 about the adult's care, dwelling, activities or social interactions, to the
25 extent reasonably feasible, and that the adult retains the right to vote and
26 the right to marry;
27 (4) be involved in healthcare decision making to the extent
28 reasonably feasible and supported in understanding the risks and benefits
29 of healthcare options to the extent reasonably feasible;
30 (5) be notified at least 14 days before a change in the adult's primary
31 dwelling or permanent move to a nursing home, mental health facility or
32 other facility that places restrictions on the individual's ability to leave or
33 have visitors unless the change or move is proposed in the guardian's plan
34 under section 79, and amendments thereto, or authorized by the court by
35 specific order;
36 (6) object to a change or move described in paragraph (5) and the
37 process for objecting;
38 (7) communicate, visit or interact with others, including receiving
39 visitors, and making or receiving telephone calls, personal mail or
40 electronic communications, including through social media, unless:
41 (A) The guardian has been authorized by the court by specific order
42 to restrict communications, visits or interactions;
43 (B) a protective order or protective arrangement instead of
HB 2359—Am. by HC 48
1 guardianship is in effect that limits contact between the adult and a person;
2 or
3 (C) the guardian has good cause to believe restriction is necessary
4 because interaction with a specified person poses a risk of significant
5 physical, psychological or financial harm to the adult, and the restriction
6 is:
7 (i) For a period of not more than seven business days if the person
8 has a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult; or
9 (ii) for a period of not more than 60 days if the person does not have
10 a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult;
11 (8) receive a copy of the guardian's plan under section 79, and
12 amendments thereto, and the guardian's report under section 80, and
13 amendments thereto; and
14 (9) object to the guardian's plan or report.
15 (c) Any person required to provide notice under this section shall file
16 proof of service of such notice with the court.
17 New Sec. 75. (a) On its own after a petition has been filed under
18 section 65, and amendments thereto, or on verified petition by a person
19 interested in an adult's welfare, the court may appoint an emergency
20 guardian for the adult if the court finds a sufficient factual basis to
21 establish probable cause that:
22 (1) Appointment of an emergency guardian is necessary to prevent
23 imminent and substantial harm to the adult's physical health, safety or
24 welfare;
25 (2) no other person has authority and willingness to act in the
26 circumstances; and
27 (3) a basis for appointment of a guardian under section 64, and
28 amendments thereto, exists.
29 (b) The duration of authority of an emergency guardian for an adult
30 may not exceed 30 days, and the emergency guardian may exercise only
31 the powers specified in the order of appointment. The emergency
32 guardian's authority may be extended up to three times for not more than
33 30 days per extension if the court finds good cause and that the conditions
34 for appointment of an emergency guardian in subsection (a) continue.
35 (c) Immediately upon filing of a petition for appointment of an
36 emergency guardian for an adult, the court shall appoint an attorney to
37 represent the respondent in the proceeding. Except as otherwise provided
38 in subsection (d), reasonable notice of the date, time, and place of a
39 hearing on the petition must be given to the respondent, the respondent's
40 attorney and any other person the court determines.
41 (d) The court may appoint an emergency guardian for an adult
42 without notice to the adult and any attorney for the adult only if the court
43 finds from an affidavit or testimony that the respondent's physical health,
HB 2359—Am. by HC 49
1 safety or welfare will be substantially harmed before a hearing with notice
2 on the appointment can be held. If the court appoints an emergency
3 guardian without giving notice under subsection (c), the court must:
4 (1) Give notice of the appointment not later than 48 hours after the
5 appointment to:
6 (A) The respondent;
7 (B) the respondent's attorney; and
8 (C) any other person the court determines; and
9 (2) hold a hearing on the appropriateness of the appointment not later
10 than five days after the appointment.
11 (e) Appointment of an emergency guardian under this section is not a
12 determination that a basis exists for appointment of a guardian under
13 section 64, and amendments thereto.
14 (f) The court may remove an emergency guardian appointed under
15 this section at any time. The emergency guardian shall make any report the
16 court requires.
17 New Sec. 76. (a) A guardian for an adult is a fiduciary. A guardian
18 shall strive to assure that the personal, civil and human rights of the
19 individual subject to guardianship are protected. Except as otherwise
20 limited by the court, a guardian for an adult shall make decisions regarding
21 the support, care, education, health and welfare of the adult subject to
22 guardianship to the extent necessitated by the adult's limitations and in
23 accordance with the guardian's plan under section 79, and amendments
24 thereto.
25 (b) A guardian for an adult shall promote the self-determination of the
26 adult and, to the extent reasonably feasible, include the adult in decision
27 making, and encourage the adult to participate in decisions, act on the
28 adult's own behalf, and develop or regain the capacity to manage the
29 adult's personal affairs. In furtherance of this duty, the guardian shall:
30 (1) Become or remain personally acquainted with the adult and
31 maintain sufficient contact with the adult, including through regular
32 visitation, to know the adult's abilities, limitations, needs, opportunities
33 and physical and mental health;
34 (2) to the extent reasonably feasible, identify the values and
35 preferences of the adult and involve the adult in decisions affecting the
36 adult, including decisions about the adult's care, dwelling, activities or
37 social interactions; and
38 (3) make reasonable efforts to identify and facilitate supportive
39 relationships and services for the adult.
40 (c) A guardian for an adult at all times shall exercise reasonable care,
41 diligence and prudence when acting on behalf of or making decisions for
42 the adult. In furtherance of this duty, the guardian shall:
43 (1) Take reasonable care of the personal effects and service or support
HB 2359—Am. by HC 50
1 animals of the adult and bring a proceeding for a conservatorship or
2 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship if necessary to protect
3 the adult's property;
4 (2) if authorized by the court under section 78, and amendments
5 thereto, expend funds and other property of the adult received by the
6 guardian for the adult's current needs for support, care, education, health
7 and welfare;
8 (3) conserve any funds and other property of the adult not expended
9 under paragraph (2) for the adult's future needs, but if a conservator has
10 been appointed for the adult, pay the funds and other property at least
11 quarterly to the conservator to be conserved for the adult's future needs;
12 and
13 (4) monitor the quality of services, including long-term care services,
14 provided to the adult.
15 (d) In making a decision for an adult subject to guardianship, the
16 guardian shall make the decision the guardian reasonably believes the
17 adult would make if the adult were able unless doing so would
18 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
19 interests of the adult. To determine the decision the adult subject to
20 guardianship would make if able, the guardian shall consider the adult's
21 previous or current directions, preferences, opinions, cultural practices,
22 religious beliefs, values and actions, to the extent actually known or
23 reasonably ascertainable by the guardian.
24 (e) If a guardian for an adult cannot make a decision under subsection
25 (d) because the guardian does not know and cannot reasonably determine
26 the decision the adult probably would make if able, or the guardian
27 reasonably believes the decision the adult would make would
28 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
29 interests of the adult, the guardian shall act in accordance with the best
30 interest of the adult. In determining the best interest of the adult, the
31 guardian shall consider:
32 (1) Information received from professionals and persons that
33 demonstrate sufficient interest in the welfare of the adult;
34 (2) other information the guardian believes the adult would have
35 considered if the adult were able to act; and
36 (3) other factors a reasonable person in the circumstances of the adult
37 would consider, including consequences for others.
38 (f) A guardian for an adult shall notify the court immediately if the
39 condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable of exercising
40 rights previously removed.
41 New Sec. 77. (a) Except as limited by court order, a guardian for an
42 adult may:
43 (1) If authorized by the court under section 78, and amendments
HB 2359—Am. by HC 51
1 thereto, apply for and receive funds and benefits for the support of the
2 adult, unless a conservator is appointed for the adult and the application or
3 receipt is within the powers of the conservator;
4 (2) establish the adult's place of dwelling;
5 (3) consent to health, including mental health, or other care, treatment
6 or service for the adult;
7 (4) if a conservator for the adult has not been appointed, commence a
8 proceeding including an administrative proceeding, or take other
9 appropriate action to compel another person to support the adult or pay
10 funds for the adult's benefit; and
11 (5) receive personally identifiable healthcare information regarding
12 the adult.
13 (b) The court by specific order may authorize a guardian for an adult
14 to consent to the adoption of the adult.
15 (c) The court by specific order may authorize a guardian for an adult
16 to litigate as petitioner or respondent an action for divorce, dissolution or
17 annulment of marriage of the individual subject to guardianship, including
18 negotiation of a settlement thereof.
19 (d) In determining whether to authorize a power under subsection (b)
20 or (c), the court shall consider whether the underlying act would be in
21 accordance with the adult's preferences, values and prior directions and
22 whether the underlying act would be in the adult's best interest.
23 (e) In exercising a guardian's power under subsection (a)(2) to
24 establish the adult's place of dwelling, the guardian shall:
25 (1) Select a residential setting the guardian believes the adult would
26 select if the adult were able, in accordance with the decision-making
27 standard in section 76(d) and (e), and amendments thereto. If the guardian
28 does not know and cannot reasonably determine what setting the adult
29 subject to guardianship probably would choose if able, or the guardian
30 reasonably believes the decision the adult would make would
31 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
32 interests of the adult, the guardian shall choose in accordance with section
33 76(e), and amendments thereto, a residential setting that is consistent with
34 the adult's best interest;
35 (2) in selecting among residential settings, give priority to a
36 residential setting in a location that will allow the adult to interact with
37 persons important to the adult and meet the adult's needs in the least
38 restrictive manner reasonably feasible unless to do so would be
39 inconsistent with the decision-making standard in section 76(d) and (e),
40 and amendments thereto;
41 (3) not later than 30 days after a change in the dwelling of the adult:
42 (A) Give notice of the change to the court, the adult and any person
43 identified as entitled to the notice in the court order appointing the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 52
1 guardian or a subsequent order; and
2 (B) include in the notice the address and nature of the new dwelling
3 and state whether the adult received advance notice of the change and
4 whether the adult objected to the change;
5 (4) establish or move the permanent place of dwelling of the adult to
6 a nursing home, mental health facility or other facility that places
7 restrictions on the adult's ability to leave or have visitors only if:
8 (A) The establishment or move is in the guardian's plan under section
9 79, and amendments thereto;
10 (B) the court authorizes the establishment or move; or
11 (C) the guardian gives notice of the establishment or move at least 14

22 (B) the court authorizes the action by specific order; or

25 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order and no objection has been
26 filed.
27 (f) In exercising a guardian's power under subsection (a)(3) to make
28 healthcare decisions, the guardian shall:
29 (1) Involve the adult in decision making to the extent reasonably
30 feasible, including, when practicable, by encouraging and supporting the
31 adult in understanding the risks and benefits of healthcare options;
32 (2) act in accordance with any declaration of the adult made pursuant
33 to the provisions of K.S.A. 65-28,101 through 65-28,109, and amendments
34 thereto; and
35 (3) take into account:
36 (A) The risks and benefits of treatment options; and
37 (B) the current and previous wishes and values of the adult, if known
38 or reasonably ascertainable by the guardian.
39 New Sec. 78. (a) A guardian for an adult may shall not initiate the
40 commitment of the adult to a mental health facility except in accordance
41 with the care and treatment act for mentally ill persons, K.S.A. 59-2945 et
42 seq., and amendments thereto.
43 (b) A guardian for an adult may shall not restrict the ability of the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 53
1 adult to communicate, visit or interact with others, including receiving
2 visitors and making or receiving telephone calls, personal mail or
3 electronic communications, including through social media, or
4 participating in social activities, unless:
5 (1) Authorized by the court by specific order;
6 (2) a protective order or a protective arrangement instead of
7 guardianship is in effect that limits contact between the adult and a person;
8 or
9 (3) the guardian has good cause to believe restriction is necessary
10 because interaction with a specified person poses a risk of significant
11 physical, psychological or financial harm to the adult and the restriction is:
12 (A) For a period of not more than seven business days if the person
13 has a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult; or
14 (B) for a period of not more than 60 days if the person does not have
15 a family or pre-existing social relationship with the adult.
16 (c) A guardian for an adult may shall not consent, on behalf of the
17 adult, to:
18 (1) Any psychosurgery, removal of any bodily organ or amputation of
19 any limb, unless such surgery, removal or amputation has been approved
20 in advance by the court, except in an emergency and when necessary to
21 preserve the life of the adult or to prevent serious and irreparable
22 impairment to the physical health of the adult;
23 (2) the sterilization of the adult, unless approved by the court
24 following a due process hearing held for the purposes of determining
25 whether to approve such, and during which hearing the adult is represented
26 by an attorney appointed by the court;
27 (3) the performance of any experimental biomedical or behavioral
28 procedure on the adult, or for the adult to be a participant in any
29 biomedical or behavioral experiment, without the prior review and
30 approval of such by either an institutional review board as provided for in
31 title 45, part 46 of the code of federal regulations, or if such regulations do
32 not apply, then by a review committee established by the agency,
33 institution or treatment facility at which the procedure or experiment is
34 proposed to occur, composed of members selected for the purposes of
35 determining whether the proposed procedure or experiment:
36 (A) Does not involve any significant risk of harm to the physical or
37 mental health of the adult, or the use of aversive stimulants, and is
38 intended to preserve the life or health of the adult or to assist the adult to
39 develop or regain skills or abilities; or
40 (B) involves a significant risk of harm to the physical or mental
41 health of the adult, or the use of an aversive stimulant, but that the
42 conducting of the proposed procedure or experiment is intended either to
43 preserve the life of the adult, or to significantly improve the quality of life
HB 2359—Am. by HC 54
1 of the adult, or to assist the adult to develop or regain significant skills or
2 abilities, and that the guardian has been fully informed concerning the

6 consented to such;
7 (4) the withholding or withdrawal of life-saving or life-sustaining

3 (d) (1) It shall be presumed that every adult under guardianship

18 New Sec. 79. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment and when
19 there is a significant change in circumstances, or the guardian seeks to
20 deviate significantly from the existing guardian's plan, a guardian for an
21 adult shall file with the court a plan for the care of the adult. The plan must
22 be based on the needs of the adult and take into account the best interest of
23 the adult as well as the adult's preferences, values and prior directions, to
24 the extent known to or reasonably ascertainable by the guardian. The
25 guardian shall include in the plan:
26 (1) The living arrangement, services and supports the guardian
27 expects to arrange, facilitate or continue for the adult;
28 (2) social and educational activities the guardian expects to facilitate
29 on behalf of the adult;
30 (3) any person with whom the adult has a close personal relationship
31 or relationship involving regular visitation and any plan the guardian has
32 for facilitating visits with the person;
33 (4) the anticipated nature and frequency of the guardian's visits and
34 communication with the adult;
35 (5) goals for the adult, including any goal related to the restoration of
36 the adult's rights, and how the guardian anticipates achieving the goals;
37 (6) whether the adult has an existing plan and, if so, whether the
38 guardian's plan is consistent with the adult's plan; and
39 (7) a statement or list of the amount the guardian proposes to charge
40 for each service the guardian anticipates providing to the adult.
41 (b) A guardian shall give notice of the filing of the guardian's plan
42 under subsection (a), together with a copy of the plan, to the adult subject
43 to guardianship, any attorney representing the adult subject to
HB 2359—Am. by HC 59
1 guardianship, a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and
2 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
3 determines. The notice must include a statement of the right to object to
4 the plan and must be given at the time of the filing.
5 (c) An adult subject to guardianship and any person entitled under
6 subsection (b) to receive notice and a copy of the guardian's plan may
7 object to the plan in writing no later than 21 days after the filing.
8 (d) The court shall review the guardian's plan filed under subsection
9 (a) and determine whether to approve the plan or require a new plan. In
10 deciding whether to approve the plan, the court shall consider an objection
11 under subsection (c) and whether the plan is consistent with the guardian's
12 duties and powers under sections 76 and 77, and amendments thereto. The
13 court shall review an initial guardian's plan at the review hearing
14 scheduled under section 73(b), and amendments thereto. When reviewing
15 subsequent guardian's plans, the court has discretion whether to set the
16 matter for hearing but may not approve the plan until 30 days after the
17 filing.
18 (e) After the guardian's plan filed under this section is approved by
19 the court, the guardian shall provide a copy of the plan to the adult subject
20 to guardianship, any attorney representing the adult subject to
21 guardianship, a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and
22 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
23 determines.
24 New Sec. 80. (a) A guardian for an adult shall file with the court at
25 least annually and at any other time the court directs a report in a record
26 regarding the condition of the adult and accounting for funds and other
27 property in the guardian's possession or subject to the guardian's control.
28 (b) A report under subsection (a) must state or contain:
29 (1) The mental, physical and social condition of the adult;
30 (2) the living arrangements of the adult during the reporting period;
31 (3) a summary of the supported decision making, technological
32 assistance, medical services, educational and vocational services and other
33 supports and services provided to the adult and the guardian's opinion as to
34 the adequacy of the adult's care;
35 (4) a summary of the guardian's visits with the adult, including the
36 frequency of the visits;
37 (5) action taken on behalf of the adult;
38 (6) the extent to which the adult has participated in decision making;
39 (7) if the adult is living in a mental health facility or living in a
40 facility that provides the adult with healthcare or other personal services,
41 whether the guardian considers the facility's current plan for support, care,
42 treatment or habilitation consistent with the adult's preferences, values,
43 prior directions and best interest;
HB 2359—Am. by HC 60
1 (8) anything of more than de minimis value which the guardian, any
2 individual who resides with the guardian, or the spouse, parent, child or
3 sibling of the guardian has received from an individual providing goods or
4 services to the adult;
5 (9) any circumstance that may constitute a conflict of interest
6 between the guardian and the adult. A conflict of interest occurs where the
7 guardian has some personal, business or agency interest that could be
8 perceived as self-serving or adverse to the position or best interest of the
9 adult, including, but not limited to, being paid for providing caregiver
10 services to the adult;
11 (10) if a guardian has been granted financial authority under section
12 78(c) 78(e), and amendments thereto, an accounting that lists property
13 included in the adult's estate and the receipts, disbursements, liabilities and

19 (12) plans for future care and support of the adult;
20 (13) a recommendation as to the need for continued guardianship and

22 whether the condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable
23 of exercising rights previously removed; and
24 (14) whether any co-guardian or successor guardian appointed to
25 serve when a designated event occurs is alive and able to serve.
26 (c) A guardian for an adult shall file a special report with the court
27 upon the occurrence of any of the following:
28 (1) A change of address of the guardian;
29 (2) a change of residence or placement of the adult;
30 (3) a significant change in the health or impairment of the adult;
31 (4) the acquisition by the adult of any real property, or the receipt or
32 accumulation of other property or income by the adult or by the guardian
33 on behalf of the adult, which causes the total value of the adult's estate to
34 equal or exceed $25,000;
35 (5) the death of the adult; or
36 (6) a change in the circumstances of the guardian or the adult that
37 may constitute a conflict of interest. A conflict of interest occurs where the
38 guardian has some personal, business or agency interest that could be
39 perceived as self-serving or adverse to the position or best interest of the
40 adult.
41 (d) The court may appoint a court liaison to review a report submitted

HB 2359—Am. by HC 61
1 guardianship or investigate any other matter involving the guardianship.
2 (e) Notice of the filing under this section of a guardian's report or

4 adult subject to guardianship, a person entitled to notice under section
5 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other
6 person the court determines. The notice and report must be given not later
7 than 14 days after the filing.
8 (f) The court shall establish procedures for monitoring a report
9 submitted under this section and review each report at least annually to
10 determine whether:
11 (1) The report provides sufficient information to establish the
12 guardian has complied with the guardian's duties;
13 (2) the guardianship should continue; and
14 (3) the guardian's requested fees, if any, should be approved.
15 (g) If the court determines that there is reason to believe a guardian
16 for an adult has not complied with the guardian's duties or the
17 guardianship should be modified or terminated, the court:
18 (1) Shall notify the adult, the guardian and any other person entitled
19 to notice under section 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent
20 order;
21 (2) may require additional information from the guardian;
22 (3) may appoint a court liaison to interview the adult or guardian or
23 investigate any matter involving the guardianship; and
24 (4) consistent with sections 81 and 82, and amendments thereto, may
25 hold a hearing to consider removal of the guardian, termination of the
26 guardianship or a change in the powers granted to the guardian or terms of
27 the guardianship.
28 (h) If the court has reason to believe fees requested by a guardian for
29 an adult are not reasonable, the court shall hold a hearing to determine
30 whether to adjust the requested fees.
31 (i) A guardian for an adult may petition the court for approval of a
32 report filed under this section. The court after review may approve the
33 report. If the court approves the report, there is a rebuttable presumption
34 the report is accurate as to a matter adequately disclosed in the report.
35 New Sec. 81. (a) The court may remove a guardian for an adult for
36 failure to perform the guardian's duties or for other good cause and appoint
37 a successor guardian to assume the duties of guardian.
38 (b) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether to remove a
39 guardian for an adult and appoint a successor guardian on:
40 (1) Petition of the adult, guardian or person interested in the welfare
41 of the adult, which contains allegations that, if true, would support a
42 reasonable belief that removal of the guardian and appointment of a
43 successor guardian may be appropriate, but the court may decline to hold a
HB 2359—Am. by HC 62
1 hearing if a petition based on the same or substantially similar facts was
2 filed during the preceding six months;
3 (2) communication from the adult, guardian or person interested in
4 the welfare of the adult which supports a reasonable belief that removal of
5 the guardian and appointment of a successor guardian may be appropriate;
6 (3) determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
7 interest of the adult; or
8 (4) determination by the court that the guardian's annual reports are
9 delinquent or deficient as filed.
10 (c) Notice of a petition under subsection (b)(1) or a hearing under this
11 section must be given to the adult subject to guardianship, the guardian, a
12 person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a
13 subsequent order, and any other person the court determines.
14 (d) If the adult subject to guardianship is not represented by an
15 attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the same conditions as
16 in section 68, and amendments thereto. The court shall award reasonable
17 attorney fees to the attorney for the adult as provided in section 42, and
18 amendments thereto.
19 (e) In selecting a successor guardian for an adult, the court shall
20 follow the priorities under section 72, and amendments thereto.
21 (f) Not later than 30 days after appointing a successor guardian, the
22 court or the court's designee shall give notice of the appointment to the
23 adult subject to guardianship and any person entitled to notice under
24 section 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
25 New Sec. 82. (a) An adult subject to guardianship, the guardian for
26 the adult or a person interested in the welfare of the adult may petition for:
27 (1) Termination of the guardianship on the ground that a basis for
28 appointment under section 64, and amendments thereto, does not exist or
29 termination would be in the best interest of the adult or for other good
30 cause; or
31 (2) modification of the guardianship on the ground that the extent of
32 protection or assistance granted is not appropriate or for other good cause.
33 (b) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether termination
34 or modification of a guardianship for an adult is appropriate on:
35 (1) Petition under subsection (a) which contains allegations that, if
36 true, would support a reasonable belief that termination or modification of
37 the guardianship may be appropriate, but the court may decline to hold a
38 hearing if a petition based on the same or substantially similar facts was
39 filed during the preceding six months;
40 (2) communication from the adult, guardian or person interested in
41 the welfare of the adult which supports a reasonable belief that termination
42 or modification of the guardianship may be appropriate, including because
43 the functional needs of the adult or supports or services available to the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 63
1 adult have changed;
2 (3) a report from a guardian or conservator which indicates that
3 termination or modification may be appropriate because the functional
4 needs of the adult or supports or services available to the adult have
5 changed or a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or other less
6 restrictive alternative for meeting the adult's needs is available; or
7 (4) a determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
8 interest of the adult.
9 (c) Notice of a petition under subsection (b)(1) or of a hearing under
10 this section must be given to the adult subject to guardianship, the
11 guardian, a person entitled to notice under section 73(e), and amendments
12 thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court determines.
13 (d) After the hearing, the court shall order termination unless it is
14 proven that a basis for appointment of a guardian under section 64, and
15 amendments thereto, continues to exist.
16 (e) The court shall modify the powers granted to a guardian for an
17 adult if the powers are excessive or inadequate due to a change in the
18 abilities or limitations of the adult, the adult's supports or other
19 circumstances.
20 (f) Unless the court otherwise orders for good cause, before
21 terminating or modifying a guardianship for an adult, the court shall
22 follow the same procedures to safeguard the rights of the adult which
23 apply to a petition for guardianship.
24 (g) An adult subject to guardianship who seeks to terminate or
25 modify the terms of the guardianship has the right to choose an attorney to
26 represent the adult in the matter. If the adult is not represented by an
27 attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the same conditions as
28 in section 68, and amendments thereto. The court shall award reasonable
29 attorney fees to the attorney for the adult as provided in section 42, and
30 amendments thereto.
31 (h) Not later than 30 days after entering an order under this section,
32 the court or the court's designee shall give notice of the order to the adult
33 subject to guardianship and any person entitled to notice under section
34 73(e), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
35 New Sec. 83. (a) On petition and after notice and hearing, the court
36 may appoint a conservator for the property or financial affairs of a minor if
37 the court finds by a preponderance of evidence that the minor owns funds
38 or other property exceeding $25,000 in value derived from court
39 settlements, death transfers or sources other than the minor's employment
40 earnings or accounts established under the uniform transfers to minors act,
41 and either:
42 (1) The minor owns funds or other property requiring management or
43 protection that otherwise cannot be provided;
HB 2359—Am. by HC 64
1 (2) the minor has or may have financial affairs that may be put at
2 unreasonable risk or hindered because of the minor's age; or
3 (3) appointment is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide funds
4 or other property needed for the support, care, education, health or welfare
5 of the minor.
6 (b) On petition and after notice and hearing, the court may appoint a
7 conservator for the property or financial affairs of an adult if the court
8 finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
9 (1) The adult is unable to manage property or financial affairs
10 because:
11 (A) Of a limitation in the adult's ability to receive and evaluate
12 information or make or communicate decisions, even with the use of
13 appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported
14 decision making; or
15 (B) the adult is missing, detained or unable to return to the United
16 States;
17 (2) appointment is necessary to:
18 (A) Avoid harm to the adult or significant dissipation of the property
19 of the adult; or
20 (B) obtain or provide funds or other property needed for the support,
21 care, education, health or welfare of the adult or of an individual entitled to
22 the adult's support; and
23 (3) the adult's identified needs cannot be met by a protective
24 arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive alternative.
25 (c) The court shall grant a conservator only those powers necessitated
26 by demonstrated limitations and needs of the adult and issue orders that
27 will encourage development of the adult's maximum self-determination
28 and independence. The court may not establish a full conservatorship if a
29 limited conservatorship, protective arrangement instead of conservatorship
30 or other less restrictive alternative would meet the needs of the adult.

HB 2359—Am. by HC 67
1 respondent of the respondent's rights at the hearing, including the right to

33 New Sec. 87. (a) If the respondent in a proceeding to appoint a

6 New Sec. 89. (a) Upon the filing of the petition or any other time at
7 or before the hearing, if the contents of the petition or evidence at the
8 hearing support a prima facie case of the need for a conservator, the court
9 shall order an examination and evaluation of the respondent to be
10 conducted through a general hospital, psychiatric hospital, community
11 mental health center or community developmental disability organization,
12 or by a licensed physician, psychiatrist, psychologist, physician assistant,
13 nurse practitioner, social worker or other professional appointed by the
14 court who is qualified to evaluate the respondent's alleged cognitive and
15 functional abilities and limitations and will not be advantaged or
16 disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition or otherwise have a
17 conflict of interest.

19 examination and evaluation submitted to the court shall contain:

22 (3) a description of the nature and extent of the respondent's cognitive
23 and functional abilities and limitations, including adaptive behaviors and
24 social skills, and, as appropriate, educational and developmental potential;
25 (4) a prognosis for any improvement and, as appropriate, any
26 recommendation for treatment or rehabilitation;

28 examinations of the respondent, including the dates thereof, which were
29 relied upon in the preparation of this evaluation;

31 occurred, and the name or names of the professional or professionals
32 performing the examination and evaluation and such professional's
33 qualifications;
34 (7) a statement by the professional that the professional has
35 personally completed an independent examination and evaluation of the
36 respondent, and that the report submitted to the court contains the results

38 regard to the issues of whether or not the respondent is in need of a
39 conservator and whether there are barriers to the respondent's attendance
40 and participation at the hearing on the petition; and

1 examination and evaluation ordered by the court. The report shall be made

17 New Sec. 90. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (b), a
18 hearing under section 85, and amendments thereto, may not proceed unless
19 the respondent attends the hearing. If it is not reasonably feasible for the
20 respondent to attend a hearing at the location court proceedings typically
21 are held, the court shall make reasonable efforts to hold the hearing at an
22 alternative location convenient to the respondent or allow the respondent
23 to attend the hearing using real-time audio-visual technology.

26 and convincing evidence that:
27 (1) The respondent is choosing not to attend the hearing after having
28 been fully informed of the right to attend and the potential consequences
29 of failing to do so;
30 (2) there is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and
31 participate in the hearing even with appropriate supportive services or
32 technological assistance; or
33 (3) the respondent is a minor who has received proper notice and
34 attendance would be harmful to the minor.
35 (c) The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under section 85, and
36 amendments thereto, by a person or persons of the respondent's choosing,
37 assistive technology or an interpreter or translator, or a combination of
38 these supports. If assistance would facilitate the respondent's participation
39 in the hearing, but is not otherwise available to the respondent, the court
40 shall make reasonable efforts to provide it.

40 thereto, or a subsequent order; and

HB 2359—Am. by HC 73
1 access to court records of the conservatorship, including the conservator's
2 plan and report. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest

19 New Sec. 92. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c), the
20 court in appointing a conservator shall consider persons qualified to be a
21 conservator in the following order of priority:
22 (1) A conservator, other than a temporary or emergency conservator,
23 currently acting for the respondent in another jurisdiction;
24 (2) a person nominated as conservator by the respondent, including
25 the respondent's most recent nomination made in a power of attorney for
26 finances;
27 (3) an agent appointed by the respondent to manage the respondent's
28 property under a power of attorney for finances;
29 (4) a spouse of the respondent;
30 (5) a family member or other individual who has shown special care
31 and concern for the respondent; and
32 (6) a person nominated as conservator by the spouse, adult child or
33 other close family member of the respondent.
34 (b) If two or more persons have equal priority under subsection (a),
35 the court shall select as conservator the person the court considers best
36 qualified. In determining the best qualified person, the court shall consider
37 the person's relationship with the respondent, the person's skills, the
38 expressed wishes of the respondent, the extent to which the person and the
39 respondent have similar values and preferences and the likelihood the
40 person will be able to perform the duties of a conservator successfully.
41 (c) The court, acting in the best interest of the respondent, may
42 decline to appoint as conservator a person having priority under subsection
43 (a) and appoint a person having a lower priority or no priority.
HB 2359—Am. by HC 74
1 (d) The following persons shall not be appointed as conservator
2 unless the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that the person is
3 the best qualified person available for appointment and the appointment is
4 in the best interest of the respondent:
5 (1) A person that provides paid services to the respondent, or an
6 individual who is employed by a person that provides paid services to the
7 respondent, or is the spouse, parent or child of an individual who provides
8 or is employed to provide paid services to the respondent;
9 (2) an owner, operator or employee of any entity at which the
10 respondent is receiving care; and
11 (3) a person who provides care or other services, or is an employee of
12 an agency, partnership or corporation that provides care or other services
13 to persons with needs similar to those of the respondent.
14 New Sec. 93. (a) A court order appointing a conservator for a minor
15 must include findings to support appointment of a conservator.
16 (b) A court order appointing a conservator for an adult must:
17 (1) Include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence has
18 established that the identified needs of the respondent cannot be met by a
19 protective arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive
20 alternative, including use of appropriate supportive services, technological
21 assistance or supported decision making; and
22 (2) include a specific finding that clear and convincing evidence
23 established the respondent was given proper notice of the hearing on the
24 petition.
25 (c) A court order establishing a full conservatorship for an adult must
26 state the basis for granting a full conservatorship and include specific
27 findings to support the conclusion that a limited conservatorship would not
28 meet the functional needs of the adult.
29 (d) A court order establishing a limited conservatorship must state the
30 specific property placed under the control of the conservator and the
31 powers granted to the conservator.
32 (e) A court order appointing a conservator must include the date of a
33 review hearing to be set 90 days after the order of appointment is entered.
34 At that hearing, the court shall review the conservator's plan filed pursuant
35 to section 103, and amendments thereto, and the inventory filed pursuant
36 to section 104, and amendments thereto.
37 (f) The court, as part of an order establishing a conservatorship, shall
38 identify any person that subsequently is entitled to:
39 (1) Notice of the rights of the individual subject to conservatorship
40 under section 94(b), and amendments thereto;
41 (2) notice of a sale or other disposition of, encumbrance of an interest
42 in, or surrender of a lease to any real or personal property of the
43 individual;
HB 2359—Am. by HC 75
1 (3) notice that the conservator will be unavailable to perform the
2 conservator's duties for more than one month;
3 (4) a copy of the conservator's plan under section 103, and
4 amendments thereto, and the conservator's report under section 105, and
5 amendments thereto;
6 (5) access to court records relating to the conservatorship;
7 (6) notice of a transaction involving a substantial conflict between the
8 conservator's fiduciary duties and personal interests;
9 (7) notice of the death or significant change in the condition of the
10 individual;
11 (8) notice that a petition has been filed to limit or modify the powers
12 of the conservator or that the court has limited or modified the powers of
13 the conservator; and
14 (9) notice that a petition has been filed to remove the conservator or
15 that the court has removed the conservator.
16 (g) If an individual subject to conservatorship is an adult, the spouse
17 and adult children of the adult subject to conservatorship are entitled under
18 subsection (e) to notice unless the court determines notice would be
19 contrary to the preferences or prior directions of the adult subject to
20 conservatorship or not in the best interest of the adult.
21 (h) If an individual subject to conservatorship is a minor, each parent
22 and adult sibling of the minor is entitled under subsection (e) to notice
23 unless the court determines notice would not be in the best interest of the
24 minor.
25 New Sec. 94. (a) Not later than 14 days after the appointment, a
26 conservator appointed under section 93, and amendments thereto, shall
27 give to the individual subject to conservatorship and to all other persons
28 given notice under section 85, and amendments thereto, a copy of the
29 order of appointment.
30 (b) Not later than 30 days after appointment of a conservator under
31 section 93, and amendments thereto, the court or the court's designee shall
32 give to the individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator, and any
33 other person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and amendments
34 thereto, a statement of the rights of the individual subject to
35 conservatorship and procedures to seek relief if the individual is denied
36 those rights. The statement must be in plain language, in at least 16-point
37 font, and to the extent feasible, in a language in which the individual
38 subject to conservatorship is proficient. The statement must notify the
39 individual subject to conservatorship of the right to:
40 (1) Seek termination or modification of the conservatorship, or
41 removal of the conservator, and choose an attorney to represent the
42 individual in these matters;
43 (2) file a grievance against the conservator under section 50, and
HB 2359—Am. by HC 76
1 amendments thereto;
2 (3) participate in decision making to the extent reasonably feasible;
3 (4) receive a copy of the conservator's plan under section 103, and
4 amendments thereto, the conservator's inventory under section 104, and
5 amendments thereto, and the conservator's report under section 105, and
6 amendments thereto; and
7 (5) object to the conservator's inventory, plan or report.
8 (c) If a conservator is appointed for the reasons stated in section 83(b)
9 (1)(B), and amendments thereto, and the individual subject to
10 conservatorship is missing, notice under this section to the individual is
11 not required. If the individual subject to conservatorship is a minor under
12 the age of 12, notice under this section to the minor is not required.
13 (d) Any person required to provide notice under this section shall file
14 proof of service of such notice with the court.
15 New Sec. 95. (a) On its own after a petition has been filed under
16 section 84, and amendments thereto, or on a verified petition by a person
17 interested in an individual's welfare, the court may appoint an emergency
18 conservator for the individual if the court finds a sufficient factual basis to
19 establish probable cause that:
20 (1) Appointment of an emergency conservator is necessary to prevent
21 imminent, substantial and irreparable harm to the individual's property or
22 financial interests;
23 (2) no other person has authority and willingness to act in the
24 circumstances; and
25 (3) a basis for appointment of a conservator under section 83, and
26 amendments thereto, exists.
27 (b) The duration of authority of an emergency conservator may not
28 exceed 30 days and the emergency conservator may exercise only the
29 powers specified in the order of appointment. The emergency conservator's
30 authority may be extended up to three times for not more than 30 days per
31 extension if the court finds good cause and that the conditions for
32 appointment of an emergency conservator under subsection (a) continue.
33 (c) Immediately on filing of a petition for an emergency conservator,
34 the court shall appoint an attorney to represent the respondent in the
35 proceeding. Except as otherwise provided in subsection (d), reasonable
36 notice of the date, time and place of a hearing on the petition must be
37 given to the respondent, the respondent's attorney and any other person the
38 court determines.
39 (d) The court may appoint an emergency conservator without notice
40 to the respondent and any attorney for the respondent only if the court
41 finds from an affidavit or testimony that the respondent's property or
42 financial interests will be substantially and irreparably harmed before a
43 hearing with notice on the appointment can be held. If the court appoints
HB 2359—Am. by HC 77
1 an emergency conservator without giving notice under subsection (c), the
2 court must give notice of the appointment not later than 48 hours after the
3 appointment to:
4 (1) The respondent;
5 (2) the respondent's attorney; and
6 (3) any other person the court determines.
7 (e) Not later than five days after the appointment, the court shall hold
8 a hearing on the appropriateness of the appointment.
9 (f) Appointment of an emergency conservator under this section is
10 not a determination that a basis exists for appointment of a conservator
11 under section 83, and amendments thereto.
12 (g) The court may remove an emergency conservator appointed under
13 this section at any time. The emergency conservator shall make any report
14 the court requires.
15 New Sec. 96. An individual subject to conservatorship or a person
16 interested in the welfare of the individual may petition for an order:
17 (a) Modifying bond requirements;
18 (b) requiring an accounting for the administration of the
19 conservatorship estate;
20 (c) directing distribution;
21 (d) removing the conservator and appointing a temporary or
22 successor conservator;
23 (e) modifying the type of appointment or powers granted to the
24 conservator, if the extent of protection or management previously granted
25 is excessive or insufficient to meet the individual's needs, including
26 because the individual's abilities or supports have changed;
27 (f) rejecting or modifying the conservator's plan under section 103,
28 and amendments thereto, the conservator's inventory under section 104,
29 and amendments thereto, or the conservator's report under section 105, and
30 amendments thereto; or
31 (g) granting other appropriate relief.
32 New Sec. 97. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c), the
33 court shall require a conservator to furnish a bond with a surety, or require
34 an alternative asset-protection arrangement, conditioned on faithful
35 discharge of all duties of the conservator. The court may waive the
36 requirement only if the court finds that a bond or other asset-protection
37 arrangement is not necessary to protect the interests of the individual
38 subject to conservatorship. Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c),
39 the court may not waive the requirement if the conservator is in the
40 business of serving as a conservator and is being paid for the conservator's
41 service.
42 (b) Unless the court directs otherwise, the bond required under this
43 section must be in the amount of the aggregate capital value of the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 78
1 conservatorship estate, plus one year's estimated income, less the value of
2 property deposited under an arrangement requiring a court order for its
3 removal, and less the value of real property. The court, in place of surety
4 on a bond, may accept collateral for the performance of the bond,
5 including a pledge of securities or a mortgage of real property.
6 (c) A regulated financial-service institution qualified to do trust
7 business in this state is not required to give a bond under this section.
8 (d) If the conservator appointed is under contract with the Kansas
9 guardianship program, the Kansas department for children and families
10 shall act as surety on the bond.
11 New Sec. 98. (a) The following rules apply to the bond required
12 under section 97, and amendments thereto:
13 (1) Except as otherwise provided by the bond, the surety and the
14 conservator are jointly and severally liable.
15 (2) By executing a bond provided by a conservator, the surety
16 submits to the personal jurisdiction of the court that issued letters of office
17 to the conservator in a proceeding relating to the duties of the conservator
18 in which the surety is named as a party. Notice of the proceeding must be
19 given to the surety at the address shown in the records of the court in
20 which the bond is filed and any other address of the surety then known to
21 the person required to provide the notice.
22 (3) On petition of a successor conservator or person affected by a
23 breach of the obligation of the bond, a proceeding may be brought against
24 the surety for breach of the obligation of the bond.
25 (4) A proceeding against the bond may be brought until liability
26 under the bond is exhausted.
27 (b) A proceeding may not be brought under this section against a
28 surety of a bond on a matter as to which a proceeding against the
29 conservator is barred.
30 (c) If a bond under section 97, and amendments thereto, is not
31 renewed by the conservator, the surety or sureties immediately shall give
32 notice to the court and the individual subject to conservatorship. Upon
33 receiving such notice, the clerk of the district court shall forward the notice
34 to the presiding judge who shall set the matter for hearing and determine
35 who should receive notice.
36 New Sec. 99. (a) A conservator is a fiduciary and has duties of
37 prudence, loyalty, reasonable care and diligence to the individual subject to
38 conservatorship.
39 (b) A conservator shall promote the self-determination of the
40 individual subject to conservatorship and, to the extent feasible, encourage
41 the individual to participate in decisions, act on the individual's own
42 behalf, and develop or regain the capacity to manage the individual's
43 personal affairs. A conservator shall strive to assure that the personal, civil
HB 2359—Am. by HC 79
1 and human rights of the individual subject to conservatorship are
2 protected.
3 (c) In making a decision for an individual subject to conservatorship,
4 the conservator shall make the decision that the conservator reasonably
5 believes the individual would make if able, unless doing so would fail to
6 preserve the resources needed to maintain the individual's well-being and
7 lifestyle or otherwise unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or
8 personal or financial interests of the individual. To determine the decision
9 the individual would make if able, the conservator shall consider the
10 individual's prior or current directions, preferences, opinions, values and
11 actions, to the extent actually known or reasonably ascertainable by the
12 conservator.
13 (d) If a conservator cannot make a decision under subsection (c)
14 because the conservator does not know and cannot reasonably determine
15 the decision the individual subject to conservatorship probably would
16 make if able, or the conservator reasonably believes the decision the
17 individual would make would fail to preserve resources needed to
18 maintain the individual's well-being and lifestyle or otherwise
19 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
20 interests of the individual, the conservator shall act in accordance with the
21 best interest of the individual. In determining the best interest of the
22 individual, the conservator shall consider:
23 (1) Information received from professionals and persons that
24 demonstrate sufficient interest in the welfare of the individual;
25 (2) other information the conservator believes the individual would
26 have considered if the individual were able to act; and
27 (3) other factors a reasonable person in the circumstances of the
28 individual would consider, including consequences for others.
29 (e) Except when inconsistent with the conservator's duties under
30 subsections (a) through (d), a conservator shall invest and manage the
31 conservatorship estate as a prudent investor would, by considering:
32 (1) The circumstances of the individual subject to conservatorship
33 and the conservatorship estate;
34 (2) general economic conditions;
35 (3) the possible effect of inflation or deflation;
36 (4) the expected tax consequences of an investment decision or
37 strategy;
38 (5) the role of each investment or course of action in relation to the
39 conservatorship estate as a whole;
40 (6) the expected total return from income and appreciation of capital;
41 (7) the need for liquidity, regularity of income and preservation or
42 appreciation of capital; and
43 (8) the special relationship or value, if any, of specific property to the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 80
1 individual subject to conservatorship.
2 (f) The propriety of a conservator's investment and management of
3 the conservatorship estate is determined in light of the facts and
4 circumstances existing when the conservator decides or acts and not by
5 hindsight.
6 (g) A conservator shall make a reasonable effort to verify facts
7 relevant to the investment and management of the conservatorship estate.
8 (h) A conservator that has special skills or expertise, or is named
9 conservator in reliance on the conservator's representation of special skills
10 or expertise, has a duty to use the special skills or expertise in carrying out
11 the conservator's duties.
12 (i) In investing, selecting specific property for distribution, and
13 invoking a power of revocation or withdrawal for the use or benefit of the
14 individual subject to conservatorship, a conservator shall consider any
15 estate plan of the individual known or reasonably ascertainable to the
16 conservator and may examine the will or other donative, nominative or
17 appointive instrument of the individual.
18 (j) A conservator shall maintain insurance on the insurable real and
19 personal property of the individual subject to conservatorship, unless the
20 conservatorship estate lacks sufficient funds to pay for insurance or the
21 court finds:
22 (1) The property lacks sufficient equity; or
23 (2) insuring the property would unreasonably dissipate the
24 conservatorship estate or otherwise not be in the best interest of the
25 individual.
26 (k) A conservator has access to and authority over a digital asset of
27 the individual subject to conservatorship to the extent provided by the
28 revised uniform fiduciary access to digital assets act or court order.
29 (l) A conservator for an adult shall notify the court immediately if the
30 condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable of exercising
31 rights previously removed.

35 granted in this section.

17 New Sec. 103. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment, and
18 whenever there is a significant change in circumstances or the conservator
19 seeks to deviate significantly from the existing conservator's plan, a
20 conservator shall file with the court a plan for protecting, managing,
21 expending and distributing the assets of the conservatorship estate. The
22 plan must be based on the needs of the individual subject to
23 conservatorship and take into account the best interest of the individual as
24 well as the individual's preferences, values and prior directions, to the
25 extent known to or reasonably ascertainable by the conservator. The
26 conservator shall include in the plan:
27 (1) A budget containing projected expenses and resources, including
28 an estimate of the total amount of fees the conservator anticipates charging
29 per year and a statement or list of the amount the conservator proposes to
30 charge for each service the conservator anticipates providing to the
31 individual;
32 (2) how the conservator will involve the individual in decisions about
33 management of the conservatorship estate;
34 (3) any step the conservator plans to take to develop or restore the
35 ability of the individual to manage the conservatorship estate; and
36 (4) an estimate of the duration of the conservatorship.
37 (b) A conservator shall give notice of the filing of the conservator's
38 plan under subsection (a), together with a copy of the plan, to the
39 individual subject to conservatorship, any attorney representing the
40 individual subject to conservatorship, a person entitled to notice under
41 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any
42 other person the court determines. The notice must include a statement of
43 the right to object to the plan and must be given at the time of the filing.
HB 2359—Am. by HC 86
1 (c) An individual subject to conservatorship and any person entitled
2 under subsection (b) to receive notice and a copy of the conservator's plan
3 may object to the plan in writing not later than 21 days after the filing.
4 (d) The court shall review the conservator's plan filed under
5 subsection (a) and determine whether to approve the plan or require a new
6 plan. In deciding whether to approve the plan, the court shall consider an
7 objection under subsection (c) and whether the plan is consistent with the
8 conservator's duties and powers. The court shall review an initial
9 conservator's plan at the review hearing scheduled under section 93(e), and
10 amendments thereto. For subsequent conservator's plans, the court has
11 discretion whether to set the matter for hearing but may not approve the

17 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
18 determines.
19 New Sec. 104. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment, a
20 conservator shall prepare and file with the appointing court a detailed
21 inventory of the conservatorship estate, together with an oath or
22 affirmation that the inventory is believed to be complete and accurate as
23 far as information permits. The inventory shall include all of the property
24 and assets of the conservatorship estate, including any sources of regular
25 income to the estate, and information about how property is titled and any
26 beneficiary designations, including pay-on-death and transfer-on-death
27 beneficiaries.

29 individual subject to conservatorship, a person entitled to notice under
30 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any
31 other person the court determines. The notice must be given not later than
32 14 days after the filing.
33 (c) A conservator shall keep records of the administration of the
34 conservatorship estate and make them available for examination on
35 reasonable request of the individual subject to conservatorship, a guardian
36 for the individual, or any other person the conservator or the court
37 determines.
38 New Sec. 105. (a) A conservator shall file with the court a report in a

1 estate and the receipts, disbursements, liabilities and distributions during

1 (3) the conservator's requested fees, if any, should be approved.
2 (f) If the court determines there is reason to believe a conservator has

31 New Sec. 106. (a) The interest of an individual subject to
32 conservatorship in property included in the conservatorship estate is not
33 transferrable or assignable by the individual and is not subject to levy,
34 garnishment, or similar process for claims against the individual unless
35 allowed under section 110, and amendments thereto.
36 (b) If an individual subject to conservatorship enters into a contract
37 after having the right to enter the contract removed by the court, the
38 contract is void against the individual and the individual's property but is
39 enforceable against the person that contracted with the individual.
40 (c) A person other than the conservator that deals with an individual
41 subject to conservatorship with respect to property included in the
42 conservatorship estate is entitled to protection provided by law of this state
43 other than this act.

1 New Sec. 107. A transaction involving a conservatorship estate which
2 is affected by a substantial conflict between the conservator's fiduciary
3 duties and personal interests is voidable unless the transaction is
4 authorized by court order after notice to persons entitled to notice under
5 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order. A
6 transaction affected by a substantial conflict includes a sale, encumbrance
7 or other transaction involving the conservatorship estate entered into by
8 the conservator, an individual with whom the conservator resides, the
9 spouse, descendant, sibling, agent or attorney of the conservator, or a
10 corporation or other enterprise in which the conservator has a substantial
11 beneficial interest.
12 New Sec. 108. (a) A person that assists or deals with a conservator in
13 good faith and for value in any transaction, other than a transaction
14 requiring a court order under section 102, and amendments thereto, is
15 protected as though the conservator properly exercised any power in
16 question. Knowledge alone by a person that the person is dealing with a
17 conservator does not require the person to inquire into the existence of
18 authority of the conservator or the propriety of the conservator's exercise
19 of authority, but restrictions on authority stated in letters of office, or
20 otherwise provided by law, are effective as to the person. A person that
21 pays or delivers property to a conservator is not responsible for proper
22 application of the property.
23 (b) Protection under subsection (a) extends to a procedural
24 irregularity or jurisdictional defect in the proceeding leading to the
25 issuance of letters of office and does not substitute for protection for a
26 person that assists or deals with a conservator provided by comparable
27 provisions in law of this state other than this act relating to a commercial
28 transaction or simplifying a transfer of securities by a fiduciary.
29 New Sec. 109. (a) If an individual subject to conservatorship dies, the
30 conservator shall deliver to the district court any will of the individual that
31 is in the conservator's possession and inform the personal representative
32 named in the will if feasible. The conservator shall give notice of the
33 delivery of the will under this section to any person entitled to notice under
34 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
35 (b) On the death of an individual subject to conservatorship, the
36 conservator shall conclude the administration of the conservatorship estate
37 as provided in section 113, and amendments thereto.
38 New Sec. 110. (a) A conservator may pay a claim against the
39 conservatorship estate or the individual subject to conservatorship arising
40 before or during the conservatorship, on presentation and allowance in
41 accordance with the priorities under subsection (d). A claimant may
42 present a claim by:
43 (1) Sending or delivering to the conservator a statement in a record of
HB 2359—Am. by HC 90
1 the claim, indicating its basis, the name and address of the claimant and
2 the amount claimed; or
3 (2) filing the claim with the court, in a form acceptable to the court,
4 and sending or delivering a copy of the claim to the conservator.
5 (b) A claim under subsection (a) is presented on receipt by the
6 conservator of the statement of the claim or the filing with the court of the
7 claim, whichever occurs first. A presented claim is allowed, if it is not
8 disallowed in whole or in part, by the conservator in a record sent or
9 delivered to the claimant not later than 60 days after its presentation.
10 Before payment, the conservator may change an allowance of the claim to
11 a disallowance in whole or in part, but not after allowance under a court
12 order or order directing payment of the claim. Presentation of a claim tolls
13 until 30 days after disallowance of the claim the running of a statute of
14 limitations that has not expired relating to the claim.
15 (c) A claimant whose claim under subsection (a) has not been paid
16 may petition the court to determine the claim at any time before it is barred
17 by a statute of limitations, and the court may order its allowance, payment
18 or security by encumbering property included in the conservatorship
19 estate. If a proceeding is pending against the individual subject to
20 conservatorship at the time of appointment of the conservator or is
21 initiated thereafter, the moving party shall give the conservator notice of
22 the proceeding if it could result in creating a claim against the
23 conservatorship estate.
24 (d) If a conservatorship estate is likely to be exhausted before all
25 existing claims are paid, the conservator shall distribute the estate in
26 money or in kind in payment of claims in the following order:
27 (1) Costs and expenses of administration;
28 (2) a claim of the federal or state government having priority under
29 law other than this act;
30 (3) a claim incurred by the conservator for support, care, education,
31 health or welfare previously provided to the individual subject to
32 conservatorship or an individual who is in fact dependent on the individual
33 subject to conservatorship;
34 (4) a claim arising before the conservatorship; and
35 (5) all other claims.
36 (e) Preference may not be given in the payment of a claim under
37 subsection (d) over another claim of the same class. A claim due and
38 payable may not be preferred over a claim not due unless:
39 (1) Doing so would leave the conservatorship estate without
40 sufficient funds to pay the basic living and healthcare expenses of the
41 individual subject to conservatorship; and
42 (2) the court authorizes the preference under section 102(a)(8), and
43 amendments thereto.
