6 New Sec. 111. (a) Except as otherwise agreed by a conservator, the
7 conservator is not personally liable on a contract properly entered into in a
8 fiduciary capacity in the course of administration of the conservatorship
9 estate unless the conservator fails to reveal the conservator's representative
10 capacity in the contract or before entering into the contract.
11 (b) A conservator is personally liable for an obligation arising from
12 control of property of the conservatorship estate or an act or omission
13 occurring in the course of administration of the conservatorship estate only
14 if the conservator is personally at fault.
15 (c) A claim based on a contract entered into by a conservator in a
16 fiduciary capacity, an obligation arising from control of property included
17 in the conservatorship estate, or a tort committed in the course of
18 administration of the conservatorship estate may be asserted against the
19 conservatorship estate in a proceeding against the conservator in a
20 fiduciary capacity, whether or not the conservator is personally liable for
21 the claim.
22 (d) A question of liability between a conservatorship estate and the
23 conservator personally may be determined in a proceeding for accounting,
24 surcharge, or indemnification or another appropriate proceeding or action.
25 New Sec. 112. (a) The court may remove a conservator for failure to

27 successor conservator to assume the duties of the conservator.

32 allegations that, if true, would support a reasonable belief that removal of
33 the conservator and appointment of a successor may be appropriate, but
34 the court may decline to hold a hearing if a petition based on the same or
35 substantially similar facts was filed during the preceding six months;
36 (2) communication from the individual subject to conservatorship,
37 conservator or person interested in the welfare of the individual which
38 supports a reasonable belief that removal of the conservator and
39 appointment of a successor may be appropriate;
40 (3) determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
41 interest of the individual subject to conservatorship; or
42 (4) determination by the court that the conservator's reports and
43 accountings are delinquent or deficient as filed.

17 New Sec. 113. (a) A conservatorship for a minor terminates on the

12 New Sec. 114. (a) A conservatorship for a minor may be extended
13 beyond the minor's 18th birthday if the minor consents or the court finds by
14 clear and convincing evidence that substantial harm to the minor's interests
15 is otherwise likely. A conservatorship may be extended under this section
16 until the minor reaches the age of 21 and may be extended for two
17 additional two-year periods upon the same finding by the court or upon
18 consent of the minor. Consent to the extension of a conservatorship may be
19 withdrawn at any time.
20 (b) Any request to extend a minor conservatorship under this section
21 must be accompanied by:
22 (1) A description of the funds or assets of the minor's estate which the
23 conservator proposes to distribute to the minor over an extended period
24 following the minor's 18th birthday;
25 (2) the factual basis upon which the conservator alleges the need for
26 such an extended distribution plan; and
27 (3) a proposed conservator's plan that describes how the distribution
28 will occur.
29 (c) The court shall appoint an attorney to represent the minor as
30 provided in section 88, and amendments thereto.
31 (d) After a hearing, the court may extend a conservatorship for a
32 minor and grant to the conservator the authority to establish an extended
33 distribution plan if the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
34 (1) Substantial harm to the minor's interests is likely if the
35 conservatorship is not extended; and
36 (2) the plan approved by the court adequately provides for meeting
37 the expected needs of the minor from the minor's 18th birthday until the
38 final distribution of the funds or assets which the court authorizes to be set
39 aside or transferred from the estate are paid over to the minor, including
40 provisions for accelerated distribution in extraordinary circumstances,
41 which may require court approval.
42 (e) If the court orders a conservatorship for a minor to be extended
43 under this section, the court shall order the conservator to report any
HB 2359—Am. by HC 95
1 expenditure or transfer of funds or assets from the minor's estate for the
2 purposes of effectuating an extended distribution plan within the
3 conservator's next accounting.
4 (f) The court may extend the conservatorship with regard to specific
5 funds or assets of the minor's estate, even though other funds or assets of
6 the minor's estate are paid over to the minor upon the minor's becoming 18
7 years of age.
8 (g) The minor shall be without the power, voluntarily or involuntarily,
9 to sell, mortgage, pledge, hypothecate, assign, alienate, anticipate, transfer
10 or convey any interest in the principal or the income from any funds or
11 assets of the minor's estate set aside or transferred to effectuate a plan for
12 extended distribution until such is actually paid to the minor.
13 New Sec. 115. (a) Unless a person required to transfer funds or other
14 property to a minor knows that a conservator for the minor has been
15 appointed or a proceeding is pending for conservatorship, the person may
16 transfer an amount or value not exceeding $25,000 in a 12-month period
17 to:
18 (1) A person that has care or custody of the minor and with whom the
19 minor resides;
20 (2) a guardian for the minor;
21 (3) a custodian under the uniform transfers to minors act; or
22 (4) a financial institution as a deposit in an interest-bearing account or
23 certificate solely in the name of the minor and shall give notice to the
24 minor of the deposit.
25 (b) A person that transfers funds or other property under this section
26 is not responsible for its proper application.
27 (c) A person that receives funds or other property for a minor under
28 subsection (a)(1) or (2) may apply it only to the support, care, education,
29 health or welfare of the minor, and may not derive a personal financial
30 benefit from it, except for reimbursement for necessary expenses. Funds
31 not applied for these purposes must be preserved for the future support,
32 care, education, health or welfare of the minor, and the balance, if any,
33 transferred to the minor when the minor becomes an adult or otherwise is
34 emancipated.
35 (d) Any accumulated balance under this section shall be subject to
36 other provisions of this act.
37 New Sec. 116. The parent of a minor has the right and responsibility
38 to hold in trust and manage for the minor's benefit all of the personal and
39 real property vested in such minor when the total of such property does not
40 exceed $25,000 in value, unless a guardian or conservator has been
41 appointed for the minor.

2 New Sec. 120. (a) After the hearing on a petition under section 65,
3 and amendments thereto, for a guardianship or under section 119(b), and
4 amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship,
5 the court may issue an order under subsection (b) for a protective
6 arrangement instead of guardianship if the court finds by clear and
7 convincing evidence that:
8 (1) The respondent lacks the ability to meet essential requirements for
9 physical health, safety or self-care because the respondent is unable to
10 receive and evaluate information or make or communicate decisions, even
11 with appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported
12 decision making; and

14 restrictive alternative.

19 (A) A particular medical treatment or refusal of a particular medical

21 (B) a move to a specified place of dwelling; or
22 (C) visitation between the respondent and another person;
23 (2) order supervised visitation with, or restrict access to the
24 respondent by, a specified person whose access places the respondent at
25 serious risk of physical, psychological or financial harm; and
26 (3) order other arrangements on a limited basis that are appropriate.

21 best interest;
22 (2) either:
23 (A) The minor owns money or property requiring management or
24 protection that otherwise cannot be provided;
25 (B) the minor has or may have financial affairs that may be put at
26 unreasonable risk or hindered because of the minor's age; or
27 (C) the arrangement is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide
28 funds or other property needed for the support, care, education, health or
29 welfare of the minor; and
30 (3) the order under subsection (c) is necessary or desirable to obtain
31 or provide money needed for the support, care, education, health or
32 welfare of the minor.
33 (c) If the court makes the findings under subsection (a) or (b), the
34 court, instead of appointing a conservator, may:
35 (1) Authorize or direct a transaction necessary to protect the financial
36 interest or property of the respondent, including:
37 (A) An action to establish eligibility for benefits;
38 (B) payment, delivery, deposit or retention of funds or property;
39 (C) sale, mortgage, lease or other transfer of property;
40 (D) purchase of an annuity;
41 (E) entry into a contractual relationship, including a contract to
42 provide for personal care, supportive services, education, training or
43 employment;
HB 2359—Am. by HC 99
1 (F) addition to or establishment of a trust;
2 (G) ratification or invalidation of a contract, trust, will or other
3 transaction, including a transaction related to the property or business
4 affairs of the respondent; or
5 (H) settlement of a claim; or
6 (2) restrict access to the respondent's property by a specified person
7 whose access to the property places the respondent at serious risk of
8 financial harm.
9 (d) After the hearing on a petition under section 119(a)(2) or (c), and
10 amendments thereto, whether or not the court makes the findings under
11 subsection (a) or (b), the court may issue an order to restrict access to the
12 respondent or the respondent's property by a specified person that the court
13 finds by clear and convincing evidence:
14 (1) Through fraud, coercion, duress or the use of deception and
15 control caused or attempted to cause an action that would have resulted in
16 financial harm to the respondent or the respondent's property; and
17 (2) poses a serious risk of substantial financial harm to the respondent
18 or the respondent's property.
19 (e) Before issuing an order under subsection (c) or (d), the court shall
20 consider the factors under section 99, and amendments thereto, a
21 conservator must consider when making a decision on behalf of an
22 individual subject to conservatorship.
23 (f) Before issuing an order under subsection (c) or (d) for a
24 respondent who is a minor, the court also shall consider the best interest of
25 the minor, the preference of the parents of the minor and the preference of
26 the minor, if the minor is 12 years of age or older.
27 (g) Any order issued under this section may include reporting
28 requirements, time limits, bond requirements or any other provisions
29 deemed necessary by the court.
30 New Sec. 122. A verified petition for a protective arrangement
31 instead of guardianship or conservatorship must state the petitioner's name,

22 New Sec. 123. (a) On filing of a petition under section 119, and

24 on the petition.

30 consequences of granting the petition. The court may not grant the petition

33 notice upon the respondent:

HB 2359—Am. by HC 102
1 subsection does not preclude the court from granting the petition.

7 New Sec. 124. (a) On filing of a petition under section 119, and
8 amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship,
9 the court may appoint a court liaison. The court liaison must be an
10 individual with training or experience in the type of abilities, limitations
11 and needs alleged in the petition.
12 (b) On filing of a petition under section 119, and amendments thereto,
13 for a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship for a minor, the
14 court may appoint a court liaison to investigate a matter related to the
15 petition or inform the minor or a parent of the minor about the petition or a
16 related matter.
17 (c) On filing of a petition under section 119, and amendments thereto,
18 for a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship for an adult, the
19 court may appoint a court liaison. The court liaison must be an individual
20 with training or experience in the types of abilities, limitations and needs
21 alleged in the petition.
22 (d) A court liaison appointed under subsection (a) or (c) shall
23 interview the respondent in person and in a manner the respondent is best
24 able to understand:
25 (1) Explain, in general, the petition, and the nature and purpose of the
26 proceeding including the potential loss of rights as a result of the
27 proceeding;
28 (2) obtain the respondent's views with respect to the order sought;
29 (3) if the petitioner seeks an order related to the dwelling of the
30 respondent, visit the respondent's present dwelling and any dwelling in
31 which it is reasonably believed the respondent will live if the order is
32 granted;
33 (4) if a protective arrangement instead of guardianship is sought,
34 obtain information from any physician or other provider known to have
35 treated, advised or assessed the respondent's relevant physical or mental
36 condition, to the extent that such information has not already been
37 provided to the court;
38 (5) if a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is sought,
39 review financial records of the respondent, if relevant to the court liaison's
40 recommendation under subsection (e)(2); and
41 (6) investigate the allegations in the petition and any other matter
42 relating to the petition as directed by the court, including, but not limited
43 to, the respondent's family relationships, past conduct, the nature and
HB 2359—Am. by HC 103
1 extent of any property or income of the respondent, whether the
2 respondent is likely to injure self or others and other matters as the court
3 may specify.
4 (e) A court liaison under this section promptly shall file a report with
5 the court at least 10 days prior to the hearing on the petition or other
6 hearing as directed by the court. Unless otherwise ordered by the court,
7 such report must include:
8 (1) To the extent relevant to the order sought, a summary of self-care,
9 independent-living tasks and financial-management tasks the respondent:
10 (A) Can manage without assistance or with existing supports;
11 (B) could manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive
12 services, technological assistance or supported decision making; and
13 (C) cannot manage;
14 (2) a recommendation regarding the appropriateness of the protective
15 arrangement sought and whether a less restrictive alternative for meeting
16 the respondent's needs is available;
17 (3) if the petition seeks to change the physical location of the

20 preference as to the respondent's dwelling;

23 (5) a statement whether the respondent is able to participate in a

29 New Sec. 125. (a) Unless the respondent in a proceeding under

36 representation.

43 advocate for the result that is the least restrictive alternative in type,

1 duration and scope, consistent with the respondent's interests.

21 New Sec. 126. (a) Upon the filing of the petition or any other time at
22 or before the hearing, if the contents of the petition or evidence at the
23 hearing support a prima facie case of the need for a protective
24 arrangement, the court shall order an examination and evaluation of the
25 respondent to be conducted through a general hospital, psychiatric
26 hospital, community mental health center, or community developmental
27 disability organization, or by a licensed physician, psychiatrist,
28 psychologist, physician assistant, nurse practitioner, social worker or other
29 professional appointed by the court who is qualified to evaluate the
30 respondent's alleged cognitive and functional abilities and limitations and
31 will not be advantaged or disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition
32 or otherwise have a conflict of interest.
33 (b) Unless otherwise specified by the court, the report of the
34 examination and evaluation submitted to the court shall contain:
35 (1) The respondent's name, age and date of birth;
36 (2) a description of the respondent's physical and mental condition;
37 (3) a description of the nature and extent of the respondent's cognitive
38 and functional abilities and limitations, including adaptive behaviors and
39 social skills, and, as appropriate, educational and developmental potential;
40 (4) a summary of self-care and independent-living tasks the
41 respondent can manage without assistance or with existing supports, could
42 manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive services,
43 technological assistance or supported decision making, and cannot
HB 2359—Am. by HC 105
1 manage;
2 (5) a prognosis for any improvement and, as appropriate, any
3 recommendation for treatment or rehabilitation;
4 (6) a list and description of any prior assessments, evaluations or
5 examinations of the respondent, including the dates thereof, which were
6 relied upon in the preparation of this evaluation;
7 (7) the date and location where this examination and evaluation
8 occurred, and the name or names of the professional or professionals
9 performing the examination and evaluation and such professional's
10 qualifications;
11 (8) a statement by the professional that the professional has
12 personally completed an independent examination and evaluation of the
13 respondent, and that the report submitted to the court contains the results
14 of that examination and evaluation, and the professional's opinion with
15 regard to the issues of whether or not the respondent is in need of a
16 guardian and whether there are barriers to the respondent's attendance and
17 participation at the hearing on the petition; and
18 (9) the signature of the professional who prepared the report.
19 (c) The professional shall file with the court, at least five days prior to
20 the date of the trial, such professional's written report concerning the
21 examination and evaluation ordered by the court. The report shall be made
22 available by the court to counsel for all parties.
23 (d) In lieu of entering an order for an examination and evaluation as
24 provided for in this section, the court may determine that the report
25 accompanying the petition is in compliance with the requirements of this
26 section and that no further examination or evaluation should be required,
27 unless the respondent, or such person's attorney, requests such an
28 examination and evaluation in writing. Any such request shall be filed with
29 the court, and a copy thereof delivered to the petitioner, at least four days
30 prior to the date of the trial. Accompanying the request shall be a statement
31 of the reasons why an examination and evaluation is requested and the
32 name and address of a qualified professional or facility willing and able to
33 conduct this examination and evaluation. If the court orders a further
34 examination and evaluation, the court may continue the trial and fix a new
35 date, time and place of the trial at a time not to exceed 30 days from the
36 date of the filing of the request.
37 New Sec. 127. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (b), a
38 hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, may not
39 proceed unless the respondent attends the hearing. If it is not reasonably
40 feasible for the respondent to attend a hearing at the location where court
41 proceedings typically are held, the court shall make reasonable efforts to
42 hold the hearing at an alternative location convenient to the respondent or
43 allow the respondent to attend the hearing using real-time audio-visual
HB 2359—Am. by HC 106
1 technology.
2 (b) A hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
3 thereto, may proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court
4 finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
5 (1) The respondent is choosing not to attend the hearing after having
6 been fully informed of the right to attend and the potential consequences
7 of failing to do so;
8 (2) there is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and
9 participate in the hearing even with appropriate supportive services and
10 technological assistance; or
11 (3) the respondent is a minor who has received proper notice and
12 attendance would be harmful to the minor.
13 (c) The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under sections 119
14 through 130, and amendments thereto, by a person or persons of the
15 respondent's choosing, assistive technology or an interpreter or translator,
16 or a combination of these supports. If assistance would facilitate the
17 respondent's participation in the hearing, but is not otherwise available to
18 the respondent, the court shall make reasonable efforts to provide it.
19 (d) The respondent has a right to retain an attorney to represent the
20 respondent at a hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
21 thereto.
22 (e) At a hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
23 thereto, the respondent may:
24 (1) Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents;
25 (2) examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator and
26 the court liaison; and
27 (3) otherwise participate in the hearing.
28 (f) A hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
29 thereto, must be closed on request of the respondent and a showing of
30 good cause.
31 (g) Any person may request to participate in a hearing under sections
32 119 through 130, and amendments thereto. The court may grant the
33 request, with or without a hearing, on determining that the best interest of
34 the respondent will be served. The court may impose appropriate
35 conditions on the person's participation.

41 New Sec. 129. (a) The existence of a proceeding for or the existence
42 of a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship is a
43 matter of public record unless the court seals the record after:
HB 2359—Am. by HC 107
1 (1) The respondent, the individual subject to the protective
2 arrangement, or the parent of a minor subject to the protective arrangement
3 requests the record be sealed; and
4 (2) either:
5 (A) The proceeding is dismissed;
6 (B) the protective arrangement is no longer in effect; or
7 (C) an act authorized by the order granting the protective arrangement
8 has been completed.
9 (b) (1) An order of protective arrangement is a matter of public record
10 unless sealed by the court. All other court records of the proceeding
11 relating to the protective arrangement are not a matter of public record
12 except as further provided.
13 (2) The following persons may access court records of the proceeding
14 and resulting protective arrangement:
15 (A) A respondent;
16 (B) an individual subject to a protective arrangement instead of
17 guardianship or conservatorship;
18 (C) an attorney designated by the respondent or individual;
19 (D) a parent of a minor subject to a protective arrangement; and
20 (E) a licensed attorney, abstractor, or title insurance agent.
21 (3) A person not otherwise entitled to access to court records under
22 this subsection for good cause may request permission from the court for
23 access. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest of the
24 respondent or individual subject to the protective arrangement or furthers
25 the public interest and does not endanger the welfare or financial interests
26 of the respondent or individual.
27 (c) A report of a court liaison or professional evaluation generated in
28 the course of a proceeding under sections 119 through 130, and
29 amendments thereto, must be sealed on filing but is available to:
30 (1) The court;
31 (2) the individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation,
32 without limitation as to use;
33 (3) the petitioner, court liaison and petitioner's and respondent's
34 attorneys, for purposes of the proceeding;
35 (4) unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a
36 power of attorney for finances in which the respondent is the principal;
37 (5) if the order is for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship
38 and unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a power of
39 attorney for healthcare in which the respondent is identified as the
40 principal; and
41 (6) any other person if it is in the public interest or for a purpose the
42 court orders for good cause.

5 develop a statement of rights form, petition forms and report and
6 accounting forms.
7 New Sec. 132. In applying and construing this uniform act,
8 consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law
9 with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it.
10 New Sec. 133. This act modifies, limits or supersedes the electronic
11 signatures in global and national commerce act, 15 U.S.C. § 7001 et seq.,
12 but does not modify, limit or supersede section 101(c) of that act, 15
13 U.S.C. § 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices
14 described in section 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. § 7003(b).
15 New Sec. 134. (a) This act applies to:
16 (1) A proceeding for appointment of a guardian or conservator or for
17 a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship
18 commenced after January 1, 2026; and
19 (2) except as provided in subsection (b), a guardianship,
20 conservatorship or protective arrangement instead of guardianship or
21 conservatorship in existence on January 1, 2026, unless the court finds
22 application of a particular provision of this act would substantially
23 interfere with the effective conduct of the proceeding or prejudice the
24 rights of a party, in which case the particular provision of this act does not
25 apply and the superseded law applies.
26 (b) Sections 79 and 103, and amendments thereto, mandating a
27 guardian's plan or conservator's plan shall not apply to guardianships or
28 conservatorships in existence on January 1, 2026, unless the court orders
29 that a guardian's plan or conservator's plan is required.
30 New Sec. 135. If any provision of this act or its application to any
31 person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect other
32 provisions or applications of this act which can be given effect without the
33 invalid provision or application, and to this end the provisions of this act
34 are severable.

43 (b) If any beneficiary is a minor at the time funds become payable to
HB 2359—Am. by HC 109
1 the beneficiary pursuant to this section, the bank shall pay out in

4 withdraw funds on deposit in the account in the manner provided in the
5 contract, in whole or in part, as though no beneficiary has been named, and
6 to change the designation of beneficiary. No change in the designation of
7 the beneficiary shall be valid unless executed in the form and manner

23 Sec. 144. K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 58-656 is hereby amended to read as
24 follows: 58-656. (a) An attorney in fact who elects to act under a power of
25 attorney is under a duty to act in the interest of the principal and to avoid
26 conflicts of interest that impair the ability of the attorney in fact so to act.
27 A person who is appointed an attorney in fact under a power of attorney
28 who undertakes to exercise the authority conferred in the power of
29 attorney, has a fiduciary obligation to exercise the powers conferred in the
30 best interests of the principal, and to avoid self-dealing and conflicts of
31 interest, as in the case of a trustee with respect to the trustee's beneficiary
32 or beneficiaries. The attorney in fact shall keep a record of receipts,
33 disbursements and transactions made on behalf of the principal and shall
34 not comingle funds or assets of the principal with the funds or assets of the
35 attorney in fact. In the absence of explicit authorization, the attorney in
36 fact shall exercise a high degree of care in maintaining, without
37 modification, any estate plan which the principal may have in place,
38 including, but not limited to, arrangements made by the principal for

40 by joint tenancy or tenancy by the entirety, trust arrangements or by will or

43 who elects to act shall exercise the authority granted in a power of attorney
HB 2359—Am. by HC 121

HB 2359—Am. by HC 122
1 principal's successors. The attorney in fact shall promptly deliver to and

26 Sec. 153. K.S.A. 59-29b49 is hereby amended to read as follows: 59-
27 29b49. (a) A person with an alcohol or substance abuse problem may be
28 admitted to a treatment facility as a voluntary patient when there are
29 available accommodations and the head of the treatment facility
30 determines such person is in need of treatment therein, and that the person
31 has the capacity to consent to treatment.
32 (b) Admission shall be made upon written application:
33 (1) If such person is 18 years of age or older the person may make
34 such application for themself; or
35 (2) (A) If such person is less than 18 years of age, a parent may make
36 such application for their child; or
37 (B) if such person is less than 18 years of age, but 14 years of age or
38 older, the person may make such written application on their own behalf
39 without the consent or written application of their parent, legal guardian or
40 any other person. Whenever a person who is 14 years of age or older
41 makes written application on their own behalf and is admitted as a
42 voluntary patient, the head of the treatment facility shall promptly notify
43 the child's parent, legal guardian or other person known to the head of the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 134
1 treatment facility to be interested in the care and welfare of the minor of
2 the admittance of that child; or
3 (3) if such person has a legal guardian, the legal guardian may make
4 such application provided that if the legal guardian is required to obtain
5 authority to do so pursuant to K.S.A. 59-3077 sections 77 and 78, and
6 amendments thereto, then only in accordance with the provisions thereof.
7 If the legal guardian is seeking admission of their ward upon an order
8 giving the guardian continuing authority to admit the ward to a treatment
9 facility as defined in K.S.A. 59-3077 sections 77 and 78, and amendments
10 thereto, the head of the treatment facility may require a statement from the
11 patient's attending physician or from the local health officer of the area in
12 which the patient resides confirming that the patient is in need of treatment
13 for an alcohol or substance abuse problem in a treatment facility before
14 accepting the ward for admission, and shall divert any such person to a
15 less restrictive treatment alternative as may be appropriate.
16 (c) No person shall be admitted as a voluntary patient under the
17 provisions of this act to any treatment facility unless the head of the
18 treatment facility has informed such person or such person's parent, legal
19 guardian, or other person known to the head of the treatment facility to be
20 interested in the care and welfare of a minor, in writing, of the following:
21 (1) The rules and procedures of the treatment facility relating to the
22 discharge of voluntary patients;
23 (2) the legal rights of a voluntary patient receiving treatment from a
24 treatment facility as provided for in K.S.A. 59-29b78 and amendments
25 thereto; and
26 (3) in general terms, the types of treatment which are available or
27 would not be available to a voluntary patient from that treatment facility.
28 (d) Nothing in this act shall be construed as to prohibit a proposed or
29 involuntary patient with capacity to do so from making an application for
30 admission as a voluntary patient to a treatment facility. Any proposed or
31 involuntary patient desiring to do so shall be afforded an opportunity to
32 consult with their attorney prior to making any such application. If the
33 head of the treatment facility accepts the application and admits the patient
34 as a voluntary patient, then the head of the treatment facility shall notify, in
35 writing, the patient's attorney, the patient's legal guardian, if the patient has
36 a legal guardian, and the district court which has jurisdiction over the
37 patient of the patient's voluntary status. When a notice of voluntary
38 admission is received, the court shall file the same which shall terminate
39 the proceedings.

15 Sec. 157. K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 59-2946 is hereby amended to read as
16 follows: 59-2946. When used in the care and treatment act for mentally ill
17 persons:
18 (a) "Discharge" means the final and complete release from treatment,
19 by either the head of a treatment facility acting pursuant to K.S.A. 59-
20 2950, and amendments thereto, or by an order of a court issued pursuant to
21 K.S.A. 59-2973, and amendments thereto.
22 (b) "Head of a treatment facility" means the administrative director of
23 a treatment facility or such person's designee.
24 (c) "Law enforcement officer" means the same as defined in K.S.A.
25 22-2202, and amendments thereto.
26 (d) (1) "Mental health center" means any community mental health
27 center as defined in K.S.A. 39-2002, and amendments thereto, or a mental
28 health clinic organized as a not-for-profit or a for-profit corporation
29 pursuant to K.S.A. 17-1701 through 17-1775, and amendments thereto, or
30 K.S.A. 17-6001 through 17-6010, and amendments thereto, and licensed in
31 accordance with the provisions of K.S.A. 39-2001 et seq., and
32 amendments thereto.
33 (2) "Participating mental health center" means a mental health center
34 that has entered into a contract with the secretary for aging and disability
35 services pursuant to the provisions of K.S.A. 39-1601 through 39-1612,
36 and amendments thereto.
37 (e) "Mentally ill person" means any person who is suffering from a
38 mental disorder that is manifested by a clinically significant behavioral or
39 psychological syndrome or pattern and associated with either a painful
40 symptom or an impairment in one or more important areas of functioning,
41 and involving substantial behavioral, psychological or biological
42 dysfunction, to the extent that the person is in need of treatment.
43 (f) (1) "Mentally ill person subject to involuntary commitment for
HB 2359—Am. by HC 138
1 care and treatment" means a mentally ill person, as defined in subsection
2 (e), who also lacks capacity to make an informed decision concerning
3 treatment, is likely to cause harm to self or others, and whose diagnosis is
4 not solely one of the following mental disorders: Alcohol or chemical
5 substance abuse; antisocial personality disorder; intellectual disability;
6 organic personality syndrome; or an organic mental disorder.
7 (2) "Lacks capacity to make an informed decision concerning
8 treatment" means that the person, by reason of the person's mental
9 disorder, is unable, despite conscientious efforts at explanation, to
10 understand basically the nature and effects of hospitalization or treatment
11 or is unable to engage in a rational decision-making process regarding
12 hospitalization or treatment, as evidenced by an inability to weigh the
13 possible risks and benefits.
14 (3) "Likely to cause harm to self or others" means that the person, by
15 reason of the person's mental disorder: (A) Is likely, in the reasonably
16 foreseeable future, to cause substantial physical injury or physical abuse to
17 self or others or substantial damage to another's property, as evidenced by
18 behavior threatening, attempting or causing such injury, abuse or damage;
19 except that if the harm threatened, attempted or caused is only harm to the
20 property of another, the harm must be of such a value and extent that the
21 state's interest in protecting the property from such harm outweighs the
22 person's interest in personal liberty; or (B) is substantially unable, except
23 for reason of indigency, to provide for any of the person's basic needs,
24 such as food, clothing, shelter, health or safety, causing a substantial
25 deterioration of the person's ability to function on the person's own.
26 No person who is being treated by prayer in the practice of the religion
27 of any church that teaches reliance on spiritual means alone through prayer
28 for healing shall be determined to be a mentally ill person subject to
29 involuntary commitment for care and treatment under this act unless
30 substantial evidence is produced upon which the district court finds that
31 the proposed patient is likely in the reasonably foreseeable future to cause
32 substantial physical injury or physical abuse to self or others or substantial
33 damage to another's property, as evidenced by behavior threatening,
34 attempting or causing such injury, abuse or damage; except that if the harm
35 threatened, attempted or caused is only harm to the property of another, the
36 harm must be of such a value and extent that the state's interest in
37 protecting the property from such harm outweighs the person's interest in
38 personal liberty.
39 (g) "Patient" means a person who is a voluntary patient, a proposed
40 patient or an involuntary patient.
41 (1) "Voluntary patient" means a person who is receiving treatment at
42 a treatment facility pursuant to K.S.A. 59-2949, and amendments thereto.
43 (2) "Proposed patient" means a person for whom a petition pursuant
HB 2359—Am. by HC 139
1 to K.S.A. 59-2952 or 59-2957, and amendments thereto, has been filed.
2 (3) "Involuntary patient" means a person who is receiving treatment
3 under order of a court or a person admitted and detained by a treatment
4 facility pursuant to an application filed pursuant to K.S.A. 59-2954(b) or
5 (c), and amendments thereto.
6 (h) "Physician" means a person licensed to practice medicine and
7 surgery as provided for in the Kansas healing arts act or a person who is
8 employed by a state psychiatric hospital or by an agency of the United
9 States and who is authorized by law to practice medicine and surgery
10 within that hospital or agency.
11 (i) "Psychologist" means a licensed psychologist, as defined by
12 K.S.A. 74-5302, and amendments thereto.
13 (j) "Qualified mental health professional" means a physician or
14 psychologist who is employed by a participating mental health center or
15 who is providing services as a physician or psychologist under a contract
16 with a participating mental health center, a licensed master's level
17 psychologist, a licensed clinical psychotherapist, a licensed marriage and
18 family therapist, a licensed clinical marriage and family therapist, a
19 licensed professional counselor, a licensed clinical professional counselor,
20 a licensed specialist social worker or a licensed master social worker or a
21 registered nurse who has a specialty in psychiatric nursing, who is
22 employed by a participating mental health center and who is acting under
23 the direction of a physician or psychologist who is employed by, or under
24 contract with, a participating mental health center.
25 (1) "Direction" means monitoring and oversight including regular,
26 periodic evaluation of services.
27 (2) "Licensed master social worker" means a person licensed as a
28 master social worker by the behavioral sciences regulatory board under
29 K.S.A. 65-6301 through 65-6318, and amendments thereto.
30 (3) "Licensed specialist social worker" means a person licensed in a
31 social work practice specialty by the behavioral sciences regulatory board
32 under K.S.A. 65-6301 through 65-6318, and amendments thereto.
33 (4) "Licensed master's level psychologist" means a person licensed as
34 a licensed master's level psychologist by the behavioral sciences regulatory
35 board under K.S.A. 74-5361 through 74-5373, and amendments thereto.
36 (5) "Registered nurse" means a person licensed as a registered
37 professional nurse by the board of nursing under K.S.A. 65-1113 through
38 65-1164, and amendments thereto.
39 (k) "Secretary" means the secretary for aging and disability services.
40 (l) "State psychiatric hospital" means Larned state hospital,
41 Osawatomie state hospital or Rainbow mental health facility.
42 (m) "Treatment" means any service intended to promote the mental
43 health of the patient and rendered by a qualified professional, licensed or
HB 2359—Am. by HC 140
1 certified by the state to provide such service as an independent practitioner
2 or under the supervision of such practitioner.
3 (n) "Treatment facility" means any mental health center or clinic,
4 psychiatric unit of a medical care facility, state psychiatric hospital,
5 psychologist, physician or other institution or person authorized or
6 licensed by law to provide either inpatient or outpatient treatment to any
7 patient.
8 (o) The terms defined in K.S.A. 59-3051 section 25, and amendments
9 thereto, shall have the meanings provided by that section.

22 thereto, whose qualified disability expenses may be paid from the account.
23 The designated beneficiary must be an eligible individual at the time the
24 account is established.
25 (e) "Eligible individual" means the same as defined in section 529A
26 of the federal internal revenue code of 1986, as amended.
27 (f) "Financial organization" means an organization authorized to do
28 business in the state of Kansas and is:
29 (1) Licensed or chartered by the commissioner of insurance;
30 (2) licensed or chartered by the state bank commissioner;
31 (3) chartered by an agency of the federal government; or
32 (4) subject to the jurisdiction and regulation of the securities and
33 exchange commission of the federal government.
34 (g) "Guardian" means a person appointed by the court pursuant to
35 K.S.A. 59-3050 et seq. the Kansas uniform guardianship, conservatorship
36 and other protective arrangements act, sections 24 through 135, and
37 amendments thereto.
38 (h) "Management contract" means the contract executed by the
39 treasurer and a financial organization selected to act as a depository and
40 manager of the program.
41 (i) "Member of the family" means the same as defined in section
42 529A of the federal internal revenue code of 1986, as amended.
43 (j) "Nonqualified withdrawal" means a withdrawal from an account

1 which is not:
2 (1) A qualified withdrawal; or

19 Sec. 164. K.S.A. 76-729 is hereby amended to read as follows: 76-
20 729. (a) (1) Persons enrolling at the state educational institutions under the
21 control and supervision of the state board of regents who, if such persons
22 are adults, have been domiciliary residents of the state of Kansas or, if
23 such persons are minors, whose parents have been domiciliary residents of
24 the state of Kansas for at least 12 months prior to enrollment for any term
25 or session at a state educational institution are residents for fee purposes. A
26 person who has been a resident of the state of Kansas for fee purposes and
27 who leaves the state of Kansas to become a resident of another state or
28 country shall retain status as a resident of the state of Kansas for fee
29 purposes if the person returns to domiciliary residency in the state of
30 Kansas within 60 months of departure. All other persons are nonresidents
31 of the state of Kansas for fee purposes.
32 (2) The provisions of this subsection shall not apply to a person who
33 is deemed a resident for fee purposes pursuant to K.S.A. 76-731a, and
34 amendments thereto.
35 (b) The state board of regents may authorize the following persons, or
36 any class or classes thereof, and their spouses and dependents to pay an
37 amount equal to resident fees:
38 (1) Persons who are employees of a state educational institution;
39 (2) persons having special domestic relations circumstances;
40 (3) persons who have lost their resident status within six months of
41 enrollment;
42 (4) persons who are not domiciliary residents of the state, who have
43 graduated from a high school accredited by the state board of education
HB 2359—Am. by HC 146
1 within six months of enrollment, who were domiciliary residents of the
2 state at the time of graduation from high school or within 12 months prior

6 (5) persons who are domiciliary residents of the state, whose

27 period and to which the person intends to return following absence.

6 Sec. 166. K.S.A. 77-201 is hereby amended to read as follows: 77-
7 201. In the construction of the statutes of this state the following rules
8 shall be observed, unless the construction would be inconsistent with the
9 manifest intent of the legislature or repugnant to the context of the statute:
10 First. The repeal of a statute does not revive a statute previously
11 repealed, nor does the repeal affect any right which accrued, any duty
12 imposed, any penalty incurred or any proceeding commenced, under or by
13 virtue of the statute repealed. The provisions of any statute, so far as they
14 are the same as those of any prior statute, shall be construed as a
15 continuation of the prior provisions and not as a new enactment.
16 Second. Words and phrases shall be construed according to the context
17 and the approved usage of the language, but technical words and phrases,
18 and other words and phrases that have acquired a peculiar and appropriate
19 meaning in law, shall be construed according to their peculiar and
20 appropriate meanings.
21 Third. Words importing the singular number only may be extended to
22 several persons or things, and words importing the plural number only
23 may be applied to one person or thing. Words importing the masculine
24 gender only may be extended to females.
25 Fourth. Words giving a joint authority to three or more public officers
26 or other persons shall be construed as given that authority to a majority of
27 them, unless it is otherwise expressed in the act giving the authority.
28 Fifth. "Highway" and "road" include public bridges and may be
29 construed to be equivalent to "county way," "county road," "common
30 road," "state road" and "territorial road."
31 Sixth. "Incompetent person" includes disabled persons and
32 incapacitated persons as defined herein in this section.
33 Seventh. "Issue," as applied to the descent of estates, includes all the
34 lawful lineal descendants of the ancestor.
35 Eighth. "Land," "real estate" and "real property" include lands,
36 tenements and hereditaments, and all rights to them and interest in them,
37 equitable as well as legal.
38 Ninth. "Personal property" includes money, goods, chattels, evidences
39 of debt and things in action, and digital assets as defined in the revised
40 uniform fiduciary access to digital assets act, K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 58-4801
41 through 58-4819, and amendments thereto.
42 Tenth. "Property" includes personal and real property.
43 Eleventh. "Month" means a calendar month, unless otherwise
HB 2359—Am. by HC 148
1 expressed. "Year" alone, and also the abbreviation "A.D.," is equivalent to
2 the expression "year of our Lord."
3 Twelfth. "Oath" includes an affirmation in all cases where an
4 affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and in similar cases "swear"
5 includes affirm.
6 Thirteenth. "Person" may be extended to bodies politic and corporate.
7 Fourteenth. If the seal of a court or public office or officer is required
8 by law to be affixed to any paper, "seal" includes an impression of the seal
9 upon the paper alone, as well as upon wax or a wafer affixed to the paper.
10 "Seal" also includes both a rubber stamp seal used with permanent ink and
11 the word "seal" printed on court documents produced by computer
12 systems, so that the seal may be legibly reproduced by photographic
13 process.
14 Fifteenth. "State," when applied to the different parts of the United
15 States, includes the District of Columbia and the territories. "United
16 States" may include that district and those territories.
17 Sixteenth. "Town" may mean a civil township, unless a different
18 meaning is plainly intended.
19 Seventeenth. "Will" includes codicils.
20 Eighteenth. "Written" and "in writing" may include printing, engraving,
21 lithography and any other mode of representing words and letters,
22 excepting those cases where the written signature or the mark of any
23 person is required by law.
24 Nineteenth. "Sheriff" may be extended to any person performing the
25 duties of the sheriff, either generally or in special cases.
26 Twentieth. "Deed" is applied to an instrument conveying lands but does
27 not imply a sealed instrument. "Bond" and "indenture" do not necessarily
28 imply a seal but in other respects mean the same kind of instruments as
29 above. "Undertaking" means a promise or security in any form where
30 required by law.
31 Twenty-first. "Executor" includes an administrator where the subject
32 matter applies to an administrator.
33 Twenty-second. Roman numerals and Arabic figures are to be taken as a
34 part of the English language.
35 Twenty-third. "Residence" means the place which is adopted by a
36 person as the person's place of habitation and to which, whenever the
37 person is absent, the person has the intention of returning. When a person
38 eats at one place and sleeps at another, the place where the person sleeps
39 shall be considered the person's residence.
40 Twenty-fourth. "Usual place of residence" and "usual place of abode,"
41 when applied to the service of any process or notice, means the place
42 usually occupied by a person. If a person has no family, or does not have
43 family with the person, the person's office or place of business or, if the
HB 2359—Am. by HC 149
1 person has no place of business, the room or place where the person
2 usually sleeps shall be construed to be the person's place of residence or
3 abode.
4 Twenty-fifth. "Householder" means a person who is 18 or more years of
5 age and who owns or occupies a house as a place of residence and not as a
6 boarder or lodger.
7 Twenty-sixth. "General election" refers to the election required to be
8 held on the Tuesday following the first Monday in November of each
9 even-numbered year.
10 Twenty-seventh. "Under legal disability" includes persons who are
11 within the period of minority, or who are incapacitated, incompetent or
12 imprisoned.
13 Twenty-eighth. When a person is required to be disinterested or
14 indifferent in acting on any question or matter affecting other parties,
15 relationship within the degree of second cousin, inclusive, shall disqualify
16 the person from acting, except by consent of parties.
17 Twenty-ninth. "Head of a family" shall include any person who has
18 charge of children, relatives or others living with the person.
19 Thirtieth. "Mentally ill person" means a mentally ill person as defined
20 in K.S.A. 59-2946, and amendments thereto.
21 Thirty-first. "Incapacitated person" means an individual whose ability
22 to receive and evaluate relevant information, or to effectively
23 communicate decisions, or both, even with the use of assistive
24 technologies or other supports, is impaired to the degree that the person
25 lacks the capacity to manage the person's estate, or to meet essential needs
26 for the person's physical health, safety or welfare, as defined in K.S.A. 59-
27 3051 section 25, and amendments thereto, whether or not a guardian or a
28 conservator has been appointed for that person.
29 Thirty-second. "Guardian" means an individual or a nonprofit
30 corporation certified in accordance with K.S.A. 59-3070 section 35, and
31 amendments thereto, which has been appointed by a court to act on behalf
32 of a ward and possessed of some or all of the powers and duties set out in
33 K.S.A. 59-3075 sections 76 through 78, and amendments thereto.
34 "Guardian" does not mean natural guardian unless specified.
35 Thirty-third. "Natural guardian" means both the biological or adoptive
36 mother and father of a minor if neither parent has been found to be an
37 adult with an impairment in need of a guardian or has had parental rights
38 terminated by a court of competent jurisdiction. If either parent of a minor
39 is deceased, or has been found to be an adult with an impairment in need
40 of a guardian, as provided for in K.S.A. 59-3050 through 59-3095 the
41 Kansas uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other protective
42 arrangements act, sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto, or
43 has had parental rights terminated by a court of competent jurisdiction,
HB 2359—Am. by HC 150
1 then the other parent shall be the natural guardian, unless also deceased, or
2 found to be an adult with an impairment in need of a guardian, or has had
3 parental rights terminated by a court of competent jurisdiction, in which
4 case no person shall qualify as the natural guardian.
5 Thirty-fourth. "Conservator" means an individual or corporation
6 appointed by the court to act on behalf of a conservatee and possessed of
7 some or all of the powers and duties set out in K.S.A. 59-3078 sections 99
8 through 102, and amendments thereto.
9 Thirty-fifth. "Minor" means any person defined by K.S.A. 38-101, and
10 amendments thereto, as being within the period of minority.
11 Thirty-sixth. "Proposed ward" means a person for whom a petition for
12 the appointment of a guardian pursuant to K.S.A. 59-3058, 59-3059, 59-
13 3060 or 59-3061 sections 17, 18, 28, 49, 52 or 65, and amendments
14 thereto, has been filed.
15 Thirty-seventh. "Proposed conservatee" means a person for whom a
16 petition for the appointment of a conservator pursuant to K.S.A. 59-3058,
17 59-3059, 59-3060 or 59-3061 sections 17, 18, 28, 49, 52 or 65, and
18 amendments thereto, has been filed.
19 Thirty-eighth. "Ward" means a person who has a guardian.
20 Thirty-ninth. "Conservatee" means a person who has a conservator.
21 Fortieth. "Manufactured home" means a structure which:
22 (1) Is transportable in one or more sections which, in the traveling
23 mode, is 8 body feet or more in width or 40 body feet or more in length,
24 or, when erected on site, is 320 or more square feet, and which is built on a
25 permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling, with or without
26 permanent foundation, when connected to the required utilities, and
27 includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning and electrical systems
28 contained therein; and
29 (2) is subject to the federal manufactured home construction and
30 safety standards established pursuant to 42 U.S.C. § 5403.
31 Forty-first. "Mobile home" means a structure which:
32 (1) Is transportable in one or more sections which, in the traveling
33 mode, is 8 body feet or more in width and 36 body feet or more in length
34 and is built on a permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling,
35 with or without a permanent foundation, when connected to the required
36 utilities, and includes the plumbing, heating, air conditioning and electrical
37 systems contained therein; and
38 (2) is not subject to the federal manufactured home construction and
39 safety standards established pursuant to 42 U.S.C. § 5403.
40 Forty-second. "Disabled person" includes incapacitated persons and
41 incompetent persons as defined herein in this section.

Session of 2025
HOUSE BILL No. 2359
By Committee on Judiciary
Requested by Nancy Strouse on behalf of the Kansas Judicial Council.

2 adult guardianship and protective proceedings jurisdiction act and the
3 uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other protective
4 arrangements act; amending K.S.A. 9-1215, 17-2263, 17-2264, 21-

19
20 Be it enacted by the Legislature of the State of Kansas:
21 New Section 1. Sections 1 through 23, and amendments thereto, may
22 be cited as the uniform adult guardianship and protective proceedings
23 jurisdiction act (2007).
24 New Sec. 2. As used in this act:
25 (a) "Adult" means an individual who has attained 18 years of age or
26 an emancipated individual under 18 years of age.
27 (b) "Conservator" means a person appointed by the court to
28 administer the property of an adult, including a person appointed under
29 section 93, and amendments thereto.
30 (c) "Guardian" means a person appointed by the court to make
31 decisions regarding the person of an adult, including a person appointed
32 under section 72, and amendments thereto.
33 (d) "Guardianship order" means an order appointing a guardian.
34 (e) "Guardianship proceeding" means a judicial proceeding in which
35 an order for the appointment of a guardian is sought or has been issued.

HB 2359—Am. by HC 2
1 (f) "Incapacitated person" means an adult for whom a guardian has
2 been appointed.
3 (g) "Party" means the respondent, petitioner, guardian, conservator or
4 any other person allowed by the court to participate in a guardianship or
5 protective proceeding.
6 (h) "Person," except in the term "incapacitated person" or "protected
7 person," means an individual, corporation, business trust, estate, trust,
8 partnership, limited liability company, association, joint venture, public
9 corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency or
10 instrumentality, or any other legal or commercial entity.
11 (i) "Protected person" means an adult for whom a protective order has
12 been issued.
13 (j) "Protective order" means an order appointing a conservator or
14 other order related to management of an adult's property.
15 (k) "Protective proceeding" means a judicial proceeding in which a
16 protective order is sought or has been issued.
17 (l) "Record" means information that is inscribed on a tangible
18 medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is
19 retrievable in perceivable form.
20 (m) "Respondent" means an adult for whom a protective order or the
21 appointment of a guardian is sought.
22 (n) "State" means a state of the United States, the District of
23 Columbia, Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands, a federally
24 recognized Indian tribe or any territory or insular possession subject to the
25 jurisdiction of the United States.
26 New Sec. 3. A court of this state may treat a foreign country as if it
27 were a state for the purpose of applying sections 1 through 17 and sections
28 21 through 23, and amendments thereto.
29 New Sec. 4. (a) A court of this state may communicate with a court in
30 another state concerning a proceeding arising under this act. The court may
31 allow the parties to participate in the communication. Except as otherwise
32 provided in subsection (b), the court shall make a record of the
33 communication. The record may be limited to the fact that the
34 communication occurred.
35 (b) Courts may communicate concerning schedules, calendars, court
36 records and other administrative matters without making a record.
37 New Sec. 5. (a) In a guardianship or protective proceeding in this
38 state, a court of this state may request the appropriate court of another state
39 to do any of the following:
40 (1) Hold an evidentiary hearing;
41 (2) order a person in that state to produce evidence or give testimony
42 pursuant to procedures of that state;
43 (3) order that an evaluation or assessment be made of the respondent;

HB 2359—Am. by HC 3
1 (4) order any appropriate investigation of a person involved in a
2 proceeding;
3 (5) forward to the court of this state a certified copy of the transcript
4 or other record of a hearing under paragraph (1) or any other proceeding,
5 any evidence otherwise produced under paragraph (2) and any evaluation
6 or assessment prepared in compliance with an order under paragraph (3) or
7 (4);
8 (6) issue any order necessary to assure the appearance in the
9 proceeding of a person whose presence is necessary for the court to make a
10 determination, including the respondent or the incapacitated or protected
11 person; and
12 (7) issue an order authorizing the release of medical, financial,
13 criminal or other relevant information in that state, including protected
14 health information as defined in 45 C.F.R 160.103.
15 (b) If a court of another state in which a guardianship or protective
16 proceeding is pending requests assistance of the kind provided in
17 subsection (a), a court of this state has jurisdiction for the limited purpose
18 of granting the request or making reasonable efforts to comply with the
19 request.
20 New Sec. 6. (a) In a guardianship or protective proceeding, in
21 addition to other procedures that may be available, testimony of a witness
22 who is located in another state may be offered by deposition or other
23 means allowable in this state for testimony taken in another state. The
24 court on its own motion may order that the testimony of a witness be taken
25 in another state and may prescribe the manner in which and the terms upon
26 which the testimony is to be taken.
27 (b) In a guardianship or protective proceeding, a court in this state
28 may permit a witness located in another state to be deposed or to testify by
29 telephone or audiovisual or other electronic means. A court of this state
30 shall cooperate with the court of the other state in designating an
31 appropriate location for the deposition or testimony.
32 New Sec. 7. (a) As used in sections 7 through 15, and amendments
33 thereto:
34 (1) "Emergency" means a circumstance that likely will result in
35 substantial harm to a respondent's health, safety or welfare, and for which
36 the appointment of a guardian is necessary because no other person has
37 authority and is willing to act on the respondent's behalf;
38 (2) "home state" means the state in which the respondent was
39 physically present, including any period of temporary absence, for at least
40 six consecutive months immediately before the filing of a petition for a
41 protective order or the appointment of a guardian, or if none, the state in
42 which the respondent was physically present, including any period of
43 temporary absence, for at least six consecutive months ending within the

HB 2359—Am. by HC 4
1 six months prior to the filing of the petition; and
2 (3) "significant-connection state" means a state, other than the home
3 state, with which a respondent has a significant connection other than mere
4 physical presence and in which substantial evidence concerning the
5 respondent is available.
6 (b) In determining under sections 9 and 16(e), and amendments
7 thereto, whether a respondent has a significant connection with a particular
8 state, the court shall consider:
9 (1) The location of the respondent's family and other persons required
10 to be notified of the guardianship or protective proceeding;
11 (2) the length of time the respondent at any time was physically
12 present in the state and the duration of any absence;
13 (3) the location of the respondent's property; and
14 (4) the extent to which the respondent has ties to the state such as
15 voting registration, state or local tax return filing, vehicle registration,
16 driver's license, social relationship and receipt of services.
17 New Sec. 8. Sections 7 through 15, and amendments thereto,
18 provides the exclusive jurisdictional basis for a court of this state to
19 appoint a guardian or issue a protective order for an adult.
20 New Sec. 9. A court of this state has jurisdiction to appoint a guardian
21 or issue a protective order for a respondent if:
22 (a) This state is the respondent's home state;
23 (b) on the date the petition is filed, this state is a significant-
24 connection state and:
25 (1) The respondent does not have a home state or a court of the
26 respondent's home state has declined to exercise jurisdiction because this
27 state is a more appropriate forum; or
28 (2) the respondent has a home state, a petition for an appointment or
29 order is not pending in a court of that state or another significant-
30 connection state, and, before the court makes the appointment or issues the
31 order:
32 (A) A petition for an appointment or order is not filed in the
33 respondent's home state;
34 (B) an objection to the court's jurisdiction is not filed by a person
35 required to be notified of the proceeding; and
36 (C) the court in this state concludes that it is an appropriate forum
37 under the factors set forth in section 12, and amendments thereto;
38 (c) this state does not have jurisdiction under either subsection (a) or
39 (b), the respondent's home state and all significant-connection states have
40 declined to exercise jurisdiction because this state is the more appropriate
41 forum and jurisdiction in this state is consistent with the constitutions of
42 this state and the United States; or
43 (d) the requirements for special jurisdiction under section 10, and

HB 2359—Am. by HC 5
1 amendments thereto, are met.
2 New Sec. 10. (a) A court of this state lacking jurisdiction under
3 section 9(a), (b) or (c), and amendments thereto, has special jurisdiction to
4 do any of the following:
5 (1) Appoint a guardian in an emergency for a term not exceeding 90
6 days for a respondent who is physically present in this state;
7 (2) issue a protective order with respect to real or tangible personal
8 property located in this state;
9 (3) appoint a guardian or conservator for an incapacitated or protected
10 person for whom a provisional order to transfer the proceeding from
11 another state has been issued under procedures similar to section 16, and
12 amendments thereto.
13 (b) If a petition for the appointment of a guardian in an emergency is
14 brought in this state and this state was not the respondent's home state on
15 the date the petition was filed, the court shall dismiss the proceeding at the
16 request of the court of the home state, if any, whether dismissal is
17 requested before or after the emergency appointment.
18 New Sec. 11. Except as otherwise provided in section 10, and
19 amendments thereto, a court that has appointed a guardian or issued a
20 protective order consistent with this act has exclusive and continuing
21 jurisdiction over the proceeding until it is terminated by the court or the
22 appointment or order expires by its own terms.
23 New Sec. 12. (a) A court of this state having jurisdiction under
24 section 9, and amendments thereto, to appoint a guardian or issue a
25 protective order may decline to exercise its jurisdiction if it determines at
26 any time that a court of another state is a more appropriate forum.
27 (b) If a court of this state declines to exercise its jurisdiction under
28 subsection (a), it shall either dismiss or stay the proceeding. The court may
29 impose any condition the court considers just and proper, including the
30 condition that a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a
31 protective order be filed promptly in another state.
32 (c) In determining whether it is an appropriate forum, the court shall
33 consider all relevant factors, including:
34 (1) Any expressed preference of the respondent;
35 (2) whether abuse, neglect or exploitation of the respondent has
36 occurred or is likely to occur and which state could best protect the
37 respondent from the abuse, neglect or exploitation;
38 (3) the length of time the respondent was physically present in or was
39 a legal resident of this or another state;
40 (4) the distance of the respondent from the court in each state;
41 (5) the financial circumstances of the respondent's estate;
42 (6) the nature and location of the evidence;
43 (7) the ability of the court in each state to decide the issue

HB 2359—Am. by HC 6
1 expeditiously and the procedures necessary to present evidence;
2 (8) the familiarity of the court of each state with the facts and issues
3 in the proceeding; and
4 (9) if an appointment were made, the court's ability to monitor the
5 conduct of the guardian or conservator.
6 New Sec. 13. (a) If at any time a court of this state determines that it
7 acquired jurisdiction to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order
8 because of unjustifiable conduct, the court may:
9 (1) Decline to exercise jurisdiction;
10 (2) exercise jurisdiction for the limited purpose of fashioning an
11 appropriate remedy to ensure the health, safety and welfare of the
12 respondent or the protection of the respondent's property or prevent a
13 repetition of the unjustifiable conduct, including staying the proceeding
14 until a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a
15 protective order is filed in a court of another state having jurisdiction; or
16 (3) continue to exercise jurisdiction after considering:
17 (A) The extent to which the respondent and all persons required to be
18 notified of the proceedings have acquiesced in the exercise of the court's
19 jurisdiction;
20 (B) whether it is a more appropriate forum than the court of any other
21 state under the factors set forth in section 12(c), and amendments thereto;
22 and
23 (C) whether the court of any other state would have jurisdiction under
24 factual circumstances in substantial conformity with the jurisdictional
25 standards of section 9, and amendments thereto.
26 (b) If a court of this state determines that it acquired jurisdiction to
27 appoint a guardian or issue a protective order because a party seeking to
28 invoke its jurisdiction engaged in unjustifiable conduct, it may assess
29 against that party necessary and reasonable expenses, including attorney
30 fees, investigative fees, court costs, communication expenses, witness fees
31 and expenses and travel expenses. The court may not assess fees, costs or
32 expenses of any kind against this state or a governmental subdivision,
33 agency or instrumentality of this state unless authorized by law other than
34 this act.
35 New Sec. 14. If a petition for the appointment of a guardian or
36 issuance of a protective order is brought in this state and this state was not
37 the respondent's home state on the date the petition was filed, in addition
38 to complying with the notice requirements of this state, notice of the
39 petition must be given to those persons who would be entitled to notice of
40 the petition if a proceeding were brought in the respondent's home state.
41 The notice must be given in the same manner as notice is required to be
42 given in this state.

17 New Sec. 16. (a) A guardian or conservator appointed in this state
18 may petition the court to transfer the guardianship or conservatorship to
19 another state.
20 (b) Notice of a petition under subsection (a) must be given to the
21 persons that would be entitled to notice of a petition in this state for the

23 (c) On the court's own motion or on request of the guardian or

25 to be notified of the petition, the court shall hold a hearing on a petition
26 filed pursuant to subsection (a).
27 (d) The court shall issue an order provisionally granting a petition to
28 transfer a guardianship and shall direct the guardian to petition for
29 guardianship in the other state if the court is satisfied that the guardianship
30 will be accepted by the court in the other state and the court finds that:
31 (1) The incapacitated person is physically present in or is reasonably
32 expected to move permanently to the other state;
33 (2) an objection to the transfer has not been made or, if an objection
34 has been made, the objector has not established that the transfer would be
35 contrary to the interests of the incapacitated person; and
36 (3) plans for care and services for the incapacitated person in the
37 other state are reasonable and sufficient.
38 (e) The court shall issue a provisional order granting a petition to

43 (1) The protected person is physically present in or is reasonably

6 contrary to the interests of the protected person; and

36 New Sec. 21. In applying and construing this uniform act,
37 consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law
38 with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it.

1 New Sec. 23. (a) This act applies to guardianship and protective
2 proceedings begun on or after January 1, 2026.
3 (b) Sections 1 through 6 and 16 through 22, and amendments thereto,
4 apply to proceedings begun before January 1, 2026, regardless of whether

6 New Sec. 24. Sections 24 through 135, and amendments thereto, may
7 be cited as the Kansas uniform guardianship, conservatorship and other
8 protective arrangements act.
9 New Sec. 25. As used in this act:
10 (a) "Adult" means an individual at least 18 years of age or an
11 emancipated individual under 18 years of age.
12 (b) "Adult subject to conservatorship" means an adult for whom a
13 conservator has been appointed under this act.
14 (c) "Adult subject to guardianship" means an adult for whom a
15 guardian has been appointed under this act.
16 (d) "Claim" includes a claim against an individual or conservatorship
17 estate, whether arising in contract, tort or otherwise.
18 (e) "Conservator" means a person appointed by a court to make
19 decisions with respect to the property or financial affairs of an individual
20 subject to conservatorship. "Conservator" includes a co-conservator.
21 (f) "Conservatorship estate" means the property subject to
22 conservatorship under this act.
23 (g) "Expressly and with informed consent" means consent
24 voluntarily given with sufficient knowledge of the subject matter
25 involved, including a general understanding of the procedure,
26 medically acceptable alternative procedures or treatments and
27 substantial risks and hazards inherent in the proposed treatment or
28 procedures, to enable the person giving consent to make an
29 understanding and enlightened decision without any element of force,
30 fraud, deceit, duress or other form of constraint or coercion.
31 (h) "Full conservatorship" means a conservatorship that grants the
32 conservator all powers available under this act.
33 (h)(i) "Full guardianship" means a guardianship that grants the
34 guardian all powers available under this act.
35 (i)(j) "Guardian" means a person appointed by the court to make
36 decisions with respect to the personal affairs of an individual. "Guardian"
37 includes a co-guardian but does not include a guardian ad litem.
38 (j)(k) "Guardian ad litem" means a person appointed to inform the
39 court about, and to represent, the needs and best interest of an individual.
40 (l) "Hydration" means water or fluid administered in any
41 manner.
42 (k)(m) "Individual subject to conservatorship" means an adult or
43 minor for whom a conservator has been appointed under this act.

1 (l)(n) "Individual subject to guardianship" means an adult or minor

5 the appointment of a guardian or conservator. "Less restrictive alternative"

8 New Sec. 29. (a) Except as provided in subsection (e), venue for a
9 guardianship proceeding for a minor is in:
10 (1) The county in which the minor resides or is present at the time the
11 proceeding commences; or
12 (2) the county in which another proceeding concerning the custody or
13 parental rights of the minor is pending.
14 (b) Except as provided in subsection (e), venue for a guardianship
15 proceeding or protective arrangement instead of guardianship for an adult
16 is in:
17 (1) The county in which the respondent resides;
18 (2) if the respondent has been admitted to an institution by court
19 order, the county in which the court is located; or
20 (3) if the proceeding is for appointment of an emergency guardian for
21 an adult, the county in which the respondent is present.
22 (c) Except as provided in subsection (e), venue for a conservatorship
23 proceeding or protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is in:
24 (1) The county in which the respondent resides, whether or not a
25 guardian has been appointed in another county or other jurisdiction; or
26 (2) if the respondent does not reside in this state, in any county in
27 which property of the respondent is located.
28 (d) If proceedings under this act are brought in more than one county,
29 the court of the county in which the first proceeding is brought has the
30 exclusive right to proceed unless the court determines that venue is
31 properly in another court or the interest of justice otherwise requires
32 transfer of the proceeding.
33 (e) If proceedings under this act are brought in a county other than as
34 provided in subsections (a), (b) or (c), the court may determine that venue
35 is proper if it is in the best interest of the respondent and in the interest of
36 justice for the proceedings to take place in that county.

20 (1) An individual resident in this state; or
21 (2) a corporation, limited partnership, limited liability partnership,
22 limited liability company or business trust that has its principal place of
23 business in this state.
24 (c) Every resident agent for a guardian or conservator shall:
25 (1) Maintain contact with and remain aware of the current address
26 and phone number of the guardian or conservator;
27 (2) accept service of process and other communications directed to
28 the guardian or conservator; and
29 (3) forward to the guardian or conservator documents sent by the
30 court, the secretary of state or any other state agency.
31 (d) Every resident agent shall accept the appointment as resident
32 agent by executing an acceptance of appointment that specifically
33 identifies the name of the guardian or conservator and expresses the
34 appointed resident agent's agreement to fulfill their role, as described in
35 this section.
36 (e) For purposes of this section, the terms guardian and conservator
37 shall include co-guardians and co-conservators, temporary substitute
38 guardians and conservators, standby guardians and conservators, successor
39 guardians and conservators and emergency guardians and conservators.
40 New Sec. 33. (a) The court at any time may appoint a co-guardian or

43 (b) If the court appoints co-guardians or co-conservators, the court

5 New Sec. 34. (a) The court at any time may appoint a successor
6 guardian or successor conservator to serve immediately or when a
7 designated event occurs, including the absence, impairment, resignation or
