4 amendments thereto, and the conservator's report under section 105, and
5 amendments thereto;
6 (5) access to court records relating to the conservatorship;
7 (6) notice of a transaction involving a substantial conflict between the
8 conservator's fiduciary duties and personal interests;
9 (7) notice of the death or significant change in the condition of the
10 individual;
11 (8) notice that a petition has been filed to limit or modify the powers
12 of the conservator or that the court has limited or modified the powers of
13 the conservator; and
14 (9) notice that a petition has been filed to remove the conservator or

16 (g) If an individual subject to conservatorship is an adult, the spouse

15 New Sec. 95. (a) On its own after a petition has been filed under
16 section 84, and amendments thereto, or on a verified petition by a person
17 interested in an individual's welfare, the court may appoint an emergency
18 conservator for the individual if the court finds a sufficient factual basis to
19 establish probable cause that:
20 (1) Appointment of an emergency conservator is necessary to prevent
21 imminent, substantial and irreparable harm to the individual's property or
22 financial interests;
23 (2) no other person has authority and willingness to act in the
24 circumstances; and
25 (3) a basis for appointment of a conservator under section 83, and
26 amendments thereto, exists.
27 (b) The duration of authority of an emergency conservator may not
28 exceed 30 days and the emergency conservator may exercise only the
29 powers specified in the order of appointment. The emergency conservator's
30 authority may be extended up to three times for not more than 30 days per
31 extension if the court finds good cause and that the conditions for
32 appointment of an emergency conservator under subsection (a) continue.
33 (c) Immediately on filing of a petition for an emergency conservator,
34 the court shall appoint an attorney to represent the respondent in the
35 proceeding. Except as otherwise provided in subsection (d), reasonable
36 notice of the date, time and place of a hearing on the petition must be
37 given to the respondent, the respondent's attorney and any other person the
38 court determines.
39 (d) The court may appoint an emergency conservator without notice
40 to the respondent and any attorney for the respondent only if the court
41 finds from an affidavit or testimony that the respondent's property or
42 financial interests will be substantially and irreparably harmed before a
43 hearing with notice on the appointment can be held. If the court appoints

HB 2359—Am. by HC 77
1 an emergency conservator without giving notice under subsection (c), the
2 court must give notice of the appointment not later than 48 hours after the
3 appointment to:
4 (1) The respondent;
5 (2) the respondent's attorney; and
6 (3) any other person the court determines.
7 (e) Not later than five days after the appointment, the court shall hold
8 a hearing on the appropriateness of the appointment.
9 (f) Appointment of an emergency conservator under this section is
10 not a determination that a basis exists for appointment of a conservator
11 under section 83, and amendments thereto.
12 (g) The court may remove an emergency conservator appointed under
13 this section at any time. The emergency conservator shall make any report
14 the court requires.
15 New Sec. 96. An individual subject to conservatorship or a person
16 interested in the welfare of the individual may petition for an order:
17 (a) Modifying bond requirements;
18 (b) requiring an accounting for the administration of the
19 conservatorship estate;
20 (c) directing distribution;
21 (d) removing the conservator and appointing a temporary or
22 successor conservator;
23 (e) modifying the type of appointment or powers granted to the
24 conservator, if the extent of protection or management previously granted
25 is excessive or insufficient to meet the individual's needs, including
26 because the individual's abilities or supports have changed;
27 (f) rejecting or modifying the conservator's plan under section 103,
28 and amendments thereto, the conservator's inventory under section 104,
29 and amendments thereto, or the conservator's report under section 105, and
30 amendments thereto; or
31 (g) granting other appropriate relief.
32 New Sec. 97. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c), the
33 court shall require a conservator to furnish a bond with a surety, or require
34 an alternative asset-protection arrangement, conditioned on faithful
35 discharge of all duties of the conservator. The court may waive the
36 requirement only if the court finds that a bond or other asset-protection
37 arrangement is not necessary to protect the interests of the individual
38 subject to conservatorship. Except as otherwise provided in subsection (c),
39 the court may not waive the requirement if the conservator is in the
40 business of serving as a conservator and is being paid for the conservator's
41 service.
42 (b) Unless the court directs otherwise, the bond required under this
43 section must be in the amount of the aggregate capital value of the

1 conservatorship estate, plus one year's estimated income, less the value of

11 New Sec. 98. (a) The following rules apply to the bond required
12 under section 97, and amendments thereto:
13 (1) Except as otherwise provided by the bond, the surety and the
14 conservator are jointly and severally liable.
15 (2) By executing a bond provided by a conservator, the surety
16 submits to the personal jurisdiction of the court that issued letters of office
17 to the conservator in a proceeding relating to the duties of the conservator
18 in which the surety is named as a party. Notice of the proceeding must be
19 given to the surety at the address shown in the records of the court in
20 which the bond is filed and any other address of the surety then known to
21 the person required to provide the notice.
22 (3) On petition of a successor conservator or person affected by a
23 breach of the obligation of the bond, a proceeding may be brought against
24 the surety for breach of the obligation of the bond.
25 (4) A proceeding against the bond may be brought until liability
26 under the bond is exhausted.
27 (b) A proceeding may not be brought under this section against a
28 surety of a bond on a matter as to which a proceeding against the
29 conservator is barred.
30 (c) If a bond under section 97, and amendments thereto, is not
31 renewed by the conservator, the surety or sureties immediately shall give
32 notice to the court and the individual subject to conservatorship. Upon
33 receiving such notice, the clerk of the district court shall forward the notice
34 to the presiding judge who shall set the matter for hearing and determine
35 who should receive notice.
36 New Sec. 99. (a) A conservator is a fiduciary and has duties of
37 prudence, loyalty, reasonable care and diligence to the individual subject to
38 conservatorship.
39 (b) A conservator shall promote the self-determination of the
40 individual subject to conservatorship and, to the extent feasible, encourage
41 the individual to participate in decisions, act on the individual's own
42 behalf, and develop or regain the capacity to manage the individual's
43 personal affairs. A conservator shall strive to assure that the personal, civil

HB 2359—Am. by HC 79
1 and human rights of the individual subject to conservatorship are
2 protected.
3 (c) In making a decision for an individual subject to conservatorship,
4 the conservator shall make the decision that the conservator reasonably
5 believes the individual would make if able, unless doing so would fail to
6 preserve the resources needed to maintain the individual's well-being and
7 lifestyle or otherwise unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or
8 personal or financial interests of the individual. To determine the decision
9 the individual would make if able, the conservator shall consider the
10 individual's prior or current directions, preferences, opinions, values and
11 actions, to the extent actually known or reasonably ascertainable by the
12 conservator.
13 (d) If a conservator cannot make a decision under subsection (c)
14 because the conservator does not know and cannot reasonably determine
15 the decision the individual subject to conservatorship probably would
16 make if able, or the conservator reasonably believes the decision the
17 individual would make would fail to preserve resources needed to
18 maintain the individual's well-being and lifestyle or otherwise
19 unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial
20 interests of the individual, the conservator shall act in accordance with the
21 best interest of the individual. In determining the best interest of the
22 individual, the conservator shall consider:
23 (1) Information received from professionals and persons that
24 demonstrate sufficient interest in the welfare of the individual;
25 (2) other information the conservator believes the individual would
26 have considered if the individual were able to act; and
27 (3) other factors a reasonable person in the circumstances of the
28 individual would consider, including consequences for others.
29 (e) Except when inconsistent with the conservator's duties under
30 subsections (a) through (d), a conservator shall invest and manage the
31 conservatorship estate as a prudent investor would, by considering:
32 (1) The circumstances of the individual subject to conservatorship
33 and the conservatorship estate;
34 (2) general economic conditions;
35 (3) the possible effect of inflation or deflation;
36 (4) the expected tax consequences of an investment decision or
37 strategy;
38 (5) the role of each investment or course of action in relation to the
39 conservatorship estate as a whole;
40 (6) the expected total return from income and appreciation of capital;
41 (7) the need for liquidity, regularity of income and preservation or
42 appreciation of capital; and
43 (8) the special relationship or value, if any, of specific property to the

HB 2359—Am. by HC 80
1 individual subject to conservatorship.
2 (f) The propriety of a conservator's investment and management of
3 the conservatorship estate is determined in light of the facts and
4 circumstances existing when the conservator decides or acts and not by
5 hindsight.
6 (g) A conservator shall make a reasonable effort to verify facts
7 relevant to the investment and management of the conservatorship estate.
8 (h) A conservator that has special skills or expertise, or is named
9 conservator in reliance on the conservator's representation of special skills
10 or expertise, has a duty to use the special skills or expertise in carrying out
11 the conservator's duties.
12 (i) In investing, selecting specific property for distribution, and
13 invoking a power of revocation or withdrawal for the use or benefit of the
14 individual subject to conservatorship, a conservator shall consider any
15 estate plan of the individual known or reasonably ascertainable to the
16 conservator and may examine the will or other donative, nominative or
17 appointive instrument of the individual.
18 (j) A conservator shall maintain insurance on the insurable real and
19 personal property of the individual subject to conservatorship, unless the
20 conservatorship estate lacks sufficient funds to pay for insurance or the
21 court finds:
22 (1) The property lacks sufficient equity; or
23 (2) insuring the property would unreasonably dissipate the
24 conservatorship estate or otherwise not be in the best interest of the
25 individual.
26 (k) A conservator has access to and authority over a digital asset of
27 the individual subject to conservatorship to the extent provided by the
28 revised uniform fiduciary access to digital assets act or court order.
29 (l) A conservator for an adult shall notify the court immediately if the
30 condition of the adult has changed so that the adult is capable of exercising
31 rights previously removed.
32 New Sec. 100. (a) Except as otherwise provided in section 102, and
33 amendments thereto, or as qualified or limited in the court's order of
34 appointment and stated in the letters of office, a conservator has all powers
35 granted in this section.
36 (b) A conservator, acting reasonably and consistent with the fiduciary
37 duties of the conservator to accomplish the purpose of the conservatorship,

39 the conservatorship estate:
40 (1) Collect, hold and retain property, including property in which the
41 conservator has a personal interest and real property in another state, until
42 the conservator determines disposition of the property should be made;
43 (2) receive additions to the conservatorship estate;

22 New Sec. 101. Except as otherwise provided in section 102, and

38 minor.

40 duties under section 99, and amendments thereto, is not liable for an
41 expenditure or distribution made based on a recommendation under

43 is not in the best interest of the individual subject to conservatorship.

1 subject to conservatorship would make if able, the court shall consider the

17 New Sec. 103. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment, and
18 whenever there is a significant change in circumstances or the conservator
19 seeks to deviate significantly from the existing conservator's plan, a
20 conservator shall file with the court a plan for protecting, managing,
21 expending and distributing the assets of the conservatorship estate. The
22 plan must be based on the needs of the individual subject to
23 conservatorship and take into account the best interest of the individual as
24 well as the individual's preferences, values and prior directions, to the
25 extent known to or reasonably ascertainable by the conservator. The
26 conservator shall include in the plan:
27 (1) A budget containing projected expenses and resources, including
28 an estimate of the total amount of fees the conservator anticipates charging
29 per year and a statement or list of the amount the conservator proposes to
30 charge for each service the conservator anticipates providing to the
31 individual;
32 (2) how the conservator will involve the individual in decisions about
33 management of the conservatorship estate;
34 (3) any step the conservator plans to take to develop or restore the
35 ability of the individual to manage the conservatorship estate; and
36 (4) an estimate of the duration of the conservatorship.
37 (b) A conservator shall give notice of the filing of the conservator's
38 plan under subsection (a), together with a copy of the plan, to the
39 individual subject to conservatorship, any attorney representing the
40 individual subject to conservatorship, a person entitled to notice under
41 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any
42 other person the court determines. The notice must include a statement of
43 the right to object to the plan and must be given at the time of the filing.

1 (c) An individual subject to conservatorship and any person entitled
2 under subsection (b) to receive notice and a copy of the conservator's plan

4 (d) The court shall review the conservator's plan filed under
5 subsection (a) and determine whether to approve the plan or require a new
6 plan. In deciding whether to approve the plan, the court shall consider an

19 New Sec. 104. (a) Not later than 60 days after appointment, a
20 conservator shall prepare and file with the appointing court a detailed
21 inventory of the conservatorship estate, together with an oath or
22 affirmation that the inventory is believed to be complete and accurate as
23 far as information permits. The inventory shall include all of the property
24 and assets of the conservatorship estate, including any sources of regular
25 income to the estate, and information about how property is titled and any
26 beneficiary designations, including pay-on-death and transfer-on-death
27 beneficiaries.
28 (b) A conservator shall give notice of the filing of an inventory to the
29 individual subject to conservatorship, a person entitled to notice under
30 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any
31 other person the court determines. The notice must be given not later than
32 14 days after the filing.
33 (c) A conservator shall keep records of the administration of the
34 conservatorship estate and make them available for examination on
35 reasonable request of the individual subject to conservatorship, a guardian
36 for the individual, or any other person the conservator or the court
37 determines.
38 New Sec. 105. (a) A conservator shall file with the court a report in a
39 record regarding the administration of the conservatorship estate annually
40 unless the court otherwise directs, on resignation or removal, on
41 termination of the conservatorship, and at any other time the court directs.

43 (1) An accounting that lists property included in the conservatorship

1 estate and the receipts, disbursements, liabilities and distributions during

1 (3) the conservator's requested fees, if any, should be approved.

22 accurate as to a matter adequately disclosed in the report.
23 (i) An order, after notice and hearing, approving an interim report of a
24 conservator filed under this section adjudicates liabilities concerning a
25 matter adequately disclosed in the report, as to a person given notice of the
26 report or accounting.

28 under this section discharges the conservator from all liabilities, claims
29 and causes of action by a person given notice of the report and the hearing
30 as to a matter adequately disclosed in the report.
31 New Sec. 106. (a) The interest of an individual subject to
32 conservatorship in property included in the conservatorship estate is not
33 transferrable or assignable by the individual and is not subject to levy,
34 garnishment, or similar process for claims against the individual unless
35 allowed under section 110, and amendments thereto.
36 (b) If an individual subject to conservatorship enters into a contract
37 after having the right to enter the contract removed by the court, the
38 contract is void against the individual and the individual's property but is
39 enforceable against the person that contracted with the individual.
40 (c) A person other than the conservator that deals with an individual
41 subject to conservatorship with respect to property included in the
42 conservatorship estate is entitled to protection provided by law of this state
43 other than this act.

HB 2359—Am. by HC 89
1 New Sec. 107. A transaction involving a conservatorship estate which
2 is affected by a substantial conflict between the conservator's fiduciary
3 duties and personal interests is voidable unless the transaction is
4 authorized by court order after notice to persons entitled to notice under
5 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order. A
6 transaction affected by a substantial conflict includes a sale, encumbrance
7 or other transaction involving the conservatorship estate entered into by
8 the conservator, an individual with whom the conservator resides, the
9 spouse, descendant, sibling, agent or attorney of the conservator, or a
10 corporation or other enterprise in which the conservator has a substantial
11 beneficial interest.
12 New Sec. 108. (a) A person that assists or deals with a conservator in
13 good faith and for value in any transaction, other than a transaction
14 requiring a court order under section 102, and amendments thereto, is
15 protected as though the conservator properly exercised any power in
16 question. Knowledge alone by a person that the person is dealing with a
17 conservator does not require the person to inquire into the existence of
18 authority of the conservator or the propriety of the conservator's exercise
19 of authority, but restrictions on authority stated in letters of office, or
20 otherwise provided by law, are effective as to the person. A person that
21 pays or delivers property to a conservator is not responsible for proper
22 application of the property.
23 (b) Protection under subsection (a) extends to a procedural
24 irregularity or jurisdictional defect in the proceeding leading to the
25 issuance of letters of office and does not substitute for protection for a
26 person that assists or deals with a conservator provided by comparable
27 provisions in law of this state other than this act relating to a commercial
28 transaction or simplifying a transfer of securities by a fiduciary.
29 New Sec. 109. (a) If an individual subject to conservatorship dies, the
30 conservator shall deliver to the district court any will of the individual that
31 is in the conservator's possession and inform the personal representative
32 named in the will if feasible. The conservator shall give notice of the
33 delivery of the will under this section to any person entitled to notice under
34 section 93(f), and amendments thereto, or a subsequent order.
35 (b) On the death of an individual subject to conservatorship, the
36 conservator shall conclude the administration of the conservatorship estate
37 as provided in section 113, and amendments thereto.
38 New Sec. 110. (a) A conservator may pay a claim against the
39 conservatorship estate or the individual subject to conservatorship arising
40 before or during the conservatorship, on presentation and allowance in
41 accordance with the priorities under subsection (d). A claimant may
42 present a claim by:
43 (1) Sending or delivering to the conservator a statement in a record of

1 the claim, indicating its basis, the name and address of the claimant and
2 the amount claimed; or
3 (2) filing the claim with the court, in a form acceptable to the court,
4 and sending or delivering a copy of the claim to the conservator.
5 (b) A claim under subsection (a) is presented on receipt by the
6 conservator of the statement of the claim or the filing with the court of the
7 claim, whichever occurs first. A presented claim is allowed, if it is not
8 disallowed in whole or in part, by the conservator in a record sent or
9 delivered to the claimant not later than 60 days after its presentation.
10 Before payment, the conservator may change an allowance of the claim to
11 a disallowance in whole or in part, but not after allowance under a court
12 order or order directing payment of the claim. Presentation of a claim tolls
13 until 30 days after disallowance of the claim the running of a statute of
14 limitations that has not expired relating to the claim.
15 (c) A claimant whose claim under subsection (a) has not been paid
16 may petition the court to determine the claim at any time before it is barred
17 by a statute of limitations, and the court may order its allowance, payment
18 or security by encumbering property included in the conservatorship
19 estate. If a proceeding is pending against the individual subject to
20 conservatorship at the time of appointment of the conservator or is
21 initiated thereafter, the moving party shall give the conservator notice of
22 the proceeding if it could result in creating a claim against the
23 conservatorship estate.
24 (d) If a conservatorship estate is likely to be exhausted before all
25 existing claims are paid, the conservator shall distribute the estate in
26 money or in kind in payment of claims in the following order:
27 (1) Costs and expenses of administration;
28 (2) a claim of the federal or state government having priority under
29 law other than this act;
30 (3) a claim incurred by the conservator for support, care, education,
31 health or welfare previously provided to the individual subject to
32 conservatorship or an individual who is in fact dependent on the individual
33 subject to conservatorship;
34 (4) a claim arising before the conservatorship; and
35 (5) all other claims.
36 (e) Preference may not be given in the payment of a claim under
37 subsection (d) over another claim of the same class. A claim due and
38 payable may not be preferred over a claim not due unless:
39 (1) Doing so would leave the conservatorship estate without
40 sufficient funds to pay the basic living and healthcare expenses of the
41 individual subject to conservatorship; and
42 (2) the court authorizes the preference under section 102(a)(8), and
43 amendments thereto.

HB 2359—Am. by HC 91
1 (f) If assets of a conservatorship estate are adequate to meet all
2 existing claims, the court, acting in the best interest of the individual
3 subject to conservatorship, may order the conservator to grant a security
4 interest in the conservatorship estate for payment of a claim at a future
5 date.
6 New Sec. 111. (a) Except as otherwise agreed by a conservator, the
7 conservator is not personally liable on a contract properly entered into in a
8 fiduciary capacity in the course of administration of the conservatorship
9 estate unless the conservator fails to reveal the conservator's representative
10 capacity in the contract or before entering into the contract.
11 (b) A conservator is personally liable for an obligation arising from
12 control of property of the conservatorship estate or an act or omission
13 occurring in the course of administration of the conservatorship estate only
14 if the conservator is personally at fault.
15 (c) A claim based on a contract entered into by a conservator in a
16 fiduciary capacity, an obligation arising from control of property included
17 in the conservatorship estate, or a tort committed in the course of
18 administration of the conservatorship estate may be asserted against the
19 conservatorship estate in a proceeding against the conservator in a
20 fiduciary capacity, whether or not the conservator is personally liable for
21 the claim.
22 (d) A question of liability between a conservatorship estate and the
23 conservator personally may be determined in a proceeding for accounting,
24 surcharge, or indemnification or another appropriate proceeding or action.
25 New Sec. 112. (a) The court may remove a conservator for failure to
26 perform the conservator's duties or other good cause and appoint a
27 successor conservator to assume the duties of the conservator.
28 (b) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether to remove a
29 conservator and appoint a successor on:
30 (1) Petition of the individual subject to conservatorship, conservator
31 or person interested in the welfare of the individual which contains
32 allegations that, if true, would support a reasonable belief that removal of
33 the conservator and appointment of a successor may be appropriate, but
34 the court may decline to hold a hearing if a petition based on the same or
35 substantially similar facts was filed during the preceding six months;
36 (2) communication from the individual subject to conservatorship,
37 conservator or person interested in the welfare of the individual which
38 supports a reasonable belief that removal of the conservator and
39 appointment of a successor may be appropriate;
40 (3) determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best
41 interest of the individual subject to conservatorship; or
42 (4) determination by the court that the conservator's reports and
43 accountings are delinquent or deficient as filed.

HB 2359—Am. by HC 92
1 (c) Notice of a petition under subsection (b)(1) or any hearing under
2 this section must be given to the individual subject to conservatorship, the
3 conservator, a person entitled to notice under section 93(f), and
4 amendments thereto, or a subsequent order, and any other person the court
5 determines.
6 (d) If the individual subject to conservatorship is not represented by

17 New Sec. 113. (a) A conservatorship for a minor terminates on the
18 earliest of:
19 (1) A court order terminating the conservatorship;
20 (2) the minor becoming an adult except as provided in section 114,
21 and amendments thereto;
22 (3) emancipation of the minor; or
23 (4) death of the minor.
24 (b) A conservatorship for an adult terminates on order of the court or
25 when the adult dies.
26 (c) An individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator, or a
27 person interested in the welfare of the individual may petition for:
28 (1) Termination of the conservatorship on the ground that a basis for
29 appointment under section 83, and amendments thereto, does not exist or
30 termination would be in the best interest of the individual or for other good
31 cause; or
32 (2) modification of the conservatorship on the ground that the extent
33 of protection or assistance granted is not appropriate or for other good
34 cause.
35 (d) The court shall hold a hearing to determine whether termination
36 or modification of a conservatorship is appropriate on:
37 (1) Petition under subsection (c) which contains allegations that, if

40 a hearing if a petition based on the same or substantially similar facts was
41 filed within the preceding six months;
42 (2) a communication from the individual subject to conservatorship,
43 conservator or person interested in the welfare of the individual which

HB 2359—Am. by HC 93
1 supports a reasonable belief that termination or modification of the

5 (3) a report from a guardian or conservator which indicates that

7 needs or supports or services available to the individual have changed or a

9 alternative is available; or
10 (4) a determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best

20 (g) The court shall modify the powers granted to a conservator if the

24 (h) Unless the court otherwise orders for good cause, before

26 to safeguard the rights of the individual subject to conservatorship which

32 same conditions as in section 88, and amendments thereto. The court shall
33 award reasonable attorney fees to the attorney as provided in section 42,
34 and amendments thereto.
35 (j) On termination of a conservatorship other than by reason of the
36 death of the individual subject to conservatorship, property of the
37 conservatorship estate passes to the individual. The order of termination
38 must direct the conservator to file a final report and petition for discharge
39 on approval by the court of the final report.
40 (k) On termination of a conservatorship by reason of the death of the
41 individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator promptly shall file a
42 final report and petition for discharge on approval by the court of the final
43 report. On approval of the final report, the conservator shall proceed

HB 2359—Am. by HC 94
1 expeditiously to distribute the conservatorship estate to the individual's

12 New Sec. 114. (a) A conservatorship for a minor may be extended
13 beyond the minor's 18th birthday if the minor consents or the court finds by
14 clear and convincing evidence that substantial harm to the minor's interests
15 is otherwise likely. A conservatorship may be extended under this section
16 until the minor reaches the age of 21 and may be extended for two
17 additional two-year periods upon the same finding by the court or upon
18 consent of the minor. Consent to the extension of a conservatorship may be
19 withdrawn at any time.
20 (b) Any request to extend a minor conservatorship under this section
21 must be accompanied by:
22 (1) A description of the funds or assets of the minor's estate which the
23 conservator proposes to distribute to the minor over an extended period
24 following the minor's 18th birthday;
25 (2) the factual basis upon which the conservator alleges the need for
26 such an extended distribution plan; and
27 (3) a proposed conservator's plan that describes how the distribution
28 will occur.
29 (c) The court shall appoint an attorney to represent the minor as
30 provided in section 88, and amendments thereto.
31 (d) After a hearing, the court may extend a conservatorship for a
32 minor and grant to the conservator the authority to establish an extended
33 distribution plan if the court finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
34 (1) Substantial harm to the minor's interests is likely if the
35 conservatorship is not extended; and
36 (2) the plan approved by the court adequately provides for meeting
37 the expected needs of the minor from the minor's 18th birthday until the
38 final distribution of the funds or assets which the court authorizes to be set
39 aside or transferred from the estate are paid over to the minor, including
40 provisions for accelerated distribution in extraordinary circumstances,
41 which may require court approval.
42 (e) If the court orders a conservatorship for a minor to be extended
43 under this section, the court shall order the conservator to report any

HB 2359—Am. by HC 95
1 expenditure or transfer of funds or assets from the minor's estate for the
2 purposes of effectuating an extended distribution plan within the
3 conservator's next accounting.
4 (f) The court may extend the conservatorship with regard to specific
5 funds or assets of the minor's estate, even though other funds or assets of
6 the minor's estate are paid over to the minor upon the minor's becoming 18
7 years of age.
8 (g) The minor shall be without the power, voluntarily or involuntarily,
9 to sell, mortgage, pledge, hypothecate, assign, alienate, anticipate, transfer
10 or convey any interest in the principal or the income from any funds or
11 assets of the minor's estate set aside or transferred to effectuate a plan for
12 extended distribution until such is actually paid to the minor.
13 New Sec. 115. (a) Unless a person required to transfer funds or other
14 property to a minor knows that a conservator for the minor has been
15 appointed or a proceeding is pending for conservatorship, the person may
16 transfer an amount or value not exceeding $25,000 in a 12-month period
17 to:
18 (1) A person that has care or custody of the minor and with whom the
19 minor resides;
20 (2) a guardian for the minor;
21 (3) a custodian under the uniform transfers to minors act; or
22 (4) a financial institution as a deposit in an interest-bearing account or
23 certificate solely in the name of the minor and shall give notice to the
24 minor of the deposit.
25 (b) A person that transfers funds or other property under this section
26 is not responsible for its proper application.
27 (c) A person that receives funds or other property for a minor under
28 subsection (a)(1) or (2) may apply it only to the support, care, education,
29 health or welfare of the minor, and may not derive a personal financial
30 benefit from it, except for reimbursement for necessary expenses. Funds
31 not applied for these purposes must be preserved for the future support,
32 care, education, health or welfare of the minor, and the balance, if any,
33 transferred to the minor when the minor becomes an adult or otherwise is
34 emancipated.
35 (d) Any accumulated balance under this section shall be subject to
36 other provisions of this act.
37 New Sec. 116. The parent of a minor has the right and responsibility
38 to hold in trust and manage for the minor's benefit all of the personal and
39 real property vested in such minor when the total of such property does not
40 exceed $25,000 in value, unless a guardian or conservator has been
41 appointed for the minor.

2 New Sec. 120. (a) After the hearing on a petition under section 65,
3 and amendments thereto, for a guardianship or under section 119(b), and
4 amendments thereto, for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship,
5 the court may issue an order under subsection (b) for a protective
6 arrangement instead of guardianship if the court finds by clear and
7 convincing evidence that:
8 (1) The respondent lacks the ability to meet essential requirements for
9 physical health, safety or self-care because the respondent is unable to
10 receive and evaluate information or make or communicate decisions, even
11 with appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported
12 decision making; and
13 (2) the respondent's identified needs cannot be met by a less
14 restrictive alternative.
15 (b) If the court makes the findings under subsection (a), the court,
16 instead of appointing a guardian, may:
17 (1) Authorize or direct a transaction necessary to meet the
18 respondent's need for health, safety or care, including:
19 (A) A particular medical treatment or refusal of a particular medical
20 treatment;
21 (B) a move to a specified place of dwelling; or
22 (C) visitation between the respondent and another person;
23 (2) order supervised visitation with, or restrict access to the
24 respondent by, a specified person whose access places the respondent at
25 serious risk of physical, psychological or financial harm; and
26 (3) order other arrangements on a limited basis that are appropriate.
27 (c) In deciding whether to issue an order under this section, the court
28 shall consider the factors under sections 76 and 77, and amendments
29 thereto, which a guardian must consider when making a decision on behalf
30 of an adult subject to guardianship.
31 (d) Any order issued under this section may include reporting
32 requirements, time limits, bond requirements or any other provisions
33 deemed necessary by the court.

19 court may appoint a court liaison. The court liaison must be an individual
20 with training or experience in the types of abilities, limitations and needs
21 alleged in the petition.
22 (d) A court liaison appointed under subsection (a) or (c) shall
23 interview the respondent in person and in a manner the respondent is best
24 able to understand:
25 (1) Explain, in general, the petition, and the nature and purpose of the
26 proceeding including the potential loss of rights as a result of the
27 proceeding;
28 (2) obtain the respondent's views with respect to the order sought;
29 (3) if the petitioner seeks an order related to the dwelling of the
30 respondent, visit the respondent's present dwelling and any dwelling in
31 which it is reasonably believed the respondent will live if the order is
32 granted;
33 (4) if a protective arrangement instead of guardianship is sought,
34 obtain information from any physician or other provider known to have
35 treated, advised or assessed the respondent's relevant physical or mental
36 condition, to the extent that such information has not already been
37 provided to the court;
38 (5) if a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is sought,
39 review financial records of the respondent, if relevant to the court liaison's
40 recommendation under subsection (e)(2); and
41 (6) investigate the allegations in the petition and any other matter
42 relating to the petition as directed by the court, including, but not limited
43 to, the respondent's family relationships, past conduct, the nature and

HB 2359—Am. by HC 103
1 extent of any property or income of the respondent, whether the
2 respondent is likely to injure self or others and other matters as the court
3 may specify.
4 (e) A court liaison under this section promptly shall file a report with
5 the court at least 10 days prior to the hearing on the petition or other
6 hearing as directed by the court. Unless otherwise ordered by the court,
7 such report must include:
8 (1) To the extent relevant to the order sought, a summary of self-care,
9 independent-living tasks and financial-management tasks the respondent:
10 (A) Can manage without assistance or with existing supports;
11 (B) could manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive
12 services, technological assistance or supported decision making; and
13 (C) cannot manage;
14 (2) a recommendation regarding the appropriateness of the protective
15 arrangement sought and whether a less restrictive alternative for meeting
16 the respondent's needs is available;
17 (3) if the petition seeks to change the physical location of the
18 dwelling of the respondent, a statement whether the proposed dwelling
19 meets the respondent's needs and whether the respondent has expressed a
20 preference as to the respondent's dwelling;
21 (4) a statement whether the respondent is able to attend a hearing at
22 the location court proceedings typically are held;
23 (5) a statement whether the respondent is able to participate in a
24 hearing and which identifies any technology or other form of support that
25 would enhance the respondent's ability to participate; and
26 (6) any other matter the court directs.
27 (f) The costs of an investigation by a court liaison shall be assessed as
28 provided for in section 42, and amendments thereto.
29 New Sec. 125. (a) Unless the respondent in a proceeding under
30 sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, is represented by an
31 attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney to represent the respondent,
32 regardless of the respondent's ability to pay. The court shall give
33 preference in the appointment of an attorney to an attorney whom the
34 respondent has requested or to any attorney who has represented the
35 respondent in other matters if the court has knowledge of that prior
36 representation.
37 (b) An attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding under
38 sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, shall:
39 (1) Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes;
40 (2) advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably
41 ascertainable; and
42 (3) if the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable,
43 advocate for the result that is the least restrictive alternative in type,

HB 2359—Am. by HC 104
1 duration and scope, consistent with the respondent's interests.
2 (c) The court may appoint an attorney to represent a parent of a minor
3 who is the subject of a proceeding under sections 119 through 130, and
4 amendments thereto, if:
5 (1) The parent objects to the entry of an order for a protective
6 arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship;
7 (2) the court determines that counsel is needed to ensure that consent
8 to the entry of an order for a protective arrangement is informed; or
9 (3) the court otherwise determines the parent needs representation.
10 (d) An attorney representing the respondent shall interview the
11 respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is best able to
12 understand:
13 (1) Explain to the respondent the substance of the petition, the nature,
14 purpose and effect of the proceeding, and the respondent's rights at the
15 hearing on the petition;
16 (2) determine the respondent's views about the order sought by the
17 petitioner; and
18 (3) inform the respondent that all costs and expenses of the
19 proceeding, including respondent's attorney fees, may be paid from the
20 respondent's assets.
21 New Sec. 126. (a) Upon the filing of the petition or any other time at
22 or before the hearing, if the contents of the petition or evidence at the
23 hearing support a prima facie case of the need for a protective
24 arrangement, the court shall order an examination and evaluation of the
25 respondent to be conducted through a general hospital, psychiatric
26 hospital, community mental health center, or community developmental
27 disability organization, or by a licensed physician, psychiatrist,
28 psychologist, physician assistant, nurse practitioner, social worker or other
29 professional appointed by the court who is qualified to evaluate the
30 respondent's alleged cognitive and functional abilities and limitations and
31 will not be advantaged or disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition
32 or otherwise have a conflict of interest.
33 (b) Unless otherwise specified by the court, the report of the
34 examination and evaluation submitted to the court shall contain:
35 (1) The respondent's name, age and date of birth;
36 (2) a description of the respondent's physical and mental condition;
37 (3) a description of the nature and extent of the respondent's cognitive
38 and functional abilities and limitations, including adaptive behaviors and
39 social skills, and, as appropriate, educational and developmental potential;
40 (4) a summary of self-care and independent-living tasks the
41 respondent can manage without assistance or with existing supports, could
42 manage with the assistance of appropriate supportive services,
43 technological assistance or supported decision making, and cannot

HB 2359—Am. by HC 105
1 manage;
2 (5) a prognosis for any improvement and, as appropriate, any
3 recommendation for treatment or rehabilitation;
4 (6) a list and description of any prior assessments, evaluations or
5 examinations of the respondent, including the dates thereof, which were
6 relied upon in the preparation of this evaluation;
7 (7) the date and location where this examination and evaluation
8 occurred, and the name or names of the professional or professionals
9 performing the examination and evaluation and such professional's
10 qualifications;
11 (8) a statement by the professional that the professional has
12 personally completed an independent examination and evaluation of the
13 respondent, and that the report submitted to the court contains the results
14 of that examination and evaluation, and the professional's opinion with
15 regard to the issues of whether or not the respondent is in need of a
16 guardian and whether there are barriers to the respondent's attendance and
17 participation at the hearing on the petition; and
18 (9) the signature of the professional who prepared the report.
19 (c) The professional shall file with the court, at least five days prior to
20 the date of the trial, such professional's written report concerning the
21 examination and evaluation ordered by the court. The report shall be made
22 available by the court to counsel for all parties.
23 (d) In lieu of entering an order for an examination and evaluation as
24 provided for in this section, the court may determine that the report
25 accompanying the petition is in compliance with the requirements of this
26 section and that no further examination or evaluation should be required,
27 unless the respondent, or such person's attorney, requests such an
28 examination and evaluation in writing. Any such request shall be filed with
29 the court, and a copy thereof delivered to the petitioner, at least four days
30 prior to the date of the trial. Accompanying the request shall be a statement
31 of the reasons why an examination and evaluation is requested and the
32 name and address of a qualified professional or facility willing and able to
33 conduct this examination and evaluation. If the court orders a further
34 examination and evaluation, the court may continue the trial and fix a new
35 date, time and place of the trial at a time not to exceed 30 days from the
36 date of the filing of the request.
37 New Sec. 127. (a) Except as otherwise provided in subsection (b), a
38 hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, may not
39 proceed unless the respondent attends the hearing. If it is not reasonably
40 feasible for the respondent to attend a hearing at the location where court
41 proceedings typically are held, the court shall make reasonable efforts to
42 hold the hearing at an alternative location convenient to the respondent or
43 allow the respondent to attend the hearing using real-time audio-visual

HB 2359—Am. by HC 106
1 technology.
2 (b) A hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
3 thereto, may proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court
4 finds by clear and convincing evidence that:
5 (1) The respondent is choosing not to attend the hearing after having
6 been fully informed of the right to attend and the potential consequences
7 of failing to do so;
8 (2) there is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and
9 participate in the hearing even with appropriate supportive services and
10 technological assistance; or
11 (3) the respondent is a minor who has received proper notice and
12 attendance would be harmful to the minor.
13 (c) The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under sections 119
14 through 130, and amendments thereto, by a person or persons of the
15 respondent's choosing, assistive technology or an interpreter or translator,
16 or a combination of these supports. If assistance would facilitate the
17 respondent's participation in the hearing, but is not otherwise available to
18 the respondent, the court shall make reasonable efforts to provide it.
19 (d) The respondent has a right to retain an attorney to represent the
20 respondent at a hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
21 thereto.
22 (e) At a hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
23 thereto, the respondent may:
24 (1) Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents;
25 (2) examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator and
26 the court liaison; and
27 (3) otherwise participate in the hearing.
28 (f) A hearing under sections 119 through 130, and amendments
29 thereto, must be closed on request of the respondent and a showing of
30 good cause.
31 (g) Any person may request to participate in a hearing under sections
32 119 through 130, and amendments thereto. The court may grant the
33 request, with or without a hearing, on determining that the best interest of
34 the respondent will be served. The court may impose appropriate
35 conditions on the person's participation.
36 New Sec. 128. The court shall give notice of an order under sections
37 119 through 130, and amendments thereto, to the individual who is subject
38 to the protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship, a
39 person whose access to the individual is restricted by the order and any
40 other person the court determines.
41 New Sec. 129. (a) The existence of a proceeding for or the existence
42 of a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship is a
43 matter of public record unless the court seals the record after:

HB 2359—Am. by HC 107
1 (1) The respondent, the individual subject to the protective
2 arrangement, or the parent of a minor subject to the protective arrangement
3 requests the record be sealed; and
4 (2) either:
5 (A) The proceeding is dismissed;
6 (B) the protective arrangement is no longer in effect; or
7 (C) an act authorized by the order granting the protective arrangement
8 has been completed.
9 (b) (1) An order of protective arrangement is a matter of public record
10 unless sealed by the court. All other court records of the proceeding
11 relating to the protective arrangement are not a matter of public record
12 except as further provided.
13 (2) The following persons may access court records of the proceeding
14 and resulting protective arrangement:
15 (A) A respondent;
16 (B) an individual subject to a protective arrangement instead of
17 guardianship or conservatorship;
18 (C) an attorney designated by the respondent or individual;
19 (D) a parent of a minor subject to a protective arrangement; and
20 (E) a licensed attorney, abstractor, or title insurance agent.
21 (3) A person not otherwise entitled to access to court records under
22 this subsection for good cause may request permission from the court for
23 access. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest of the
24 respondent or individual subject to the protective arrangement or furthers
25 the public interest and does not endanger the welfare or financial interests
26 of the respondent or individual.
27 (c) A report of a court liaison or professional evaluation generated in
28 the course of a proceeding under sections 119 through 130, and
29 amendments thereto, must be sealed on filing but is available to:
30 (1) The court;
31 (2) the individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation,
32 without limitation as to use;
33 (3) the petitioner, court liaison and petitioner's and respondent's
34 attorneys, for purposes of the proceeding;
35 (4) unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a
36 power of attorney for finances in which the respondent is the principal;
37 (5) if the order is for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship
38 and unless the court orders otherwise, an agent appointed under a power of
39 attorney for healthcare in which the respondent is identified as the
40 principal; and
41 (6) any other person if it is in the public interest or for a purpose the
42 court orders for good cause.

5 develop a statement of rights form, petition forms and report and
6 accounting forms.
7 New Sec. 132. In applying and construing this uniform act,
8 consideration must be given to the need to promote uniformity of the law
9 with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it.
10 New Sec. 133. This act modifies, limits or supersedes the electronic
11 signatures in global and national commerce act, 15 U.S.C. § 7001 et seq.,
12 but does not modify, limit or supersede section 101(c) of that act, 15
13 U.S.C. § 7001(c), or authorize electronic delivery of any of the notices
14 described in section 103(b) of that act, 15 U.S.C. § 7003(b).
15 New Sec. 134. (a) This act applies to:
16 (1) A proceeding for appointment of a guardian or conservator or for
17 a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship
18 commenced after January 1, 2026; and
19 (2) except as provided in subsection (b), a guardianship,
20 conservatorship or protective arrangement instead of guardianship or
21 conservatorship in existence on January 1, 2026, unless the court finds
22 application of a particular provision of this act would substantially
23 interfere with the effective conduct of the proceeding or prejudice the
24 rights of a party, in which case the particular provision of this act does not
25 apply and the superseded law applies.
26 (b) Sections 79 and 103, and amendments thereto, mandating a
27 guardian's plan or conservator's plan shall not apply to guardianships or
28 conservatorships in existence on January 1, 2026, unless the court orders
29 that a guardian's plan or conservator's plan is required.
30 New Sec. 135. If any provision of this act or its application to any
31 person or circumstance is held invalid, the invalidity does not affect other
32 provisions or applications of this act which can be given effect without the
33 invalid provision or application, and to this end the provisions of this act
34 are severable.

9 Sec. 139. K.S.A. 21-5417 is hereby amended to read as follows: 21-
10 5417. (a) Mistreatment of a dependent adult or an elder person is

28 through 135, and amendments thereto; or

15 by a physician to be necessary for the welfare of such child, if the parents
16 are not available or refuse to consent.
17 (4) When the court has adjudicated a child to be in need of care, the
18 custodian or an agent designated by the custodian is the personal
19 representative for the purpose of consenting to disclosure of otherwise
20 protected health information and shall have authority to consent to the
21 performance and furnishing of hospital, medical, surgical or dental
22 treatment or procedures or mental care or treatment other than inpatient
23 treatment at a state psychiatric hospital, including the release and
24 inspection of medical or hospital records, subject to terms and conditions
25 the court considers proper and subject to the limitations of K.S.A. 59-3075
26 (e)(4), (5) and (6) section 78, and amendments thereto.
27 (5) Any health care provider who in good faith renders hospital,
28 medical, surgical, mental or dental care or treatment to any child or
29 discloses protected health information as authorized by this section shall
30 not be liable in any civil or criminal action for failure to obtain consent of
31 a parent.
32 (6) Nothing in this section shall be construed to mean that any person
33 shall be relieved of legal responsibility to provide care and support for a
34 child.
35 (b) Care and treatment requiring court action. If it is brought to the
36 court's attention, while the court is exercising jurisdiction over the person
37 of a child under this code, that the child may be a mentally ill person as
38 defined in K.S.A. 59-2946, and amendments thereto, or a person with an
39 alcohol or substance abuse problem as defined in K.S.A. 59-29b46, and
40 amendments thereto, the court may:
41 (1) Direct or authorize the county or district attorney or the person
42 supplying the information to file the petition provided for in K.S.A. 59-
43 2957, and amendments thereto, and proceed to hear and determine the

HB 2359—Am. by HC 115
1 issues raised by the application as provided in the care and treatment act
2 for mentally ill persons or the petition provided for in K.S.A. 59-29b57,
3 and amendments thereto, and proceed to hear and determine the issues
4 raised by the application as provided in the care and treatment act for
5 persons with an alcohol or substance abuse problem; or
6 (2) authorize that the child seek voluntary admission to a treatment
7 facility as provided in K.S.A. 59-2949, and amendments thereto, or K.S.A.
8 59-29b49, and amendments thereto.
9 The application to determine whether the child is a mentally ill person
10 or a person with an alcohol or substance abuse problem may be filed in the
11 same proceedings as the petition alleging the child to be a child in need of
12 care, or may be brought in separate proceedings. In either event, the court
13 may enter an order staying any further proceedings under this code until
14 all proceedings have been concluded under the care and treatment act for
15 mentally ill persons or the care and treatment act for persons with an
16 alcohol or substance abuse problem.

23 Sec. 144. K.S.A. 2024 Supp. 58-656 is hereby amended to read as
24 follows: 58-656. (a) An attorney in fact who elects to act under a power of
25 attorney is under a duty to act in the interest of the principal and to avoid
26 conflicts of interest that impair the ability of the attorney in fact so to act.
27 A person who is appointed an attorney in fact under a power of attorney
28 who undertakes to exercise the authority conferred in the power of
29 attorney, has a fiduciary obligation to exercise the powers conferred in the
30 best interests of the principal, and to avoid self-dealing and conflicts of
31 interest, as in the case of a trustee with respect to the trustee's beneficiary
32 or beneficiaries. The attorney in fact shall keep a record of receipts,
33 disbursements and transactions made on behalf of the principal and shall
34 not comingle funds or assets of the principal with the funds or assets of the
35 attorney in fact. In the absence of explicit authorization, the attorney in
36 fact shall exercise a high degree of care in maintaining, without
37 modification, any estate plan which the principal may have in place,
38 including, but not limited to, arrangements made by the principal for
39 disposition of assets at death through beneficiary designations, ownership
40 by joint tenancy or tenancy by the entirety, trust arrangements or by will or
41 codicil. Unless otherwise provided in the power of attorney or in a separate
42 agreement between the principal and attorney in fact, an attorney in fact
43 who elects to act shall exercise the authority granted in a power of attorney

HB 2359—Am. by HC 121
1 with that degree of care that would be observed by a prudent person
2 dealing with the property and conducting the affairs of another, except that
3 all investments made on or after July 1, 2003, shall be in accordance with
4 the provisions of the Kansas uniform prudent investor act, K.S.A. 58-
5 24a01 et seq., and amendments thereto. If the attorney in fact has special
6 skills or was appointed attorney in fact on the basis of representations of
7 special skills or expertise, the attorney in fact has a duty to use those skills
8 in the principal's behalf.
9 (b) On matters undertaken or to be undertaken in the principal's
10 behalf and to the extent reasonably possible under the circumstances, an
11 attorney in fact has a duty to keep in regular contact with the principal, to
12 communicate with the principal and to obtain and follow the instructions
13 of the principal.
14 (c) If, following execution of a durable power of attorney, a court of
15 the principal's domicile appoints a conservator, guardian of the estate or
16 other fiduciary charged with the management of all of the principal's
17 property or all of the principal's property except specified exclusions, the
18 attorney in fact is accountable to the fiduciary as well as to the principal.
19 The fiduciary has the same power to revoke or amend the durable power of
20 attorney that the principal would have had if the principal were not an
21 adult with an impairment in need of a guardian or conservator or both as
22 defined by subsection (a) of K.S.A. 59-3051 section 25, and amendments
23 thereto.
24 (d) A principal may nominate by a power of attorney, a guardian or
25 conservator, or both, for consideration by the court. If a petition to appoint
26 a guardian or conservator, or both, is filed, the court shall make the
27 appointment in accordance with the principal's most recent nomination in
28 the power of attorney, so long as the individual nominated is a fit and
29 proper person.
30 (e) An attorney in fact shall exercise authority granted by the
31 principal in accordance with the instrument setting forth the power of
32 attorney, any modification made therein by the principal or the principal's
33 legal representative or a court, and the oral and written instructions of the
34 principal, or the written instructions of the principal's legal representative
35 or a court.
36 (f) An attorney in fact may be instructed in a power of attorney that
37 the authority granted shall not be exercised until, or shall terminate on, the
38 happening of a future event, condition or contingency, as determined in a
39 manner prescribed in the instrument.
40 (g) On the death of the principal, the attorney in fact shall follow the
41 instructions of the court, if any, having jurisdiction over the estate of the
42 principal, or any part thereof, and shall communicate with and be
43 accountable to the principal's personal representative, or if none, the

HB 2359—Am. by HC 122
1 principal's successors. The attorney in fact shall promptly deliver to and
2 put in the possession and control of the principal's personal representative
3 or successors, any property of the principal and copies of any records of
4 the attorney in fact relating to transactions undertaken in the principal's
5 behalf that are deemed by the personal representative or the court to be
6 necessary or helpful in the administration of the decedent's estate.
7 (h) If an attorney in fact has a property or contract interest in the
8 subject of the power of attorney or the authority of the attorney in fact is
9 otherwise coupled with an interest in a person other than the principal, this
10 section does not impose any duties on the attorney in fact that would
11 conflict or be inconsistent with that interest.

15 (2) uses alcoholic beverages or any substance to the extent that the
16 person's health may be substantially impaired or endangered without
17 treatment.
18 (j) (1) "Person with an alcohol or substance abuse problem subject to
19 involuntary commitment for care and treatment" means a person with an
20 alcohol or substance abuse problem who also is incapacitated by alcohol or

22 (2) "Incapacitated by alcohol or any substance" means that the
23 person, as the result of the use of alcohol or any substance, has impaired
24 judgment resulting in the person:
25 (A) Being incapable of realizing and making a rational decision with
26 respect to the need for treatment; or
27 (B) lacking sufficient understanding or capability to make or
28 communicate responsible decisions concerning either the person's well-
29 being or estate.
30 (3) "Likely to cause harm to self or others" means that the person, by
31 reason of the person's use of alcohol or any substance: (A) Is likely, in the
32 reasonably foreseeable future, to cause substantial physical injury or
33 physical abuse to self or others or substantial damage to another's property,
34 as evidenced by behavior threatening, attempting or causing such injury,
35 abuse or damage; except that if the harm threatened, attempted or caused is
36 only harm to the property of another, the harm must be of such a value and
37 extent that the state's interest in protecting the property from such harm
38 outweighs the person's interest in personal liberty; or
39 (B) is substantially unable, except for reason of indigency, to provide
40 for any of the person's basic needs, such as food, clothing, shelter, health
41 or safety, causing a substantial deterioration of the person's ability to
42 function on the person's own.

23 a treatment facility or such person's designee.
24 (c) "Law enforcement officer" means the same as defined in K.S.A.
25 22-2202, and amendments thereto.
26 (d) (1) "Mental health center" means any community mental health
27 center as defined in K.S.A. 39-2002, and amendments thereto, or a mental
28 health clinic organized as a not-for-profit or a for-profit corporation
29 pursuant to K.S.A. 17-1701 through 17-1775, and amendments thereto, or
30 K.S.A. 17-6001 through 17-6010, and amendments thereto, and licensed in

32 amendments thereto.

34 that has entered into a contract with the secretary for aging and disability
35 services pursuant to the provisions of K.S.A. 39-1601 through 39-1612,
36 and amendments thereto.
37 (e) "Mentally ill person" means any person who is suffering from a
38 mental disorder that is manifested by a clinically significant behavioral or
39 psychological syndrome or pattern and associated with either a painful
40 symptom or an impairment in one or more important areas of functioning,
41 and involving substantial behavioral, psychological or biological
42 dysfunction, to the extent that the person is in need of treatment.
43 (f) (1) "Mentally ill person subject to involuntary commitment for

HB 2359—Am. by HC 138
1 care and treatment" means a mentally ill person, as defined in subsection
2 (e), who also lacks capacity to make an informed decision concerning
3 treatment, is likely to cause harm to self or others, and whose diagnosis is
4 not solely one of the following mental disorders: Alcohol or chemical
5 substance abuse; antisocial personality disorder; intellectual disability;
6 organic personality syndrome; or an organic mental disorder.
7 (2) "Lacks capacity to make an informed decision concerning
8 treatment" means that the person, by reason of the person's mental
9 disorder, is unable, despite conscientious efforts at explanation, to
10 understand basically the nature and effects of hospitalization or treatment
11 or is unable to engage in a rational decision-making process regarding
12 hospitalization or treatment, as evidenced by an inability to weigh the
13 possible risks and benefits.
14 (3) "Likely to cause harm to self or others" means that the person, by
15 reason of the person's mental disorder: (A) Is likely, in the reasonably
16 foreseeable future, to cause substantial physical injury or physical abuse to
17 self or others or substantial damage to another's property, as evidenced by
18 behavior threatening, attempting or causing such injury, abuse or damage;
19 except that if the harm threatened, attempted or caused is only harm to the
20 property of another, the harm must be of such a value and extent that the
21 state's interest in protecting the property from such harm outweighs the
22 person's interest in personal liberty; or (B) is substantially unable, except
23 for reason of indigency, to provide for any of the person's basic needs,
24 such as food, clothing, shelter, health or safety, causing a substantial
25 deterioration of the person's ability to function on the person's own.
26 No person who is being treated by prayer in the practice of the religion
27 of any church that teaches reliance on spiritual means alone through prayer
28 for healing shall be determined to be a mentally ill person subject to
29 involuntary commitment for care and treatment under this act unless
30 substantial evidence is produced upon which the district court finds that
31 the proposed patient is likely in the reasonably foreseeable future to cause
32 substantial physical injury or physical abuse to self or others or substantial
33 damage to another's property, as evidenced by behavior threatening,
34 attempting or causing such injury, abuse or damage; except that if the harm
35 threatened, attempted or caused is only harm to the property of another, the
36 harm must be of such a value and extent that the state's interest in
37 protecting the property from such harm outweighs the person's interest in
38 personal liberty.
39 (g) "Patient" means a person who is a voluntary patient, a proposed
40 patient or an involuntary patient.
